# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 17

## 6146

6146

B"H, 2 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to the notification from your husband, the Rav, shlita, regarding your birthday: May it be the will of Hashem that the coming year be one of peace, goodness, and success, in a way that is revealed and manifest.

It is understood and simple that the more one’s bitachon in Hashem—the Creator of the world and its Guide, who oversees every single person with hashgacha pratis—increases, the more the flow of Hashem’s blessings below will increase, and the measure of blessing and success will grow. It is already well-known from the instruction of our Torah, Toras Chaim, that a person must be in a state of simcha and goodness of heart. After all, all of one’s days, and all the hours and moments within those days, are dedicated to the avodah of the Creator, as it is written, "You shall serve Hashem your G-d with simcha and goodness of heart." This applies all the more so to a woman, the mainstay of the home, as it is tangibly evident that the mood in the home depends on the mood of the woman. Furthermore, blessing only rests upon a place where there is simcha. Since we have been commanded regarding this, it is certainly possible to achieve. Especially when you contemplate, even for a brief moment, the kindnesses of Hashem toward you and your husband, shlita, in the past—which will certainly continue in the future, as mentioned above—you will see that the vessel to draw down and receive blessing is the strength of bitachon and an internal, genuine simcha. May it be the will of Hashem that in this year, He fulfills the desires of your hearts for the good, in health and joy.

With blessings and for good tidings regarding all the above, and for a kosher and happy Pesach, with revealed goodness.

P.S.
You are surely participating in the activities of Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad, and you are also increasing your involvement in this from time to time.

#### ***6146***

Most of the letters are from the secretariat's copy, and some are from a photocopy of the letter itself. They are not marked with footnotes unless the source is different, or if they have already been printed in Likutei Sichos.

The letter before us was printed in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 14, p. 358, and was completed according to the secretariat's copy.

**Bitachon:** See also the following letter—to her husband.

## 6147

B"H, 2 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 25th of Adar, in which you write regarding the mood of your wife, Mrs. [Name]—may she live and be well—noting that she is at times sad, etc.

You will surely be able to explain to her the concept of *bitachon* (trust) in the Creator of the world and its Guide, who oversees every single person with *hashgacha pratis* (Divine providence), and there is no place devoid of Him. Indeed, how can a Jewish man or woman be sad when they are in the immediate presence of a King who is great and good with true goodness? It is obvious that one has nothing to worry about or fear within the "four cubits" of the King. The analogy is understood, and in particular, this is not merely an analogy but the absolute reality of the matter, only on a level infinitely higher and more exalted, as in the well-known *piyut*: "There is no comparison to You," etc.

It would be appropriate for her to also study the *Tanya Kadisha* in the places that discuss the negation of sadness, which will surely enable you to explain the above to her. Likewise, you should have the *mezuzos* in your home checked to ensure they are all *kosher* according to the law. Your wife—may she live—should observe the custom of kosher Jewish women to set aside money for *tzedakah* before lighting the candles every *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*, and you should set aside money for *tzedakah* every weekday before morning *tefillah*.

Regarding what you wrote about the apartment—whether to exchange it—generally, in such matters, one should take into account the opinion of the wife, the *akeres habayis* (mainstay of the home). Since a beautiful dwelling expands a person's mind, one should not be overly concerned if it requires taking on a moderate amount of debt, for such is the way of the world.

Presumably, you are participating in the activity of *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah* (spreading the wellsprings outward) and increasing this from time to time, for we have been commanded that we must always ascend in matters of holiness.

With blessings for good tidings and for a *kosher* and happy *Pesach*.

6148

B"H, 2 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, who toils and accomplishes much,
R’ Yehoshua
Shneur Zalman, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos—you have surely already received a reply to your previous letters. I see in your letter a contradiction from beginning to end: you begin by describing the gatherings, farbrengens, and speeches, and how they have served to bring hearts closer, yet you conclude that "everything is useless," etc. Even though for several years we have become accustomed to the double and redoubled darkness of *ikvesa d’Meshicha*, there must still be some limit even to this; for the *bli gevul* (limitless) exists only in goodness and holiness, and is not found in the *sitra achra*.

My intention is that you should take a piece of paper and write down the difficult situation of the institution two or three years ago, and its situation now. You will see progress that, by the laws of nature, had no place to exist. I will mention only two matters from recent times:

a) The allocation of 4,500 pounds for the building at the conference in Rome, at a time when the decision here was not to give even a penny, and even in Rome there was no such *hishtadlus* that, by the laws of nature, they would agree to such a complete reversal.

b) What you mention in this letter, that the Lieber family donated the entire sum that the yeshivah needs to pay for the building. I doubt whether, even in your current state of *nefilas ruach* (which has no rational explanation), you can find a natural explanation for how this came about.

In truth, the above proofs are only for the sake of preference, for the clear instruction is already known: any matter that weakens activities for *Torah u’mitzvos* certainly has its source in the *yetzer hara* (see *Hayom Yom*, 23 Sivan)—that is, the opposite of the *Melech Malchei HaMelachim*, the Holy One, Blessed be He. Anyone who does not wish to deceive himself—as has already been explained in *Kuntres Uma’ayan* and in many *maamarim*—knows that it is one of two: are you for us, or [for our enemies]?

Regarding the matter of *ratzon* (as opposed to the matter of *sechel*), it makes no difference whether one fails to fulfill a minor detail or transgresses the entire matter.

It is understood that I am not speaking for the sake of debate, but to clarify the situation: that *nefilas ruach* is founded upon the temptations and stratagems of the *yetzer hara*. Just as one fights against him and his temptations when he speaks regarding a *mitzvah d’oraysa* in its literal sense—where the thing is certainly absurd to him—so too, **literally**, regarding these temptations.

It is understood and also simple that none of the above implies that the activities in the Chabad institutions in Australia are in a state of absolute perfection, and that there is no room for improvement or refinement. For there are no such activities in our world after the sin of the Tree of Knowledge. And the command is known, that there must be not just *avodah* in general, but *avodah* "as one ought to do it." Therefore, one must always search for the shortcomings and fill and correct them—but not through *nefilas ruach* and *nemichas ruach* will anyone be saved, and the matters about which you write will also not be helped.

As is apparent from this letter and the previous one, you still hold to the extreme approach that it is impossible to rely on anyone, from the smallest matter to the most important. And if it is impossible for you yourself to fulfill it, this is a most distinct sign that it is not worth engaging in. It is considered absurd to entrust even secondary matters, or those dependent on the local language and the like, to others. A direct result of the approach mentioned here is that there is no place to consult with anyone; for in any case, if one is capable of the matter, he does not need the advice of anyone, and if his own *sechel* is insufficient, then what will others help?

This, too, has no basis, after the simple teaching of the Mishnah: "A single judge does not judge," and things that are well-known and seen tangibly at every step do not require proof.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you recognize the truth: that it is possible for your existence and the existence of others to be, and that one complements the other. This is no reason for *nemichas ruach* on the part of anyone—if one needs advice and instruction, and sometimes even the correction of a mistake. Not only is there no reason in this to neglect the *avodah*, but **on the contrary, and on the contrary**.

I await good news regarding all that has been said, and that ultimately you will stand upon what is stated above **with joy and goodness of heart**, and will add strength in your **beautiful** portion that Divine Providence has placed you in—to be among those who take a **leading** part in *hafatzas hamaayanos* in the country of [Australia]. May it be the will [of Hashem] that all this be with inner and true joy and goodness of heart—in proper health.

With a blessing for a kosher and happy Pesach and for good news soon,

**M. Schneerson**

## 6149

6149

B"H, 2 Nissan 5718
Brooklyn

To the Administrations of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad and Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch in Eretz Yisrael, may Hashem protect them, may they live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 24 Adar, and in response to your questions:

a) When a proposal or even an instruction is received from here, it is understood and simple that this does not mean that unlimited sums and unlimited efforts can be expended on it. For when one takes upon oneself an obligation, it must be settled at the appointed times, and if the obligation is unlimited, it is not a viable consideration.

b) Based on the above, it is understood that regarding travel to gatherings and the like, the establishment of shiurim, the founding of schools, etc., this is a matter like all human activities—conducted within limitations, in accordance with the aforementioned point.

c) Conversely, the commitment from the special campaign for half the expenses of the youth convention remains in effect. It is surprising that you have not yet received this from the funds of that campaign; perhaps, for the time being, there was a shortfall there.

d) Regarding involvement in the field of education, I believe I said here to the esteemed Chossid, etc., Rabbi Y.G. shlita, and I also wrote, that what is being discussed first and foremost is those who currently do not have a livelihood or who are at a crossroads. But [it is not intended] to leave a stable livelihood—and who is to say, even a prosperous one—for the aforementioned purpose. At the very least, in the first stage, these individuals are not part of the aforementioned consideration. And as of now, you have not recruited anyone from among those who are available and at a crossroads...

11) Taking into account the time spent working until now, it would be appropriate to gather and make a summary of the work in the past years and its results. It is a well-known saying that was often on the lips of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that the past teaches the future. Surely, with appropriate reflection, additional points will be added to the plan and organization of the work in the future.

With a blessing for success in your holy work of spreading the wellsprings until they reach the outermost reaches.

## 6150

6150

B"H, 2 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning your attitude toward your daughter, may she live and be well: The ruling of our holy Torah, the Torah of life, is well known, both regarding oneself and regarding fellow Jews: that the ways must be "ways of pleasantness" and the paths must be "paths of peace." It is also a well-known ruling that "the right hand should always draw near," etc. If, for whatever reason, it becomes necessary to demonstrate that a certain behavior was not as it should have been at all, there are many ways to do so, and this is understood. May it be the will of Hashem that very soon you will derive from her much true nachas—nachas that is Jewish and Chassidishe.

## 6,151

6,151

B"H, 2 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter received on the eve of Rosh Chodesh Nissan.

In general, the reasoning for purchasing a house with more than one apartment is correct, and this is the common practice here. The reason is simple: the expenses for one's own apartment become significantly lower, especially since there is usually a larger garage, etc.

Regarding the concern you wrote about—that the second apartment might remain vacant for some time—it should be investigated whether there is any basis for this, in accordance with the conditions of the neighborhood where the building is located.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in whatever way it comes about, your matter will be resolved in the best possible way, in a manner that is good and revealed.

You will surely distribute matzah shemurah in accordance with the well-known sicha on this subject.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach holiday.

## 6152

[2 Nissan 5718]

In response to your letter, requesting a blessing for your studies and for yiras shamayim:

It is my hope that you will fulfill the command of our holy Torah to study with hasmadah and shekidah, and that Hashem will fulfill His promise: "You have labored and you have found." The more you increase your hasmadah and shekidah, the more your success will increase—especially if you also influence your friends, shiy, to conduct themselves in the same way. For the measure of the Ribono shel Olam is "measure for measure," only that it is many times over, rewarding them many times more than their efforts.

I trust that you are keeping the takanah of reciting the monthly Tehillim shiur—as the Tehillim is divided for the days of the month—every day after morning davening. Likewise, that you set aside money for tzedakah from time to time, and especially at the auspicious time—every weekday before morning davening.

#### ***6152***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 18, p. 438.

## 6153

6153

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning the *avreich*... *sheyichyeh*, and his desire to travel to the United States to continue his studies and finish high school here, etc., and he is fourteen or fifteen years old—it is understood that this is entirely impossible. That an *avreich* coming from Eretz Yisrael *tichyeh* to the Tomchei Temimim yeshiva here should have his studies be as mentioned above—(in addition to the **halachic ruling** regarding this, as brought in the Rambam, Hilchos Melachim)—this is a breach of boundaries, both for the students here and, all the more so, for the students from Eretz Yisrael *tichyeh*. Furthermore, and this is the main point: even if they were different for the better than the aforementioned *avreich*, I would not be comfortable with their traveling here. To my regret, experience in this matter has proven the validity of this concern (with very few exceptions). It is obvious that this is not at all appropriate at the age of fourteen or fifteen. If the aforementioned individual truly desires it, he can be absorbed into the Tomchei Temimim yeshiva in Lod or similar institutions—that is to say, a Chabad institution in Eretz Yisrael *tichyeh*. And this is well understood.

I am sure you are preparing the students in the appropriate manner in connection with the upcoming days of Nissan, just as was done in connection with the days of Purim and the month of Adar in general. May it be His will that you see good fruit from your labor in raising students who are the seed blessed by Hashem.

With blessings for good tidings and for a kosher and happy Pesach.

6,154

6,154

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter dated the 27th of Adar, in which you write that you find yourself in an environment of non-observant people and are concerned about the impression this environment might have on you regarding the observance of Torah and mitzvos, etc.

It is understood that, on the contrary, since you are in the army, all those in such a situation are commanded to exercise additional caution in matters of Torah and mitzvos in general, and in matters of holiness in particular. Furthermore, their good conduct, in accordance with the above, determines not only their own fate but the fate of the entire army. As it is written: "And your camp shall be holy, so that He see no unseemly thing among you, and turn away from behind you" (Devarim 23:15) — and see the commentaries on the Torah there. Since Hashem demands this of you, it is certainly possible to fulfill His command.

It would be appropriate for you to connect with those from Tzeirei Agudas Chabad who have served in the army; they will instruct you on how to increase your observance of Torah and mitzvos. There is nothing that can stand before the will.

You are surely aware of the takanah to recite the monthly Tehillim shiur—according to the division of Tehillim for the days of the month—every day after morning davening. Likewise, that every weekday before davening, you should set aside a few coins for tzedakah.

With blessings for good tidings and a kosher and happy Pesach.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6155

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Friday, in which you write about how you have been lonely since your youth, etc., and feel that this loneliness is extremely difficult for you, etc.

It is understood that for a bochur who is in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, in a class with several bochurim of his own age, the matter depends to a great extent on his making friends with them. While it is also understood that this cannot fully replace a parental home, it helps to a significant and great degree in getting through these years until one settles down, with the help of Hashem, into family life.

What also helps in situations such as these are activities for the benefit of others, for then one feels in the depths of one’s soul the connection of Bnei Yisrael to one another. Even if at first this feeling does not come out entirely openly, in the end, it performs its function. If this is true regarding all Bnei Yisrael, how much more so for one who is in a Chassidishe environment and participates in activities for the benefit of Chassidus.

May Hashem grant you success in increasing your *hasmadah* and *shekidah* in our Torah, whose ways are all ways of pleasantness, permeated with the light and vitality of Chassidus. Then you will feel in practice the truth of the statement we heard from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe: "Chassidus makes it so that one does not feel lonely," and even a higher level than that, where one also feels closeness and friendship.

With blessings for good news regarding all the above, and in connection with your notification of your birthday, for a year of success in everything you need, from soul to body.

And with blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

***

**6155**

**The saying:** See also above, Vol. 14, Letter 4950, and the references in the notes there.

## 656

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

After the longest of intervals, your letter arrived with the good news of the improvement in your health. May it be His will that you return to your full strength soon, and that you celebrate the upcoming holidays in peace, with health and true peace of mind.

Regarding what you wrote about the young woman, Miss... may she live and be well.

At an opportune time, I will mention her at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever she needs in general, and specifically for her health and a truly good shidduch.

As for what you wrote regarding what she went through concerning her health, we have nothing to rely on but what is written in our Torah, the Torah of life: that the mitzvah mentioned is a great mitzvah, and the first in the order of the mitzvos of the Torah. As is well known from the adage of our Rebbes, the order in the Torah is itself a Torah and a lesson. Since she is G-d-fearing, modest, and conducts herself accordingly, may Hashem grant her success in building a home in Israel, an everlasting edifice, with blessed children. May it be His will that she, and those around her, completely put out of their minds what has passed, so that no impression remains at all, and may you bring good news regarding her aforementioned arrangements.

As we approach the days of Pesach, may it come upon us for good, I will conclude my letter with a blessing for a kosher and happy Pesach for you and your entire family, may they live and be well.

With respect and holiday blessings,

#### ***656***

**What she went through:** A nervous breakdown. She returned to her full strength without any lasting impression.

## 6157

6157

B"H, 4 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

After a long silence, your letter of 2 Nissan arrived. It is still not clear from it why you did not let me know all this time about your arrangements in...

Regarding what you write about the environment in your current location—insofar as it is not like the environment in Montreal—it is surely unnecessary to explain at length that this itself should awaken those who know the preciousness of Torah and mitzvos. Finding yourself in an environment that lacks so much, as you write, in ruchnius, you should throw yourselves into it with chayos and energy to the maximum extent possible, to do what you can to change such a situation and, in time, bring about the opposite result. Who knows? Perhaps this is the very intent behind you and your husband earning a livelihood in... for the time being: because of the parnassah ruchnis that you need to obtain there, by improving the spiritual state in... through your actions.

As is well known from the letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of his grandfather, the Rebbe Maharash—ztzvkllh"h nbg"m zy"a—Hashem can provide parnassah gashmis in any place, etc. It is surely impossible that, while being in..., one should be unable to accomplish anything—especially those who have merited the Toras HaChassidus, its guidance, and its practices, and who also have the blessing and help of our Rebbes to succeed in the work of *hafatzas hayahadus* and its matters.

Therefore, in my opinion, regardless of the question of where you will settle in the future—and in any case, this is not relevant for this summer, during which you will surely be in...—you must begin to search with the proper will for ways and means to influence Yiddishkeit, both you and your husband, shiy. Surely, in this, the words of Chazal will be fulfilled: "You labored and you found." The zechus of this is beyond measure, to the point that it would be worthwhile to travel to... even if you were in Montreal, in order to accomplish this. This is especially true when you are already located there. And who knows? It may be that when you fulfill the shlichus of *hafatzas hamaayanos* in..., the way will naturally open up to move away from there—in the language of the verse, "with great wealth" of many deeds for Yiddishkeit and Chassidus—to move to another place.

I am sending this letter out of turn, with the hope that the above-mentioned lines will have their effect and that you will still be able to begin to influence your environment regarding matters of Pesach as well. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

#### ***6157***

**The letter of my father-in-law:** Igros Kodesh of the Rebbe, Vol. 17, p. 883. See also above, Vol. 5, letter 1512.

Vol. 9, p. 2930.

## 6158

6158

B"H, 4 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning [the individual]—that all words have already been exhausted in speaking with him—the contradiction is evident when compared to your concluding remark that he remains steadfast in his previous positions. For since there is no truth other than Torah and its directives, and it is also a well-known directive of the Torah that every Jewish person desires to fulfill what is stated in the Torah, but there are those whom their yetzer hara has coerced (and therefore *kefiyah* is effective, as it is merely the removal of the coercion), and since *kefiyah* is sometimes more powerful through words than in other ways—and it is certainly more pleasant—then as long as there is no shift in the aforementioned person’s position, this is clear proof that they have not yet truly spoken *with* him, meaning, spoken *to* him.

Furthermore, regarding the mitzvah of *hochei'ach tochi'ach*, Chazal have explained that it extends even to the point of rebuke, to the point of cursing, and to the point of striking. This is according to the law and the revealed dimension of Torah. How much more so is this true beyond the letter of the law, according to the inner dimension of Torah and the well-known principle that, ultimately, "no one shall be cast out from Him," especially now that the end of the galus is approaching and it is necessary for the whole [Jewish people] to be *zakai* (innocent/meritorious). As the interpretation of this is known: that the evil is separated from the good, to the side of "the whole is *zakai*," etc.—it is certain that one must exert influence upon the aforementioned individual...

## 659

659

B”H, 5 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, man of many accomplishments,
R’ Nissan, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I received with pleasure your letter of 4 Nissan, along with the enclosure. As you requested, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter. May it be His will that you bring good tidings regarding all that was mentioned.

I also received in due time the joyous news from our friends, anash in Miami, regarding the public study of Tanya in the shiur that was established there. Surely, before you left, you appointed a substitute to strengthen the matter—especially since we are commanded not only to strengthen, but also to increase in matters of Torah and mitzvos. And since the Ribono shel Olam does not deal unjustly with His creatures, and we have been commanded to act, Hashem prepares the possibilities in advance to fulfill the command. The matter depends only on the one who initiates it. Based on what was written to me from there regarding the impression made by the study of Tanya, my hope is that if you maintain a correspondence with those who head the shiur, and from time to time inspire them regarding the importance of the matter and the necessity of continuing it, you will certainly succeed. We have already been promised that words that come from the heart enter the heart.

In anticipation of the Festival of Matzos, the time of our freedom, which approaches us and all of Israel for good, I hereby express my blessing for a kosher and happy holiday, and for true freedom—freedom from material worries and spiritual worries, from everything that hinders the avodah of Hashem with joy and a good heart.

And may this freedom and joy be continued throughout all the days of the year.

Especially since the avodah of Hashem, as we are commanded in our Torah—the Torah of life—encompasses all of a person’s affairs throughout the entire day and the entire night, as it is said: “In all your ways, know Him.”

With blessings for the holiday and for good tidings in all matters.

#### ***659***

**R’ Nissan:** Teleshevsky, Brooklyn. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 16, 656, and in the references in the notes there. Below, 670, 816.

## 616

616

B"H, 5 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Mrs. Shula Shefra, may she live,

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter in which you write about the Purim seudah of all the N'shei Chabad branches. May Hashem help that this gathering of all the branches together—in addition to the gatherings of each individual chapter—should bring all the members closer and closer, in the spirit of the well-known phrase, "And they shall all become one fellowship to do Your will with a whole heart." The greatness of the reward for all those who exert themselves in this is already explained in our holy Torah, Toras Chaim.

With blessings for success in the holy work of strengthening and spreading Yiddishkeit, permeated with Chassidishe light and warmth, more and more, and with a wish for a kosher and happy Yom Tov Pesach to all the members and their families, may they live.

With holiday blessings,

#### ***616***

**Mrs. Shula Shefra, may she live:** Katzenelenbogen. Cleveland. Another letter to her—see Vol. 12, 3888.

## 661

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To each and every one in Kfar Chabad—founded and directed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and abundant blessing!

In anticipation of the festival of Matzos, the season of our freedom, which approaches us and all of Israel for good, I hereby express my blessing to each and every one of you for a kosher and joyous holiday—a season of our freedom, true freedom.

May you continue to draw from this freedom and joy throughout the entire year.

Especially since the avodah of Hashem, as commanded to us in our Torah—the Torah of life—encompasses all of a person’s affairs throughout the entire day and night, just as it is said, "In all your ways, know Him."

And may we see the fulfillment, speedily and in our days, of the promise: "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders," with the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for a kosher and joyous Pesach, with true expansion, and for a healthy and happy summer.

I have entrusted the local Rabbi, the venerable and pious Rav, the esteemed Rabbi R. Sh. Z. [Gurelick] shlita, with Shmurah Matzah, and I have requested that, in conjunction with the General Committee of Kfar Chabad and the Spiritual Committee, they distribute it to the residents of Kfar Chabad.

May it be Hashem's will that it achieves its full effect—the effect of the "food of faith" and the "food of healing."

## 6162

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the members of the holy congregation — Shuva Yisrael — and at their head, the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-scholar, etc., Ze'ev, shlita,
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and abundant blessing!

Approaching the festival of Matzos, the season of our freedom, which is arriving for us and for all of Israel for the good, I hereby express my blessing to each of them and their families, shlita, with a blessing for a kosher and happy holiday—the season of our freedom, true freedom.

And may they draw from this freedom and joy throughout all the days of the entire year.

Especially since the avodah of Hashem, as it is commanded to us in our Torah, the Torah of life, encompasses all of a person’s affairs throughout the entire day and night, as it is said, "In all your ways know Him."

My request is that, in good time, they send from here to their holy congregation Shmurah Matzah, in such a way that it reaches everyone—at the very least, two kezaysim. It is my hope that they were received in due time.

May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam that the Shmurah Matzah accomplish its effect—the effect of "food of faith" and "food of healing"—in its entirety.

And may the Guardian of Israel, according to the exposition of our Sages, of blessed memory, on the verse "They were guarded [shemurim]... in Nissan they were redeemed, and in Nissan they are destined to be redeemed" (Rosh Hashanah 11b), fulfill speedily in our days, literally, the prophecy: "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show him wonders."

And as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, explained (in the maamar "Ki Yemei Tzeischa," 5708):

"The days of your exodus" is in the plural—all the days from the time of the exodus from Egypt until the future redemption, at which time "I will show him wonders" through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and with a blessing for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 6163

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

After a very long interval, your letter of 2 Nissan—the day of the Hillula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—was received.

In it, you write that you have sold your business and, for the time being, have no concrete proposals for what to do next.

Certainly, for someone like you, it is unnecessary to point out that falling into low spirits or sadness is absolutely forbidden in general, and especially regarding a matter such as this, as is explained in our holy Torah, Toras Chayim, and in the Seforim of Chassidus in particular. Furthermore, on the contrary: through an increase in strengthening one’s bitachon, one adds energy toward arranging a new livelihood that is expanded in goodness—in goodness that is visible and revealed.

It was pleasant for me to read in your letter about your assistance and involvement on behalf of the holy institutions and the affairs of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Surely, you will continue to do so in the future, and with even greater intensity.

However, as I have heard several times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, it is necessary in such a situation, for the sake of the institutions and their affairs, that this be done with remuneration. That is to say: even though the inner and essential point of this involvement (meaning, the dedication and the vitality) cannot be compensated with money, nevertheless, to ensure peace of mind—and consequently, that there be no lack of composure in the work—it is necessary that it be compensated with an appropriate salary. As is known, there are stories regarding this from the Rebbe Rashab, the father of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. In my opinion, you should dedicate your time now to the work of assisting the institutions, and after you speak with Rabbi [Name] regarding the efforts and assistance, the manner and timing, and also regarding the payment (which, as mentioned, in my opinion is necessary for the success of the work), you should still keep a portion of your time free each day to engage in business affairs as well. "From this and from that, do not withdraw your hand," and Hashem will guide you on the path that is good for you, in goodness that is visible and revealed.

As we approach the festival of Matzos, the season of our freedom, which is coming upon us and upon all of Yisrael for good, I hereby express my blessing for a kosher and joyous holiday and for true freedom—freedom from worries in material matters and from worries in spiritual matters, from everything that hinders the service of Hashem with joy and a good heart.

And may you continue this freedom and joy throughout all the days of the year.

Especially since the service of Hashem, as we are commanded in our Torah, Toras Chayim, encompasses all of a person’s affairs and extends throughout the entire day and the entire night, as it is said, "In all your ways, know Him."

With holiday blessings,

## 6164

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, in which you write about your daily life and current family situation, and ask for an opinion regarding:

1) Your husband, may he live, works at the electric company and is simultaneously building a farm. He finds it difficult to handle both matters at once, and therefore there is a suggestion that he quit the electric company and focus only on the farm.

In my opinion, the time is not appropriate for such a change, especially since working at the electric company surely involves special benefits, such as a pension, security, and the like. Rather, a way should be found to lighten the workload. This is surely easier to achieve regarding the farm work, whether by hiring an assistant or by planning a longer timeframe for the farm’s establishment and development.

2) Regarding your husband’s, may he live, setting fixed times for Torah study—it is understood that this is an essential matter for every Jew, and all the more so when one is in need of a special blessing for an increase in this from the Creator of the world, who is the Giver of the Torah, and as in their eyes. Even though you write that there are no suitable people in your area for a chavrusa, if you search as required, you will certainly find at least one or two. After learning with someone else once or twice a week, he can also learn on his own on the other days. Torah study is mandatory every single day, and with an increase on Shabbos.

3) Regarding your eldest son, may he live, and his current lifestyle, which is not suitable—neither in terms of his environment nor his lack of interest in his future, etc.—and he justifies this by saying that he did not succeed, in his opinion, in his studies in the past, and so on.

You will certainly find the appropriate words to explain to him that this thought of "lack of success" is **forbidden**, as it leads to a lack of energy and a deficiency in terms of getting settled, especially since there is no basis for it. The fact that one does not succeed in a certain area cannot serve as proof or a reason for discouragement at all. It is possible that he will succeed in other areas, even more than usual. Furthermore, the reasons for a lack of success can be external and not dependent on the person himself. The Creator of the world gives every single person the strengths and possibilities to settle into an orderly life, provided that we follow His command and instruction: "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you **do**"—specifically through action. It is also understood that in order to make it easier for your son, may he live, to enter a straight and productive path, it would be especially good for him to join a religious kibbutz as soon as possible. As for his fear that the discipline there is too strict for him, etc., I am confident that he will only feel this during the first few days. After a short time, on the contrary, the positive aspects will make him completely forget the difficulties of his initial entry into the kibbutz.

It is appropriate that your husband, may he live, set aside a few coins for tzedakah every weekday before morning davening. You should also follow the custom of virtuous Jewish women to set aside tzedakah before lighting the candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

With blessings for good news and a kosher and happy Pesach,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 665

In response to your letter in which you write about your studies at the vocational school in Kfar Chabad, and conclude regarding the difficult financial situation in your home, and that therefore someone suggested that perhaps you should go out to work as a laborer, etc., in order to assist with the livelihood.

Therefore, it is certain that if you continue your studies with the appropriate diligence and perseverance, this is the greatest assistance you can provide for the household's livelihood—and not by stopping your studies, Heaven forbid, to begin working. This is in addition to the simple calculation that if you continue your studies and consequently become an expert in your profession, you will be able to earn (after a few years) much more than as a simple laborer. May it be His will that you dedicate your time to the study of Torah with diligence and perseverance, and fulfill the mitzvos with beauty, and may Hashem bless all the members of your household with what they require.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.

6167

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 27th of Adar and the one preceding it, in which you write regarding the financial situation of the yeshivah. While the spiritual state is of the highest order, the material situation is most difficult. It is understood that you must turn to the activists in this field in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and given the general situation, a one-time appeal is insufficient; rather, one must arouse and remind them time and again.

Regarding what you wrote about the shidduch—that you met with the young woman and her conduct did not seem right to you—in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, there are many young women who are G-d-fearing and anxious to fulfill the word of Hashem and His mitzvos—may they increase—and the Ribono shel Olam will provide you with your suitable match, as it is written, "A prudent wife is from Hashem." It is understood that any increase on your part in matters of Torah and mitzvos will add to the blessing of Hashem in what you require.

I was alarmed by your writing that you have no concept regarding pnimiyus haTorah (which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chabad). My intention is primarily regarding the fact that you write about this with such indifference, as if it were a peripheral matter or something optional. Yet, all parts of the Torah complete one another, for it is one Torah for us all. One who contemplates the fiery words in the holy Zohar, and at greater length in the words of the Arizal—and from them in the introduction of Rav Chaim Vital to Shaar HaHakdamos (which are explained even further in Kuntres Eitz Chaim by the Rebbe Rashab)—will see how vital this matter is, especially in this generation, the footsteps of Moshiach. See there how the terrifying decrees, etc., are due to the lack of engagement in pnimiyus haTorah, the "Tree of Life." Especially for those who are engaged in establishing and disseminating Yiddishkeit, it is simple that they must not only set times for this study, but also increase it from time to time and disseminate this study wherever their reach extends. For there is no room—on one hand, to engage in diminishing the darkness of the golus, and on the other hand, to cause all those consequences brought in the aforementioned sefarim that result from the lack of study of pnimiyus haTorah. It is difficult to elaborate on this alarming matter, as, due to our many sins, so many err in this and pay no heed to the declaration of the Arizal that in our generations, it is a duty and a mitzvah to reveal this wisdom (he refers to the study of pnimiyus haTorah). The matter of study is specifically through understanding and comprehension, not merely rote recitation, as per the well-known halachic ruling regarding the mitzvah of Torah study; see also Magen Avraham to Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, siman 50.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 6168

6168

B"H, 7 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc.,
R' Avraham Moshe, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 2 Nissan, the day of the hillula of our Rebbe, the Rebbe Rashab, of blessed memory, of righteous memory, of holy memory, may his merit protect us and all of Israel.

In it, you ask about that which is brought in many places in Tanya, in D'ch, and in Chassidic literature in general, regarding the statement of our Sages that "the Patriarchs are the Chariot." You note that this indicates their bitul to Hashem, similar to the bitul of a chariot to the one who rides upon it. You express wonder, as in several books, the concept of the "Chariot" is explained to mean that through this, the Holy One, blessed be He, conducts the world.

It is not understood where the contradiction lies between these two details, for on the contrary, they complement one another. In Tanya, the level of the **person** is explained—his standing and his state in his avodah to his Creator, through which his avodah becomes in the category of a "Chariot." In the books that discuss them, they explain the **action in the world** that comes about through this.

This is analogous to the explanation of the concept of Kehunah and the Kohanim, who are the shluchim in the avodah of the Beis Hamikdash to offer the sacrifices of Israel, etc. This concerns their action in the world and in the Mikdash specifically. Regarding their standing and level in the avodah of Hashem, it is—in the language of the Rambam (at the end of Hilchos Shemittah V'Yovel)—like the Leviim, whose spirit moved them and whose knowledge enlightened them to separate themselves to stand before Hashem, etc., and they were separated from the ways of the world, etc.

It is my hope that you have fixed times for the study of Chassidus and that you also influence your surroundings to disseminate this study, for it is the demand of the hour and also a necessity, as is explained at length with wonderful words in the introduction of R' Chaim Vital, the foremost student of the Arizal, to Shaar HaHakdamos. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 6169

[7 Nissan 5718]

...Regarding his studies, the statement of our Sages, "You have labored and you have found," is well known. From this it is understood that the success of his learning is in his own hands. However, in order to increase *siyata d’shmaya*, he should be careful to go to the *mikveh* (for *tvilas Ezra*), and every weekday before *davening* he should set aside a coin for *tzedakah*. Furthermore, every day after *davening*—including on *Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*—he should recite the daily portion of *Tehillim* as it is divided for the days of the month.

Regarding what you wrote about his ailment, he is surely under the care of a specialist and is following his instructions. It is well known that peace of mind and the strengthening of one’s *bitachon* are among the most excellent remedies for ailments such as these.

He surely has a set time for studying *Toras HaChassidus*, and he increases this from time to time, for as with every matter of Torah and *mitzvos*, we are commanded that "we increase in holiness."

## 670

670

B"H, 9 Nissan, 5718

Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—which was significantly delayed before reaching me—in which you write regarding your second daughter, may she live, who is currently in the United States and has not yet become engaged.

It is understood, and especially consistent with the custom in the United States, that it is difficult to take any action in this matter before the person concerned herself reaches out to ask for advice or, at the very least, to discuss the matter. For it is contrary to the accepted custom here to invite someone and inquire about their situation, etc., especially regarding the youth—even those born elsewhere, provided they have been here for some time and are familiar with the local customs. Nevertheless, since everything is by Divine Providence and I have received your letter regarding the aforementioned matter, I will endeavor to find ways to have one of my friends or acquaintances speak with her and clarify the situation, perhaps to see if some path can be found in the direction you wrote about in your letter.

Certainly, for someone like yourself, it is unnecessary to elaborate that you need not ask forgiveness for writing to me about this. For the matter of assisting in *shidduchim* for a son of Yisrael, and especially for a daughter of Yisrael, is something our Sages were deeply concerned with, and they spoke at length of its greatness and importance. Indeed, it is founded upon the principle: "Great is Torah, and love your fellow as yourself."

May it be Hashem's will that the promise of our Torah, the Torah of life, be fulfilled in you: "Those who honor the Sages will have sons-in-law who are Sages." And may it be His will that you be accustomed to a "good lamp" (*sharga tava*)—in the inner sense of the matter, as explained in the holy Zohar, that oil represents the secrets of the secrets of the Torah. The Chanukah lamp and the Shabbos lamp have the specific purpose of illuminating the darkness, or illuminating even the outside—that is, to disseminate and explain even the secrets of the Torah. And as the *sugya* there indicates, the result of this is sons and sons-in-law who are *talmidei chachamim*.

With respect and blessings for good tidings in all the above, and for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 6171

B"H, 9 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished,
R' Yaakov, may he live.

...Regarding the Gemara in Kiddushin 57a, which poses the question concerning the bird of a metzora that was slaughtered and found to be a treifah: why is it permitted for benefit? Where was its prohibition (its status as hekdesh) permitted? (Rashi).

You raise a difficulty: Why not say that it was not slaughtered with the intent that it be a treifah, similar to the principle in Bava Kamma (110b)?

Therefore, it is **impossible** to say so, for if that were the case, when its blood is spilled, why would the bird that is sent away die? — as the conclusion of the aforementioned Mishnah states (Negaim 14:5).

The reason why we do not apply the principle of "it was not slaughtered with that intent" in such a case can be explained by several arguments.

The one that appeals to me most is along the lines of what is written in Tosafos (s.v. *Ada'ata*, Bava Kamma ibid.), that one does not contemplate such a possibility. In our case as well, one does not contemplate the possibility [of it being a treifah], for we do not concern ourselves with the possibility of treifos. This is especially true according to the explanation of the Gemara in Kiddushin that it became a treifah through the slaughter itself—and the majority of those involved in slaughtering are experts. This is particularly true regarding kodshim, which require kavanah, and even more so according to the halacha regarding the bird of a metzora, where the slaughter must be performed by kohanim—who are diligent.

Alternatively, one could say: When it has been slaughtered, it is not within one's power to say "it was not slaughtered with that intent" (and furthermore, one would not wish to stipulate such a condition during the slaughter), because doing so would render it a case of slaughtering chullin in the Azarah.

Alternatively, one could say: When it has been slaughtered, it is already in the domain of the kohen. And if one were to stipulate in such a case, it would be as mentioned above.

This is analogous to the question regarding terumah and kodshim, which does not apply in these two ways (Nedarim 59a; Divrei Chamudos and Shach, Yoreh Deah, siman 323, se'if 2).

B"H, 9 Nissan, 5718

## 6173

B"H, 10 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with the needs of the community, etc., R' Yosef, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha,

I received your letter in due time, responding to my comments regarding the Yud-Tes Kislev celebration in Kfar Chabad. While I must say that the explanation in your letter did not satisfy me—as it is based, in the words of your letter, on the fact that "since I am not among those who merited growing up in a Chassidic environment, I did not feel myself on that level of the soul, etc."—this is, in fact, the foundation of all matters of Torah and Jewish custom. For "a Jewish custom is Torah," and we must first fulfill them through *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke), and subsequently, they exert their influence upon our revealed soul-powers as well. This follows the well-known principle of *naaseh* (we will do) preceding *nishma* (we will understand), for ultimately, the *nishma* follows as well.

However, there is no point in crying over the past. My hope is that in the future there will be no room for such debate, and that you will participate in *farbrengens* without prior calculation—in the humorous vein of the saying regarding a standard meal, where the "distinguished ones of Jerusalem would not recline at it," etc.

As we approach the Festival of Matzos, the time of our freedom, I send you my wishes for true freedom from Egypt, from limitations, and from all matters that cause confusion, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 674

674

B”H, 10 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the end of Shevat—which took longer than usual to arrive—

It gave me pleasure to read that you are within a Chabad framework. It is certainly unnecessary to emphasize that being part of this framework means taking an interest in, and studying, its Torah. More importantly, it means conducting oneself in accordance with the instructions and customs of this Torah.

It is human nature to progress step by step, rather than going from one extreme to the other all at once. However, the path and the journey must be in this direction, and there is nothing that can stand before the will. I hope you will bring me good news regarding your progress in this, and that you will also influence your friends in this regard.

2) Regarding the matter of tzitzis, where the tzitzis become soiled while at work:

One must wear a tallis katan (adorned with tzitzis) at all times, especially since this is surely the main part of your work and the majority of your day. You should make every effort to avoid soiling them, and ensure that you have a second tallis katan for the time of davening, for Shabbos Kodesh, and for Yom Tov.

3) Regarding the place and manner of davening, it is understood that this depends on the local conditions. Therefore, you should consult with those who are knowledgeable in this matter. May it be His will that you make a good decision, appropriate to the intent and purpose of davening, which is the "service of the heart" that brings a person closer to their Creator and draws down the blessings of Hashem to fulfill a person’s needs for the good.

I am certain you utilized the days of Purim in an appropriate manner, and that you have a suitable plan for the upcoming days of the festival of Pesach. May it be His will that you strengthen yourselves in Yiddishkeit, in Torah and mitzvos in your daily life, for as the Mishnah states, "the deed is the essential thing."

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

B"H, 10 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Shabbos. Since we are currently in the auspicious days of the month of Nissan, the month of redemption, it is my hope that you will bring me good news regarding an improvement in all matters. This is the concept of the exodus from Egypt that occurs every single day—an exodus from matters that restrict, distress, and conceal. This, of course, includes matters of physical health, for as the Rambam states, maintaining a healthy and sound body is among the ways of Hashem.

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate that the stronger one’s *bitachon*, the sooner one sees this [improvement] and to a greater degree. Especially knowing your wife’s family through our correspondence, it is certainly unnecessary to elaborate for her—not only on the necessity of *bitachon*, but also on the fact that it is a relatively easy *avodah*. For one who observes with open eyes sees the *hashgacha* of the Ribono shel Olam and the kindness of the Ribono shel Olam day by day. Even though one encounters matters of concealment and difficulty in life—as we live in this world, which is a physical and material world, the lowest world in the *seder hishtalshelus*, as is explained at length in *Tanya* and elsewhere—the Creator of the world gives strength to every man and woman of *anash* not to be impressed by this, and to proceed in the ways of the Torah day by day, step by step, with joy and a good heart. On the contrary, *bitachon* and joy themselves diminish the concealments and hiddenness, and one sees tangibly that from the outset, it was nothing more than a matter of a test.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach and for good tidings.

## 176

B"H, 10 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

...Regarding what is written in the Siddur to say before davening, "I hereby accept upon myself the positive mitzvah of..."

There is no need to add "bli neder" (without a vow) — since the Alter Rebbe did not specify this — and there is no place for it at all, for it is a mitzvah (see Nedarim 8, top of the first column; Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah 209, at the end).

## 6157

6157

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5718

(may he live and be well) surely also conveyed to you that I emphasized the point that the matter of separation is truly not only a religious question, but also a moral one, and if you will, a pedagogical one that is accepted by the heart. For the great destruction caused by mixed education is well known, both from a moral perspective and from the perspective of education and learning, as it negatively impacts the focus of the students—both in their studies and in their laboratory work—which, in a short time, also affects their comprehension of their studies, and so on. Surely, for someone like you, elaboration on this is superfluous. With appropriate and persistent explanation, it is surely possible to convince those who have the opinion and the ability to rectify the matter. May it be the will of Hashem that He grant them the merit to accept your words in their entirety, to bring the matter into actual practice, and to do so promptly.

For "man is a tree of the field," and in his youth, he is like a tender sapling, where even a slight scratch is liable to leave a blemish on the full-grown tree. This is why acting promptly is so important, especially in rectifying matters of education.

As we approach the Festival of Matzos, the time of our freedom, which comes upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I send you my blessing for a kosher and happy Pesach, and for true freedom from Egypt, from limitations, and from anything that distracts, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

## 6178

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may Hashem protect them
Tel Aviv Branch
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and peace!

After the **longest** of intervals, I received your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, 2 Nissan—the day of the Hilula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—along with the enclosed report of your activities throughout the winter months.

May it be Hashem’s will that your activities increase, both in quantity and in quality, in accordance with the demands and the necessity of the hour. The magnitude of the reward for those who occupy themselves with this is beyond expression, as is explained in many places. Certainly, the Ribono shel Olam, who does not deal tyrannically with His creatures, provides the opportunities and the strengths to fulfill this work completely. Through this, the blessings also come in their fullness—and indeed, with the addition of the Ribono shel Olam, which exceeds the primary measure.

May it be His will that, just as in those days, so too in this time—in accordance with the statement of our Sages—that in the merit of righteous women our ancestors were redeemed from the first exile, so too may we merit in this, our generation, in the final exile, that Moshiach Tzidkeinu will redeem us very soon, truly and completely. May the prophecy be fulfilled: "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders."

With blessings for success in your holy work, for good tidings regarding all that was mentioned, and for a kosher and happy Pesach.

679

B”H, 11 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our brethren, the Children of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

Every Yom Tov has its own unique content, and therefore its own specific teachings and directives, which are relevant to everyone to whom the Yom Tov is given. That is to say, to every Jew—as an individual and as a part of Klal Yisrael—as well as to Klal Yisrael as a whole.

The character of each Yom Tov is reflected and expressed in the name of the Yom Tov and in the mitzvos, laws, and customs associated with it.

One of the primary aspects of the Yom Tov of Pesach is indicated in the name that the Anshei Knesses HaGedolah established for this festival—*Zman Cheiruseinu*, the time of our freedom.

And the Torah, which is called *Toras Chaim*, a guide for life, demands that every Jew remember—that is, relive—this freedom, *Yitziyas Mitzrayim*, every single day of our lives. As the Sages express it:

In every generation and every day, a Jew must **see** himself as if he personally went out of Mitzrayim that day.

This instruction and demand are directed to **every** generation—both in the times when we had the kingdom of the House of David and the Beis HaMikdash for generations, and in the dark times of the eras of persecution, *R”L*.

And it is directed to every Jew **every** day. Even though he relived *Yitziyas Mitzrayim* yesterday, he must experience *Yitziyas Mitzrayim* anew today, and again tomorrow.

For the content of *Yitziyas Mitzrayim* consists of freeing oneself from the obstacles and limitations that stand in one’s way and prevent one from being what one must be and doing what one must do.

Therefore, the *Yitziyas Mitzrayim* of yesterday is insufficient for one’s state and level today, and the *Yitziyas Mitzrayim* of today will be insufficient for tomorrow.

***

A reflection that makes the aforementioned even clearer and sharper: Among the levels of the world around us is the *tzomeiach* (vegetative). When everything necessary for growth—earth, water, air, etc.—is provided in full measure, the *tzomeiach* is "freed" from all its "worries" and obstacles. And although it cannot move from its place—it is "sentenced" to remain there all its years—it possesses the full freedom of a *tzomeiach*. As long as it is nothing more than a *tzomeiach*, it is truly free.

However, a *chai* (living creature), even if it is provided with all its needs of food, drink, etc., if it is forced to remain in one place, this is the greatest limitation for it—a prison, the most terrible prison, because it lacks the **essence** of its being.

A human being, who is a rational creature—even if he has the full freedom of movement, if he is locked away from a life of intellect, he finds himself in a prison, a prison that robs him of his **essential being**.

And so it is in the world of intellect itself: whoever is capable of reaching the highest levels of intellect, yet is restricted to the intellectual life of a small child—this is the most difficult prison for his **true self**. And if he limits himself to this—

By squandering his years, intellect, and potential on food, drink, etc., and seeking only how to obtain food and drink, without rising any higher—

Then, in many respects, this self-imposed prison is far more bitter and carries harsher consequences.

***

Jews, each of whom possesses a *nefesh elokis*, a literal part of Hashem from above, which—even when clothed in the *nefesh habahamis* and in the body—is connected to the Ribono shel Olam, to the *Ein Sof*—its yearning for its true freedom, for *Yitziyas Mitzrayim*, is constant and "infinite." It cannot remain in one place. Every day, with the added *aliyah* through Torah and mitzvos, which bring one closer to the *Ein Sof*, it feels deep inside that yesterday’s level is already "Mitzrayim," from which one must go out in order to rise higher.

***

May the Ribono shel Olam help that the coming *Zman Cheiruseinu* should bring everyone the liberation from all obstacles—physical, material, and spiritual—and that we should rise, with joy and goodness of heart, ever higher and higher—until the *Zman Cheiruseinu* in its fullest measure—the *Geulah HaAmitis VeHaShleimah* through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 6181

6181

B"H, 12 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

After a very long silence, I received your letter of 10 Nissan. It goes without saying that it caused me pain to read that in the matter of your son, shlita, there is currently no news, and that you offer no explanation for this. As for your son, shlita—if I am not mistaken, I have not received any letters from him at all since before Rosh Hashanah, and even then, he did not write regarding this matter.

While I do not know the exact reason for the above, I surmise that it stems from being overly selective and focusing on details that are not at all important. I am surprised by him; how does this come to be? He surely knows that such an approach does not align with the demands of our Torah, Toras Chaim. This is especially true for your son, shlita, who studied for many years in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim and conducts himself in all other matters according to the guidance of Toras HaChassidus. Yet, when it comes to such a highly important matter and a highly important mitzvah, there is a reluctance to fulfill what the Torah instructs in this regard.

It goes without saying that I do not mean that one should enter a shidduch with closed eyes, without knowing what or when. However, after a very, very long time during which I spoke with him and later also wrote to him that one must act energetically regarding a shidduch, there has long been the opportunity to settle on one of the suggestions that have come up during this time—especially in our Holy Land, tichyeh, where the circle of suitable suggestions is larger than in other countries. It is also understood that my writing this to you is not intended to cause you pain, chas v'shalom, but rather to draw your attention to it, in case you or others might have influence to persuade your son, shlita, to fundamentally change his approach to this matter, in accordance with the guidance of our holy Torah, as mentioned earlier.

I am not at all opposed to you showing this letter to your son, shlita, but I leave that to your discretion. May it be His will that, just as we approach the joyous days of Pesach—when we have seen the kindnesses of Hashem even with our physical eyes, and even in matters that were connected with great difficulties, even more so than the matter of your son, shlita—this should also be a fortunate time, and that you will soon be able to share good news in this regard.

Regarding what you write at the end of your letter, that for others it also takes time: in the cases I am aware of, this is mostly due to reasons beyond one's control. But as I said, in this case, I assume it is due to a mindset that is hindering progress, and a focus on details that are entirely unimportant.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S. I would have written directly to your son, shlita, but I am not doing so because I do not know the reason why he is not writing to me. You will surely convey to him the content of what has been written, or the entire letter. I only wish to add to it a blessing for him for a chag Pesach kasher v'sameach and a good shidduch very soon.

## 6,183

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in the needs of the community, etc.,
Rabbi A. D. (may he live and be well)

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received the "Shalom" booklet for Pesach, as well as the one preceding it. I am certain that you will continue to do so in the future, sending me materials published for the benefit of the Jewish soldiers under your influence, and I thank you in advance.

Furthermore, I am certain it will also be of benefit in your avodah, for this is the primary intent of these words—that they reach the attention of the greatest number of our fellow Jews, including those under your influence, of course, and find an echo in their hearts.

This is also one of the points of the Pesach Seder, which begins by gathering all four sons. Even if at the beginning of the Seder they represent four different types, by the end, they all answer and say with one voice and with the appropriate hispaalus: "Next year in Jerusalem." It is well known that the concept of "Jerusalem" is the perfection of yirah, as brought in Midrash Rabbah, Bereishis (ch. 56, 10), and as explained at length by the Alter Rebbe, the author of the Tanya, in his book Likutei Torah, Chelek Devarim, on the verse "And those who were lost in the land of Ashur and those who were cast out in the land of Mitzrayim"—who are the vast majority of the aforementioned four sons—"shall come and bow down to Hashem on the holy mountain in Jerusalem."

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 6184

6184

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 3 Nissan, in which you ask:

1) You have dedicated your time to studying Torah, and consequently, you are not studying the English language as you should. You are seventeen years old and ask if this order is correct.

Certainly, this is correct. Our holy Torah is called Toras Chaim—the Torah of Life—not only because of the life in the World to Come, but also because of life in this world. This means that through persistence and diligence in Torah study (and great is study, for it leads to action—the fulfillment of mitzvos), this is the most correct and appropriate preparation for a livelihood when the time comes. You will certainly find the appropriate words to explain this to your parents, may they live.

2) Since for everything one requires Siyata Dishmaya, it is appropriate that every weekday, before morning davening, you set aside some coins for tzedakah. And every day, including Shabbos and Yom Tov, after morning davening, you should recite the daily portion of Tehillim—as the Tehillim is divided for the days of the month. It is also very good to keep the known daily shiurim of Chumash and Tanya.

With blessings for good tidings, for Torah study with yiras shamayim, for the fulfillment of mitzvos with hidur, and for a kosher and happy Pesach,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

P.S.

## 6185

6185

B”H, 13 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding your article, stating that in your opinion it does not contradict the tradition, but rather its intent is to clarify a historical matter, etc.

Regarding that which is printed for the public, the essential point is what conclusion the reader will draw from the printed words. Therefore, even if the writer’s intent is pure and desirable, he must clothe himself in the reader’s perspective and foresee the consequences.

The extent to which Chazal emphasized the benefit of others is highlighted in their statement in Sifrei (24:19) regarding one who lost a sela and a poor person came and found it; it is considered charity for him, even though he did not intend to perform a mitzvah. Similarly, in general, they permitted charity that is not *lishmah* (for its own sake), since it concerns the benefit of others.

To my regret, the impression received by the reader of the aforementioned article is that the opinion accepted by the Rabbis of Israel has been refuted, etc. It is surely unnecessary to emphasize the custom in the United States, where in such matters people apply the principles of *binyan av* and *gezeirah shavah*—that if they have been refuted on this point, it implies that all their words are subject to criticism and scrutiny, and whoever innovates in this regard gains the upper hand.

Enclosed are the main points from the recent farbrengen, and I hope that you will find in them substance and benefit.

Approaching the festival of Pesach, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I send you my blessing for a kosher and joyous Pesach, and for true freedom from everything that causes confusion, and for an exodus from the constraints of Mitzrayim, as explained in Chassidus.

With respect and blessing,

#### ***6185***

**In general, they permitted:** See at length the *drush* of the Tzemach Tzedek (in the name of the Alter Rebbe?) in the journal *Yagdil Torah* (N.Y.), Issue 36, Section 138.

## 6186

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned individual, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
R' Yitzchak, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter, as well as the book *HaSaba HaKadosh*, and the booklet *Machanayim* in which your article on the Aliyah of the Chassidim to Eretz Yisrael and the Aliyah of Chabad appeared. Thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending them to me. I trust you will also send your other books to my library for the benefit of the many.

May it be the will of Hashem that you utilize the talents with which you have been gifted by Divine Providence to disseminate the concepts of Chassidus, its Torah, and its way of life, to ever-widening circles. And although the dissemination of Yiddishkeit in general is certainly necessary—serving as the foundation and background for the dissemination of the concepts of Chassidus—the special importance of a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others is well known (see Moed Katan 9b and there). While mitzvos in general do not equal even one word of Torah study, a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others tips the scales to the point that it overrides Torah study. Therefore, the matter of disseminating Chassidus, for which there are few experts, falls into the category of a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others. Anyone gifted with a special talent for this must prioritize it, even over the work of disseminating Yiddishkeit in general. Furthermore, one mitzvah leads to another, and it is impossible for a Yid to absorb the concepts of Chassidus without this ultimately causing a revolution in his world and his way of life regarding Yiddishkeit, its matters, the Torah of truth, and its mitzvos.

As we approach the Chag HaMatzos, which is coming upon us and all of Yisrael for good, I hereby express my blessing for a kosher and joyous holiday and for true freedom—freedom from material worries and spiritual worries—from everything that hinders the service of Hashem with joy and a glad heart.

And may you continue this freedom and joy throughout all the days of the year.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

B”H, 23 Nissan, 5718

Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 3rd of Chol Hamoed Pesach, in which you write regarding the sale of the plot of land.

It is already known how our Sages of blessed memory viewed the sale of land in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established). However, regarding a daughter’s dowry, the aforementioned restriction does not apply (though even in this case, it is worthwhile to retain some portion of real estate in Eretz Yisrael for oneself). This is not the case, however, regarding the travel expenses for the wedding; one must consider whether the aforementioned sale is worthwhile, especially since the expenses involved are significant.

It is appropriate that you convene three of your friends and detail the entire matter to them, and may Hashem grant them the correct insight on how to advise you.

With blessings.
