## 6,192

B"H, 24 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 13 Nissan, with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed, which will be read at a time of favor at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—in which you write regarding the thought that your son, may he live and be well, should travel to study at the *yeshiva* here.

I have already written to several of *anash* regarding such matters, that such thoughts are nothing more than enticements of the *yetzer hara* to confuse them from considering how to arrange things properly. For the "workshop of the world is one," and the *yetzer hara* travels even across borders of countries and lands. However, when they are in close proximity to their parents, there is additional *hashgacha* beyond the *hashgacha* of the *yeshiva* administration, which is not the case in a foreign land. And even though the statement of our Sages is known, "Exile yourself to a place of Torah," this is not relevant to our current discussion, for we are not coming to negate the question of pampering, and *kal v'chomer* (it is understood).

Regarding this, the same applies to what you write, that "apparently this is my *mazal* and my fate, etc." It is a great wonder for *anash* in general, and especially for *temimim*, to multiply such words and to write them, at a time when our Sages have clearly explained the teaching of our Sages, "There is no *mazal* for Yisrael." This refers to *mazal* in its literal sense—it does not exist in reality. And regarding the true *mazal*, the interpretation is "there is no *mazal* for Yisrael," in accordance with the interpretation of the *Zohar* on the verse, "Is there a tree in it or not?"

With blessings for good tidings in general matters and in private matters, for the one hangs upon the other.

#### ***6,192***

**I have already written:** See letter 6,153 above. See Vol. 14, letter 5,105, and the references in the notes there.

6193

B"H, 24 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R. Yaakov Meir, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter—which lacks the date of writing—in which you ask:

1) How should a resident of Eretz Yisrael who traveled abroad with his family conduct himself regarding the second day of Yom Tov?

Our practical custom, and indeed the straightforward approach, is that he should follow the custom of the place to which he has traveled, especially since he is accompanied by his family. The same applies in reverse: a resident of the Diaspora who travels with his family to Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) follows the custom of Eretz Yisrael. It is understood that this applies even if he intends to return after some time to the place from which he came (for if he traveled with the intention of settling there permanently, what is there to teach?).

2) The order for beginners studying the Tanya: Although I have not heard a definitive instruction on this, it seems to me—and this is how I answer those who ask—that one should begin with Iggeres HaTeshuvah, then Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah, then Part I (Sefer Shel Beinonim), and finally Iggeres HaKodesh. Naturally, this applies to beginners; but after having studied it once or twice, one should study it in the established order, as is also evident from the study schedule printed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and it is also simple logic, as the sections are named Part I, Part II, etc.

It is worth noting the Chassidic stories that there was initially an opinion that Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah should precede the Sefer Shel Beinonim, and they bring proof for this from the language in the introduction to Shaar HaYichud, "as will be explained," and the matters were explained in the Sefer Shel Beinonim.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding your efforts in spreading the wellsprings of Chassidus until they reach the "outside," as I believe I have written to you many times that this is the demand and necessity of the hour, as explained in the writings of the Arizal, and specifically to his primary disciple, R. Chaim Vital, in the introduction to Shaar HaHakdamos—words that are startling and wondrous.

With blessings for good tidings.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 625

B"H, 26 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Nissan.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you, as well as the young lady (may she live) about whom you write, at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, each according to the content of your letter.

Regarding your question, etc.: Experience has shown that, in general, one succeeds more and more quickly through pleasant ways. We see this tangibly: through "propaganda" in action—that is, not merely by proving the incorrectness of the path she is currently following, but by providing her (as if inadvertently) with positive matters to occupy herself with, which will also interest her without the need for propaganda—one is more likely to detach her from the undesirable things, and this is easy to understand. And although in such a case it is necessary for someone to take a stance of protest against her behavior, as I see from the letters, this protest is coming from the father (may he live) with full force. Furthermore, even when conducting oneself in pleasant ways, this does not preclude a protest that is also expressed in a pleasant manner.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 696

In response to your letter of Monday, in which you write that you are eighteen years old and studying in a yeshiva, and regarding what people in your environment are telling you concerning your future:

It is a simple matter that you must continue your studies in the yeshiva, studying the holy Torah, for it is the channel and the vessel for receiving the blessings of Hashem, the Giver of the Torah, who alone sustains and provides for everyone with goodness, grace, kindness, and mercy. Certainly, being meticulous in your observance of mitzvos will add to the blessings of Hashem, including regarding your future livelihood when the time comes for that. There are thousands upon thousands of avreichim of your age and even older who study Torah with diligence and persistence and are successful; many of them have already become established in matters of livelihood after having studied Torah. Things that are well-known require no proof. It is my hope that you will find acquaintances who can explain all of the above to those who speak to you in a different spirit. May it be His will that you study Torah with such diligence and persistence that it leads to exertion, and may the promise of the holy Torah be fulfilled in you: "You have exerted yourself and you have found."

6197

28 Nissan, 5718
Brooklyn

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter of the 15th, in which you write regarding your son that he has become acquainted with a non-Jewish girl, and according to how you express it, she is going to a Rav to become Jewish and is keeping kashrus, and your son—as you put it—is putting his whole world into this matter, and you ask what you should do in such a case.

Before you decide on your approach to this, you must do two things:

a) Find a way for your son, may he live and be well, to meet Jewish girls. It is possible that one of them will please him, and that would be the best way to resolve the entire matter. Although in this country it is not customary for parents to officially arrange shidduchim for their children, as is done in **thousands** of cases, parents arrange such opportunities without the children knowing that it originated from them. You write that your son is in California and do not write in which city, but if it is a city where there are many Jews, there are various opportunities to arrange this. Given your son’s occupation, it is certainly connected to Jewish homes, through which this can be done.

b) One must find out to which Rav she is going there, and what is meant by her "becoming Jewish." You can likely find out the name of the Rav through your son, but in such a way that he does not think that you are in agreement with the matter, for then the attempt with the first method would be lost.

You add in your letter that you do not know why this is happening to you, etc.

In many cases, such occurrences are a result of the mother, at the time she was pregnant with the child, not having properly observed the laws of Taharas Hamishpacha (mikveh, hefsek taharah, etc.). If in your case this was so, chas v'shalom, then in order to rectify this to a certain extent, you should endeavor to influence other Jewish women to observe the laws of Taharas Hamishpacha. When you influence at least two or three, this will, to a certain extent, be an atonement for the aforementioned.

You should have the mezuzos in your home checked (bedikah) to ensure they are all kosher according to the law. You should also maintain the good custom of the kosher daughters of Israel to give charity every time before lighting candles on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6199

6199

B"H, 28 Nissan, 5718

I received your letter with great surprise, in which you write regarding my suggestion that your son... *shiyeh* should go on **a shlichus of mine** to... and you strongly oppose this in your letter.

But it turned out that before he makes a decision, he must hear what his mother and family *shichyu* have to say. And it is self-evident that this is not the work of a soldier — to ask for conditions, how much time, and then to inquire of the family for their opinion on the matter.

Therefore, I am withdrawing my suggestion entirely. Consequently, you have no reason to be agitated, and you need not write about how this affects your health, for it goes without saying that I do not wish to affect anyone’s health.

May Hashem Yisbarach help them and you with much success in all that you need, and may it be His will that this should be true success, in a way that is good and revealed.

With blessings,

## V’ra

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter—which was delayed in transit much longer than usual before reaching me—in which you write regarding your studies until now and how you have met people from Chabad circles who introduced you to its teachings and concepts.

Since our Sages have said that "great is study, for it leads to action," my hope is strong that this introduction—which surely means that you have studied at least something regarding the teachings of Chabad Chassidus—has led to action. That is to say, an increase in diligence and perseverance in the study of our holy Torah, both the revealed and the Chassidic, as well as greater care in the performance of mitzvos, the refinement of character traits, etc., and that you will also influence your friends—may they live—in this regard. There is nothing that can stand before the will, especially for a young man of your age who is not yet burdened by the worries of livelihood and can dedicate all his time and energy to the study of our holy Torah, the Torah of life. May it be His will that you bring me good news regarding all the above.

With blessings for success in Torah study with fear of Heaven, for the performance of mitzvos with care, and for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.

Regarding what you wrote about matters of Chassidus where you have questions or lack understanding: you should turn to the elder Chassidim in your vicinity and detail the doubts you have. The nature of such matters is that one doubt begets another; that is, when one doubt is resolved, a second doubt—or even two—immediately arises in its place. The general answer to your doubts is to contemplate the reality: the teachings of Chassidus have been active for over two hundred years, and the very phenomena that have caused you to doubt their nature have existed throughout this time. We see the results and the influence of this Torah, which has brought strength in the trials of keeping Torah and mitzvos, and improvement in human character and interpersonal relationships, etc. There is no better proof of the essence of a system than seeing that it leads to good results. Indeed, this is also proof that even **those who opposed** this system generations ago, before they knew its results, had from the very outset **designated** this system with the name "Chassidus," and those who follow it as "Chassidim."

## 602

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...Although you do not mention this, my hope is strong that you are aware of what is told orally and what is also in print: that the eye of a Yid must be a "good eye" regarding others as well. When one hears words of hisorerus and words of Chassidus, one should not hide them away, for then, in most cases, they do not even affect oneself. Rather, one should endeavor to share them with others, for then the impact on oneself is also magnified—as is seen tangibly, and as our Sages said, "And from my students, more than from all of them."

## 6103

6103

B”H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I am responding to your letter—which arrived with much more delay than usual—at an *eis ratzon*, and I will read your *pidyon nefesh* regarding your son, may he live, at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever he needs, and especially for the improvement of his health in the near future.

It is puzzling that you mention consulting with a physician and add that he is not a specialist in his specific ailment, but rather an internist. While it is already said that "in the multitude of counselors there is safety," it is understood and simple that the primary consultant must be a specialist in the field, and there are several specialists in this field in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established. If this is the case for standard treatment, it is all the more so regarding treatment with a new medication, where such medications generally require extra caution, as experience has shown.

It is understood that if a specialist physician prescribes a treatment using medicinal substances that are found only in the United States, then efforts should be made to send them from here, provided that the physician writes out the details of the substances (in the terminology of medical texts and in Latin characters), along with the necessary information for this. For example, as you mention in your letter regarding pills—many of these substances come in pills of different sizes and the like. When you tell a specialist physician that you are writing about this to someone overseas, he will surely know how to specify the substances.

In general, the suggestion is correct that for some time, at least, he should reduce his studies and engage in physical labor, or at the very least, office work. If he is reluctant to do this, as you write in your letter, then it should be clarified that this is a matter of "there is a time to act for Hashem by breaking Your Torah," as the great teacher, the Rambam, also writes in *Hilchos Deios*, end of chapter 3 and beginning of chapter 4.

Since, according to the content of your letter, you are engaged in the "healing of the soul" for your students, it is understood according to the measure of the Holy One, blessed be He—*midah k’neged midah*—that your reward will be doubled regarding the healing of your son, in the literal sense. Furthermore, according to the language of the Rambam, the soul has health and illness just as the body does (*Shemonah Perakim l’HaRambam*, chapter 3, and *Hilchos Deios*, chapter 2). We see in the healing of the body that it is possible to use bitter or sweet substances, and the distinction is understood, especially when the treatment is not a one-time occurrence. In general, the path of *Mussar* and the path of *Chassidus* are divided on this: the content of *Mussar*, as its name implies, is *mussar* (reproof) in the literal sense—that is, the emphasis is on negative matters and character traits, etc. This is unlike the path of *Chassidus*, which emphasizes the loftiness and preciousness of the soul (though this requires the negation of all things that prevent the soul's elevation).

Therefore, it is most appropriate that you establish a fixed time for yourself to study the teachings of *Chassidus*. Although I hope that you study it from time to time anyway, that is not the matter of *kviyus* (fixity). Specifically, as per the instruction of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, *kviyus* means not only in time, but—and this is the main point—*kviyus* in the soul. Consequently, you should also adopt this approach in your influence upon your students. After all, the ways of the Torah are "ways of pleasantness," and there is nothing that can stand before the will. Especially since you have merited (as you put it in your letter) to hear many lofty *sichos* from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the above.

#### 6103

**As per the instruction of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe:** See also above, Vol. 13, p. 371, and the references in the notes there. Vol. 14, p. 837. Vol. 14, p. 893. Vol. 15, p. 663. Vol. 16, p. 820. Below, 6249. 6273. 6305. 6310. 6318. 6452.

Furthermore, before this is demanded of a Jewish man and woman, they are given the strengths to fulfill this in practice; and not only that, but Hashem assists them, and the practical outcome is certainly understood.

## 6106

6106

B"H, 1 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Nissan, I was pleased to read that for some time now you have been strengthening yourself through the mercies of Hashem, even though you do not mention it specifically. It is my hope that you have studied the holy Tanya, which teaches that one should not be discouraged by the fact that there are ups and downs in the interim, as it is written, "and one nation shall be stronger than the other". See the index printed at the end of the Tanya.

Regarding the proverb you cite concerning [the fact] that a person is given [challenges] according to their strength, this is the essence of the Sages' saying, "According to the camel, the load", and explained in greater detail in Midrash Rabbah on the verse "Hashem tests the righteous" (Bereshis Rabbah 32:3) and in Yalkut Tehillim in its place.

As for your mention that when you study, you are reminded of the Gemara in Yevamos regarding causing *nachas ruach*—this matter concerns the receiving of reward through the performance of *nachas ruach*. However, we have heard something even greater, which is based on the *maamar*, "But in a shadow man walks" (Tehillim 39:7)... that one who repeats a teaching should envision the author of the teaching standing before him. You should also look into the *Likutei Dibburim* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which contains wonderful words on this subject.

At an *eis ratzon*, you will be remembered at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for whatever you need in general, and specifically for success in Torah study with *yiras shamayim* (which is one of the fundamentals in the life of a *bochur*), both in the *nigleh* of Torah and in the teachings of Chassidus.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

## 607

607

B"H, 1 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Nissan and the one preceding it, in which you write of your efforts to ascend in matters of Torah and mitzvos, and the opposition stemming from the *kelipah* of Amalek—namely, coldness and doubts—and you ask for advice regarding this.

The matter is addressed in general in the books of Chassidus in many places. The essential point is this: pay no attention whatsoever to the enticements of the *yetzer*. When it comes with a tactic meant to induce coldness or cast doubt, the advice and the response must be that you have no free time to engage in arguments and counter-arguments. You have to learn, you have to fulfill a certain mitzvah, you have to influence your friends and acquaintances to do the same. After all, each one of us is a servant to the Master of the World, and a servant is not at liberty to waste his time speaking with just anyone, since the Master has charged him with fulfilling this mission and that one.

In order to increase *siyata d’shmaya*, every weekday before morning *davening*, set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*. After *davening* each day—including on *Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*—recite the monthly *Tehillim* portion, as the *Tehillim* is divided for the days of the month. Furthermore, strive to benefit others, both spiritually and materially. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success and bring you good tidings in all the aforementioned.

With blessings,

## 6108

B"H, 1 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, the distinguished Rabbi, scion of holy lineage, etc., etc., our teacher Rabbi Shalom, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 25 Nissan.

It gave me pleasure to read therein about your son’s, may he live, beginning to lay tefillin, and I have enclosed a letter to him as you suggested. It is understood that your son did well to begin laying tefillin now, for we heard explicitly from my father-in-law, the Rebbe (recorded in the *Hayom Yom* for 2 Menachem Av), an instruction to the masses to begin laying tefillin two months before the day of the Bar Mitzvah [this is precise regarding the "masses," for in the Rebbe’s home they would begin much earlier, and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, once related that he began laying tefillin in his twelfth year].

Now, it has not escaped my notice that some of the *Acharonim* (cited in the commentaries on *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim*, end of section 37) hold that since tefillin require a clean body, one should not hasten to lay them, especially in these generations. Nevertheless, since the instruction was given explicitly as mentioned above, it is a mitzvah to fulfill the words of the later sages, especially when they instructed that their opinion be publicized (as expressed by the term "to the masses").

It seems to me that the reason for this instruction is similar to the effort and labor to disseminate the teachings of Chassidus in the widest possible circles, without setting preconditions for this Torah. Although in earlier generations (before the revelation of the Baal Shem Tov, his student the Maggid, and his students, among them the Alter Rebbe), they were particular about such conduct, the parable from the Alter Rebbe is well known: regarding a precious stone from the King’s crown, when the King’s only son falls ill and the danger is great, G-d forbid, the King commands—even for a doubt or a double doubt—to take a precious stone from his crown and attempt to heal his only son with it. As the expression goes, it is worth spilling a great deal [of the essence] outside for the sake of the possibility that a few drops will reach the King’s son so that he may recover and be healed. The analogy is understood.

And we see this tangibly in recent years, how the dissemination of Chassidus has saved many from various trials and obstacles; these things are well known to all those who were in the countries of Russia and stood firm in the trials there, etc.

At a time of favor, please mention all those you write about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be His will that you bring good tidings in all the matters mentioned in your letter.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

## 614

B"H, 1 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the avreich Avraham Mordechai, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to hear that you have begun to put on tefillin.

May it be the will of Hashem that this be at a good and auspicious time, and may you achieve all the matters associated with this. It begins in the literal sense—as explained in the Shulchan Aruch and brought down in the Tanya Kadisha at the beginning of Chapter 41: "And specifically through tefillin, etc." (see there). Indeed, the entire Torah is compared to tefillin; meaning, that through the action of tefillin, one draws down [influence] into all matters of Torah. And after the two-month preparation, may you accept upon yourself on the day of your Bar Mitzvah the yoke of Torah and mitzvos in its entirety.

## 6116

B"H, 1 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 23 Adar II in due time, along with the enclosure. In accordance with my request, my friend Dr. Seligson—may he live and be well—consulted with one of the leading specialists in this field. Enclosed is Dr. Seligson’s letter, in which he conveys the specialist’s opinion. May Hashem Yisbarach help that it should be successful, and may you be able to report good news regarding this very soon.

However, as we say in the *Birchas HaShachar*, Hashem Yisbarach is the true *Rofeh Kol Basar U’mafli La’asos* (Healer of all flesh and Worker of wonders), and the doctors are nothing more than His *shluchim*. Therefore, it is absolutely necessary to conduct one’s daily life in accordance with the instructions of the *Rofeh Kol Basar U’mafli La’asos*. Especially when it concerns children, the first and foremost priority is that the laws and *dinim* of our holy Torah regarding *Taharas HaMishpacha* (Niddah, *hefsek taharah*, *mikveh*, and the like) must be strictly observed. No matter how good the situation may be in this regard, there is always room to add more, and Hashem Yisbarach is trusted to add to His blessings in whatever one is in need of.

It would be a proper thing to have your *tefillin* checked (*check-up*), as well as the *mezuzos* in your home, to ensure that they are all *kosher* according to the *din*. Also, your wife—may she live and be well—should maintain the good custom of the virtuous daughters of Israel: to give *tzedakah* each time before lighting candles on *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*.

With blessings for good tidings,

P.S. Due to the absence of the secretary who writes in English, this letter is written in Yiddish. However, you may continue to write in English in the future.

## 6111

B.H., 2 Iyar, Tiferes sheb'Tiferes, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all those participating in the laying of the cornerstone for the "Tomchei Temimim" building in Kfar Chabad, and to all our brethren, the Children of Israel, lovers of Torah and mitzvos, may Hashem grant them life,

Shalom Rav and Bracha!

Regarding the laying of the cornerstone for the central building of the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in our Holy Land—may it be built and established speedily in our days through Moshiach Tzidkeinu—I hereby send my heartfelt and soulful blessing to all who are participating in this great simcha shel mitzvah, both those participating at the time of the cornerstone laying and those who participated in the preparations for this and made it possible.

It is my hope that the participation of each and every one will be a full participation, now and in the future—participation with his money, his body, and his soul:

With his money—literally—by pledging the largest possible sums for the construction of the building;

With his body—by exerting himself and laboring as much as is required to be among those who act and who also activate others to participate;

With his soul—meaning, even if it seems to him that his involvement in this mitzvah will temporarily diminish his additional Torah study and the like. For this is the generosity of the soul: to sacrifice from the life of the soul of the individual in order to establish a building and an institution for the public study of Torah. Furthermore, there is the promise, "Give a tithe so that you may become wealthy," for what he does not add for the moment in his own study will be multiplied through this by the study and dissemination of Torah to the many, in which he also acquires a share through his labor.

For the charity of "Zevulun" to enable the Torah of "Yissachar" is not merely charity; rather, he also has a share in the Torah of Yissachar.

***

And if in every place the study of Torah is great, as it is equivalent to them all, how much more so in our Holy Land, may it be built and established, the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year. This is especially true in Kfar Chabad, which was founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, who sacrificed his life for the dissemination of the revealed and internal Torah—Torah that is perfect and complete—and who imbued the students of the Tomchei Temimim yeshivos and the place itself—this village—with the spirit to engage in Torah with self-sacrifice, with vitality, and with light.

And we roll merit through days of merit—the days of Sefira, the days of preparation and yearning for the receiving of the Torah, as the Sages of blessed memory say in the Aggadah:

"At the time that Moshe said to them, 'You shall serve G-d upon this mountain,' the Jewish people said to him, 'Moshe Rabbeinu, when is this service?' He said to them, 'After fifty days.' And each and every one of them counted for himself. From here, the Sages established the counting of... counting fifty days for the Simchas Torah."

It is my hope that this time will serve to arouse and strengthen in each and every one a love for Torah and its matters, and from this—to increase action, in all the ways mentioned above, in the building and establishment of this fortress of Torah: the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Kfar Chabad.

***

And through these actions and this avodah, one elevates the money from the matters of the world and sanctifies it to the perfect Torah (the revealed and the internal) and its institutions, so that we will not be occupied "all our days with things the body needs, but rather we will sit free to study in wisdom and perform the mitzvos."

These actions and our avodah will hasten and bring the true Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, the days of Moshiach, when he will compel all of Israel to walk in the Written and Oral Torah and fight the wars of Hashem, and they will be free to engage in Torah and its wisdom, and the entire world will be occupied with nothing other than knowing Hashem alone.

With respect and a blessing for great success in your aforementioned endeavor in particular, and in the general avodah of disseminating the wellsprings of Chassidus (until they reach) the outside.

6112

B"H, 2 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...It would be appropriate for them to consult among themselves whether there is room to print a booklet that would include the presentations of the students of the evening yeshivah at the time of the distribution of the certificates. Perhaps it could contain just the content of their presentations, or key points, naturally accompanied by the speeches (in full or in summary) of the Rabbis who were present, etc. For this would certainly bring encouragement to the students of the evening yeshivah and would serve as a catalyst for an increase in "jealousy of scribes" [which increases wisdom], etc.

On the other hand, one must take into account the reasoning not to provoke too much, and in the style of "not opening eyes" [i.e., not drawing undue attention]. By considering this all together, they will surely be able to weigh which arguments are decisive.

With blessings for success in his own study of Nigleh and Chassidus, and for an increase in the avodah of tefillah, for additional success in his influence upon others, to see good fruit in those he influences—true good, and along with it, also good that is visible and revealed.

With blessings for good tidings regarding the above.

## 6113

B"H, 2 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Yaakov Eliezer, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

Following a very long hiatus, your letter of 25 Nissan was received. Regarding what you wrote—that great and immense work is required with the yeshiva students here, and the reasons you provide for this:

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate to someone like yourself that this is the case regarding yeshiva students everywhere, even in the earlier generations. For this matter is called the "work of Hashem," and our Sages of blessed memory spoke at great length regarding the immense responsibility and the ceaseless engagement that is required in this. See Bava Basra 8b, the Laws of Torah Study in the Shulchan Aruch, the Laws of Torah Study by our Alter Rebbe, and many more.

Likewise, regarding what you wrote that there should be more frequent meetings of anash: this is certainly most correct, especially as explained in Kuntres Hecholotzu. However, for such matters to have any permanence, they must be brought about through an *is'arusa d'lesata* (an awakening from below), as is evident in practice, and not through directives from a higher place.

Regarding what you wrote about studying Maseches Sotah with the students, may they live: it is surprising. Since there are differing opinions on this, why should they involve themselves in this matter? Especially since, in classes such as those you describe, many other masechtos have been studied in yeshivos since time immemorial, as is well known. Why change this?

As for your reliance on the Kuntres Tnuas HaHaskalah, etc.—that text speaks regarding skipping [parts of the curriculum], and also about not rejecting it on principle; the matter is understood.

Regarding what you wrote about reciting Hallel before davening: I have not heard an explicit instruction on this. However, it is told by Chassidim that although our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, would extend their Shabbos davening for several hours after the congregation had finished, on Yom Tov they would arrange to finish Shacharis with the congregation and recite Hallel with them.

With blessings for success in the holy work of *hafatzas hamaayanos* through education suitable for this, and also in your personal matters.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned, and in this—that you perform your work in the *oholei Torah* without being impressed in the slightest by enticements against it, from whatever place they may openly come and with whatever open explanation they may come (for their true source is understood and simple). On the contrary, these enticements add to you courage, joy, and a good heart in the aforementioned holy work.

***

6113

A portion was printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 26, p. 412, and it was completed based on the secretariat’s copy.

R' Yaakov Eliezer: Herzog, Melbourne. Additional letters to him—above, Vol. 16, 5837, and in the references noted there.

## 614

B"H, 2 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Mrs. Chaya Sarah, may she live:

Blessings and peace!

I am surprised that for quite some time now, there have been no letters or news from you regarding your activities in general, and specifically concerning the Nshei U’Bnos Chabad of Chicago, may Hashem grant them life. Although I assume that everything is proceeding in order—and in such matters, "in order" according to Torah means not remaining at the same level, but rather continuing to grow, as our holy Torah instructs us: "We ascend in matters of holiness"—it is self-understood that I have asked your husband, the Rav, shlita, about this. However, I only know general information, that the meetings are taking place according to the established schedule, etc. I hope that at the next opportunity, you will write to me with more details. May Hashem help that we should only hear good news, and as I have said, that the Agudas Nshei U’Bnos Chabad in Chicago is carrying out its work to an ever-increasing degree, and, of course, that I hear good news regarding your personal matters as well.

Since it is summer, there are presumably certain changes in everyone’s private arrangements, which indirectly affects the work structure of Nshei U’Bnos Chabad (this does not mean, however, that summer should be a time of stagnation in the work). One simply needs to adjust the work to fit the summer circumstances, and not reduce the frequency of gatherings—and if possible, even increase them; for there is nothing that can stand before the will.

I hope that in your work as a teacher in chinuch, you also utilized the time of Pesach and the days of Sefirah with appropriate ideas and explanations for the students, and that you will do the same regarding Chag HaShavuos, Kabbalas HaTorah. Furthermore, in due time, you should work out a plan of interest for the students during the vacation period, for unfortunately, in most cases, vacation brings the students matters of "casting off the yoke," which are disguised under the cloak of vacation.

With blessings for success in your holy work to strengthen and spread Yiddishkeit, and for good news in all matters.

## 6,216

B"H, 3 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos, in which you write about the state of your livelihood, how it is affecting your health, and how you are preoccupied with it from early morning until late at night, etc.

In such a situation, you should look into finding a suitable partner. If the profits of the store in its current state are insufficient for partners, it is customary for the partner to bring in additional capital to expand the business, which in turn increases the profits. In this way, after some time, you will certainly be able to arrange the working hours in the store so that there is time for rest, and generally, for more comfortable work. It is understood that a primary condition for a partner is that he be a person who is pleasant to others, etc.

2) Regarding what you wrote about your spiritual state—that you are not religious—and the reasons you provide for this, even noting that you are not careful about putting on tefillin, stating in your letter that you have no time to put on tefillin because you are preoccupied, etc.—with even a slight amount of reflection, you will see how the content of your letter contradicts itself. For the putting on of tefillin is a mitzvah from the Creator and Guide of the world, Who promised great reward and abundant blessing for the fulfillment of this mitzvah. Yet, at the same time that you describe at the beginning of your letter how much you are in need of a blessing for additional success, you write subsequently that you do not fulfill the primary mitzvah whose reward is the blessings of the Creator of the world for what a person needs. Furthermore, you explain that you have no time to fulfill the mitzvah because you are preoccupied with your business. This is as if you were writing that you cannot engage in the matter of earning a livelihood because you are preoccupied with the fact that you have no livelihood.

Whatever the reasons may be for this (that until now you have not conducted yourself as a religious Jew), this does not justify your conduct from here on out in the slightest. It is simple that the consequences of such conduct—namely, the deficit in the blessings of Hashem and success in life—remain in place. Therefore, first and foremost, you must immediately begin to conduct yourself in accordance with the requirements of our Torah, the Torah of life, in your daily life, both you and your wife, may she live and be well. Be strong in your bitachon in the Creator and Guide of the world, in accordance with what He says in His Torah: "If you walk in My statutes and observe My mitzvos, etc., I will provide your rains, etc."—with all the blessings enumerated in the parsha. Based on what was stated above, it is understood that immediately, you must begin putting on tefillin every weekday. It is understood that the tefillin must be checked to ensure they are kosher.

Awaiting good news regarding all of the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 6117

B.H., 3 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated communal worker, R' Dovber, may he live.

Shalom u’vracha,

In response to your letter of the 19th of Nissan:

It is surprising that you do not write regarding the utilization of the days of the Pesach holiday for strengthening the communal matters in which you are involved, and specifically their central and inner point: the dissemination of the wellsprings until they reach the "outside." My hope is strong that these days of *ratzon* were utilized for all of this, in accordance with what is explained regarding the concept of "festivals for joy"—that joy breaks through boundaries—whereby activities in this area are easier and more successful, and this is understood...

Regarding your telegram and its contents, as well as the *pidyon nefesh* that will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and the good tidings regarding the hope for full-day study—may it be the will [of Hashem] that the hope of our Rebbes, the *Nesi'im*, be fulfilled in these students as well: that they be Chassidim, G-d-fearing, and scholars.

With blessings for good tidings in all communal and personal matters.

P.S.

Regarding the expression mentioned above—a Chossid, G-d-fearing, and a scholar—which we have heard on several occasions, one must explain the precision in the order of these terms. First and foremost must be the matter of Chassidus, as explained by the Alter Rebbe regarding its essence: that one nullifies oneself for the sake of another, to the point of not fearing harm to oneself for the sake of the other’s benefit (the proof cited by the Alter Rebbe from the statement of our Sages, "the pious one [Chossid] burns it" [Niddah 17a and Tosafos, s.v. *shorfah*], is well known). The diminution of one’s own *yeshus* (selfhood) and existence provides a place for *yiras shamayim* (fear of Heaven), as our Sages stated: "Any person who has arrogance, the Holy One, blessed be He, says: 'He and I cannot dwell in the world'" (Sotah 5a).

See also the *sicha* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of 19 Kislev 5693, section 3, [quoting] the teachings of the Alter Rebbe: that when a person’s heart is naturally haughty, and he does not engage in Chassidus to refine his character traits, etc., even the *Shechinah* is not considered important to him, etc. It is obvious that in such a state there is no room for the fear of the *Shechinah*. When this fear exists—at the very least, *yirah tata'ah* (lower-level fear)—then there is also *chochma* (wisdom), for if there is no fear, there is no wisdom; on the contrary, when one innovates new insights [without fear], he only adds foolishness (see there in the teachings of the Alter Rebbe, unlike the manner and order mentioned above). Only then does one become a *lamdan* (scholar).

[This is written] with an additional *nun* (the letter *nun* at the end of the word *lamdan*), which indicates that one is accustomed to this (see Bava Metzia 33a, beginning of the page, and *Likutei Torah*, Bamidbar 21a, Devarim 20b, regarding the concept of the final *nun* according to Chassidus), in the study of Torah that is equivalent to all [other mitzvos], the study that leads to actual deed, for the deed is the essential thing.

## 6221

6221

B.H., 4 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in Torah study, etc., Rabbi Sh. Y. [Zevin], may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the beginning of the month of Iyar and the one preceding it...

About two weeks ago, I sent via registered mail the index—*Derchei HaKabbalah*—to the writings of the Arizal, in accordance with your instruction. You will surely confirm its receipt.

I am certain that you have read with the necessary attention the speech of Professor Segal. It is surprising that no one mentions anything regarding this. Yet this is the very point and the litmus test of these viewpoints, against which our Nasi and the Gedolei Yisrael fought—against the winds that were blowing in the Jewish street at that time, etc. If we had been worthy, these things should have been stated by those who serve in holiness in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, the leaders of the parties who march under the banner of religion, and all the more so by the Rabbis. And the greater the title of the Rabbi, the greater should have been his outcry, his scream, and his sigh. Since we were not worthy, all those mentioned above do not cease from reciting Hallel, songs, and praises, and they have already explicitly ruled that the Geulah has already begun, even though all those who have ruled this way know what is brought in the Rambam as a halachic ruling regarding the Geulah and its nature. Using the well-known language of prophecy, they explain how there is peace for Judaism, for Torah and its mitzvos, and that there will be peace in the future as well, and that the situation is improving and will rise from moment to moment, etc., etc. And the one who is not ashamed to speak the truth is specifically one of those whose books regarding the holy writings have content that is known and publicized, and the war against Hashem and His Torah—at least against His Torah—has touched his heart. If only the Rabbis and the religious parties would restrain themselves from coming out against him and denying his words in the same manner and with the same "proofs" with which they denied all those who said things similar to the above, even if not with his sharpness, etc. And as I wrote regarding certain matters—the panic regarding this is not so much about the conduct that is the opposite of the logic of holiness and common sense, but rather that these religious individuals do not pay attention to the fact that there is room here for doubt and discussion, and that one ought to write the exact opposite of what they are saying and printing.

It is interesting to know: surely the aforementioned individual "receives funds from the State," and not only that, but he serves in a position connected to the field of education—meaning that his influence is in a manner that is ever-increasing upon his students and the students of his students. Have they come out against him from the offices officially, with a blast of trumpets, and with all those titles they used regarding those who sit in prison for these matters, who were not raised on the knees of "Chachmas Yisrael" in the land of Ashkenaz, and in exchange for the title "Professor," they bear the title of Rabbi, Dayan, Shochet, teacher, or even a Yeshiva *avreich* in Meah Shearim? It is characteristic that there is a weekly publication here that receives assistance from the **Torah** department of the Jewish Agency, and it had no choice but to print at least a summary of the Professor's speech. And at the very least, they printed it on the back pages, and in that same issue—but in a more respectable place and at greater length—there appeared a defense article, which is completely baseless!

You write at the end of your letter that there was distress, etc.—I do not have the article you are writing about at hand. But remembering what I have said and spoken regarding the aforementioned subject, it is as I said—it is far from the sharpness of the aforementioned speech.

It seems that in such cases, I have already written that not only am I interested in knowing the details when you write that there was distress and anguish, but as I mentioned, I added even then that there is generally no benefit in hiding things, because there are "lovers and friends" who report on such matters, only they distort the facts and usually exaggerate as well. You will surely fill me in on the aforementioned at the next opportunity.

With blessings for good tidings in good health.

**M. Schneerson**

622

622

B”H, 5 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Mr. Moshe Yaari
Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the second of Iyar, and I was pleased to read of your joy and the joy of your family—may they live and be well—upon your son Yosef—may he live and be well—reaching the age of mitzvos.

May it be the will of Hashem that he take upon himself the yoke of Torah and the yoke of mitzvos, with the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven as the foundation for this.

As our Sages instruct us regarding this, the order mentioned is essential for the matter to endure. As the Mishnah states, one must first accept the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven, and only afterwards accept the yoke of mitzvos.

The language of the Mishnah is extremely precise, and we learn from this that the fulfillment of a mitzvah must be through a sense of "yoke." Just as the initial acceptance of the Torah was specifically through the precedence of "we will do" over "we will hear," even then, one is not yet guaranteed in the matter until one first precedes it with the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven—that is to say:

A general surrender and dedication, like a servant who accepts the yoke of the King with simplicity and total bitul. Only then is there endurance for the acceptance of the yoke in every specific matter and every individual mitzvah.

And since you have merited that Divine Providence has placed you in a position where you influence the education of youth, and the fate of tens and hundreds of them is in your hands to guide them toward the path of good and righteousness—which is the path of the King, the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, as He has taught us in our Torah, the Torah of truth and the Torah of life—then according to the measure of the Holy One, Blessed be He, which is "measure for measure" but many times over, may your good reward be paid in full to experience an abundance of true nachas—that is, traditional Jewish nachas—together with your wife and your entire family—may they live and be well.

With respect and with blessings of mazal tov for the joyous occasion of the Bar Mitzvah, and with blessings for success in your work—holy work—guiding the sons and daughters of Israel on a path that brings their hearts closer to our Father in Heaven, and in their daily lives as well—I await good tidings.

## 6,223

6,223

B"H, 5 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, I write briefly to note that you are drawing closer to your spiritual rest and inheritance.

May it be Hashem’s will that you gain further strength in this, to go from strength to strength. Our holy Torah has promised us that one who comes to purify himself is assisted. Since "rest and inheritance" refers to the concept of the Beis Hamikdash—as our Sages of blessed memory have explained—the essence of the Beis Hamikdash is, in its literal sense, a holy house dedicated to the service of the Creator of the world. This means that even within the world and its affairs, one draws down from His holiness.

May it be His will that you work, both regarding yourself and regarding others, in a manner that is permeated with yiras shamayim, ahavas Hashem, and chassidishe warmth, so as to illuminate them with the "candle of a mitzvah and the light of Torah," and the "light of the Torah"—which is the pnimiyus haTorah.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6224

B"H, 5 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 23 Nissan. Regarding what you write concerning the matter of the committee, etc., the demand of our Rebbeim, the Nesi'im—and specifically of the Mitteler Rebbe—is well known: one must have at least one person with whom to consult. In such a case, there are two *nefesh habehamis* [animal souls] against one *nefesh habehamis*, and one will certainly arrive at a good and correct decision. This is even more understandable in a matter that concerns the public; one must cease and avoid relying solely upon oneself.

I was pleased to read in your letter, albeit very briefly, about the activities of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad. May it be His will that this continues in a manner of *mosif v'holech* [increasing and progressing], both within one's own *daled amos* and regarding others. This is especially true as we find ourselves between *Zeman Cheiruseinu*—freedom from Egypt *d'le'umas zeh* [the negative side] and even from the Egypt *d'kedushah* [of holiness]—and the time of *Matan Torah*. As the precision of the word **Matan** [giving] implies, it is given as a gift; one only needs to make the preparation through *u'sefartem lachem* [and you shall count for yourselves]. As is well known, the interpretation of the Alter Rebbe [...] *u'sefartem lachem* means to make [it] luminous.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6225

B"H, 7 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
R' Naftali, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, end of Chapter 4, regarding the letters *Man-Tza-Pach*, etc., and the *Butzina D'Kardunisa*—for the explanation according to Chassidus, see the *Siddur*, *Maamar* entitled *Adonai Sefatai* **(for Rosh Hashanah)**. [See also] *Torah Or*, *Miketz* (39a), and in the additions there at the end of *Parshas Shemos*.

Regarding what you wrote in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 6 (107b), that the *Hei Tata'ah* in its written form, etc., indicates, etc., the four directions—

The intention is not that the written form [itself] indicates the four directions (for if so, it would also have to indicate "above" and "below," which he mentions prior to that).

Rather, he is specifying here which type of expansion of the *Hei Tata'ah* is being discussed. That is to say, the *Hei* in its written form (length and width) indicates expansion. However, in the *Hei Ila'ah*, this is an expansion of the hidden intellect which terminates in the heart; whereas in the *Hei Tata'ah*, it is an expansion in speech, from which it is drawn down and expands to "above and below" and the "four directions."

#### ***6225***

**R' Naftali:** Gluskin, Ramat HaSharon. Another letter to him appears above, Vol. 15, 5399.

6228

6228

B"H, 8 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Nissan:

At a time of favor, I will mention all of you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever each of you is in need of.

You should have your tefillin checked, as well as the mezuzos in your home, to ensure that they are all kosher according to the law.

Regarding what you wrote concerning your wife, may she live and be well, that since the birth of your first child, may he live and be well, you have not yet been blessed with more children:

In general, one must be strong in bitachon in the Creator of the world, who is the essence of good, that He will fulfill your heart’s desire with more children.

However, it is highly likely that you need to increase your care and precision regarding the laws and customs of taharas hamishpacha and tzniyus. Although I hope that the fundamentals are being observed, in such a critically important matter, one must observe them properly according to the instructions of our Toras Chaim. Once you do so, be strong in bitachon in the Giver of the Torah and the mitzvos, that He will fulfill the requests of your hearts for good in the near future.

Regarding what you wrote about the difficulties in parnassah, the instruction of our holy Torah is well known: "Salt your wealth by diminishing it"—meaning, to increase in tzedakah, and to distribute that tzedakah in smaller, more frequent amounts. Among the auspicious times for this is every weekday morning before davening.

In a broader sense, one must accept both of these matters as a test, according to the expression of the verse, "For Hashem your G-d is testing you to know whether you love Him." When it is seen from Above that one is strong in bitachon in Hashem Yisbarach and is increasing in matters of Torah and mitzvos in general—and in the aforementioned matters in particular—the test is nullified from Above, and one is granted blessing, salvation, and success.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all of the above.

P.S.

Surely you are keeping up with the three daily shiurim of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, which, as we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, are appropriate for every soul and a segulah for many matters.

## 629

B"H, 8 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...May it be the will of Hashem that, since we are currently in the days of Sefirah—and as is explained in Chassidus, we do not count in ordinal numbers, "first day," "second day," but rather "one day," "two days," meaning that the avodah of yesterday remains in its entirety, and additional avodah is simply added upon the matters of the first day, etc.—that each and every one of us be stirred to action. And when we say "each of us," we truly mean ourselves, not just the other person. This demand must be in the manner of "a sickle to the standing grain," as the language of Likutei Torah (Bamidbar 15:4) states: "The natural middos are strong in the body by their nature and birth, and one must subdue and humble them in the aspect of iskafya and is'hapcha, and swing a sickle upon them to cut them down, to consume them, and to transform them literally into ayin, etc., so that they become nullified and included within the supernal middos," see there. These matters are discussed in the maamar beginning with the subject of the giving of the Torah, the Aseres HaDibros, and those which we heard from the mouth of the Gevurah, see there. 

However, our inheritance is beautiful, for now this avodah is easier than it was the first time—similar to what is explained regarding the superiority of the matzah of "now," before chatzos—after Matan Torah—compared to the matzah of "before chatzos" that was before Matan Torah. From this, one can also understand the difference before the revelation of the teachings of Chassidus and after the revelation of this Torah, regarding the refinement and purification of the middos through the paths of Chassidus...

## 6230

6230

B"H, 8 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

New York Women’s Division
For the Bais Rivkah Schools

Even in our generation, they should know their merit and responsibility: that today, too, they can be the ones to bring about a Geulah for Klal Yisrael through their contribution to raising upright Jewish children—both their own and others—and by helping the mosdos that are engaged in chinuch al taharas hakodesh.

And it is self-understood that Hashem Yisbarach rewards this from His full hand, granting all those who take part in this, they and their families, the threefold blessing of children, life, and ample sustenance.

With blessings for success.

## 6,231

B"H, 8 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 1 Iyar, in which you write regarding two worthy proposals—one of which you feel a greater inclination of the heart toward, while regarding the second, you were told that a *goral* (lot) was cast, and the *goral* indicated the second proposal.

Generally, in matters of *shidduchim*, when both proposals involve a *yarei shamayim*, there is room for the decision to be based on the inclination of the heart—as it is written, "And we shall ask her [the maiden's] opinion." I have not heard of casting lots in such matters.

However, since it appears from your letter that your father, *shichye*, leans toward the second proposal, you should clarify his reasons and rationale for this, and in accordance with that clarification, deliberate once more regarding both proposals.

And since it is sometimes difficult to decide on a matter that affects one's life so profoundly, it is advisable that you consult with those who are familiar with the details of the situation.

May it be the will of the Creator of the world and its Guide, who oversees each and every one with *hashgacha pratis*, to lead you on the path that is good for you.

## 6132

6132

B”H, 9 Iyar, 5718

Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 26 Nissan, in which you write regarding the situation in your camp concerning registration and the upcoming school term, and in particular regarding the possibility of opening a Chabad school there...

In general, you are surely aware of the Chabad approach: our conduct is not guided by fear. On the other hand, it is not our role to squander strength and energy on battles with politicians of any faction whatsoever, at a time when these very energies should be utilized for essential matters that are directly incumbent upon us. It is obvious that even in this matter, the principle of "follow the majority" applies—that is, when anash are faced with the choice of engaging in a certain location where, according to your assessment, their work will proceed without excessive interference and the number of children will be double or more, versus choosing a second location where the number of children will be a fraction of that and even that will be achieved through struggle—it is surely your opinion as well that they should occupy themselves with the first location.

Furthermore, since even the head of a small irrigation ditch is appointed from Heaven, and all the more so a Rav and a teacher of Torah in Israel, and the Ribono shel Olam does not deal unjustly with His creatures, it is certain that the strengths and possibilities to fulfill one’s true role were granted in advance. That is, to instill fear of Hashem and love of Hashem, Torah study with yiras shamayim, and the performance of mitzvos with hiddur in all the people of the place. Our Sages of blessed memory related (Sanhedrin 37a) in our Torah—Torah of life—that even the ruffians in the neighborhood of Rebbe Zeira were considered Rebbe Zeira’s responsibility. And as is known, the saying of our Alter Rebbe regarding the name *mara d’asra* (master of the place), that its content is literally as it sounds: he is the "baal habayis" (master of the house) over all matters of the place.

Regarding your request at the end of your letter—and everything follows the conclusion—to mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention you. My hope is strong that from the mention will come action—actual, practical deeds regarding your community, and certainly regarding yourself, to increase and ascend from strength to strength in the levels of "becoming a Chassid." I mean, to instill the *maor* (light-source) of Chassidus—the light and vitality within it—into all matters of Torah and mitzvos, and in the conduct of "in all your ways know Him." The totality of this consists of the three lines: *mili d’nezikin* (the matters of "turn from evil"), *mili d’avos* (the middle line—Torah study, for "from the days of our forefathers, the yeshiva has never ceased from them"; furthermore, Torah study is the only mitzvah that a father is obligated by Torah law to educate his son in—see the Laws of Torah Study by the Alter Rebbe, beginning of Chapter 1, and in the *Piskei Dinim* of the Tzemach Tzedek on the Rambam’s Laws of Torah Study), and *mili d’berachos* (and *hemshechos*—the line of "do good," the drawing down of light and abundance into the worlds and also upon one’s own soul; see *Iggeres HaKodesh*, beginning of Chapter 1).

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and in the central point: to make your place a *dirah lo yisbarach* (a dwelling place for Him, blessed be He). As the teachings of Chassidus explain, just as in an earthly kingdom the king is found in his palace with his entire essence, being, and concerns, so too is it in the "dwelling place" that the Ribono shel Olam, King of the world, desired to have in the lower realms.

With respect and esteem,

## 6,233

B"H, 9 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, Moreinu HaRav Yosef Chaim Meir, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter of Monday, along with the enclosure.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you and your wife, may she live, at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

May it be G-d’s will that for many more years you continue to participate in farbrengens where we speak words of inspiration regarding Torah and mitzvos, imbued with the light and vitality of Chassidus, and that you also influence your surroundings in this direction; for there is nothing that can stand before the will.

In your letter, you also mention the matter of the "ten gold coins" among the offerings of the Nesi'im. As is known from our Sages (Zohar Vol. III, 11b; see also Kuntres U'Maayan, beginning of section 16), the repetition of "ten, ten" signifies that the Ten Commandments must be directed toward—and one must draw them down into—the Ten Utterances through which the world was created, and through this, into the world itself and its affairs. This obligation is constant, especially for those who have been gifted with the power to influence their surroundings, just as our Sages have made known that the Holy One, blessed be He, desired to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds (see also Tanya, Chapter 36).

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6,234

B"H, 9 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Isser, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 5 Iyar, in which you ask regarding the Bar Mitzvah of your son, Menachem Mendel, may he live, which falls on Erev Rosh Hashanah—specifically, when he should begin wearing tefillin, etc.

It is surprising that this question is being asked, given that the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (printed in *Hayom Yom*, 2 Menachem Av), has already been publicized. It is an instruction for the many: one begins wearing tefillin two months before the Bar Mitzvah—initially without a *bracha*, and after several weeks, with a *bracha*.

Regarding your question as to whether there is room to hold the *seudas mitzvah* on Motzaei Shabbos—this is simple: since the entry into the age of *mitzvos* occurs at the very first moment after the completion of thirteen years, this is also one of the reasons for the beginning of *Shas* with "From when do we recite the Shema in the evening"—the first *mitzvah* that a Jewish man becomes obligated in at the time he becomes an adult (*adam*).

Regarding the *aliyah* to the Torah: the *sicha* of 25 Shevat 5696 is well known, regarding the virtue of an *aliyah* to the Torah at Mincha on Shabbos. However, it is obvious that one should not, G-d forbid, delay the *aliyah* until the Shabbos following the Bar Mitzvah. He should have an *aliyah* on Rosh Hashanah. Since it is proven from the aforementioned instruction that the custom of the world to have the Bar Mitzvah boy receive *Maftir* is not necessarily a binding custom (and there is room to say that in every place they act according to this, because they do not rely on the parents—as to whether the *aliyah* is exactly on time or beforehand—and therefore they instituted an *aliyah* to *Maftir*, but as mentioned, this custom is not universally accepted), and it seems that in every place the *Maftir* of Rosh Hashanah belongs to the Rabbi or similar, there is no reason to change this. Rather, based on what was said regarding this matter, and similarly for everyone, he should also have an *aliyah* at the Mincha of the following Shabbos.

With blessings for good tidings.

***

**R' Isser:** Klovgant, Melbourne. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 5, 1,221, and in the references in the notes there.

**Two months:** See also above, Vol. 16, letter 6,182b, and in the references in the notes there.

## 6,236

6,236

B"H, 10 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, answering my inquiry regarding a shidduch, in which you list the reasons that have held you back from this until now.

It is understood that since our Torah is a Torah of life, it has commanded us that "it is not good for man to be alone," and "in the evening do not withhold your hand," and the halachah is also ruled in Shulchan Aruch (Even HaEzer, at the beginning), then certainly these reasons can be addressed and safeguarded against. Indeed, we have seen tangibly in the recent past that there were many who were in a similar situation, yet they became engaged, married, are satisfied, and are living happy lives. Regarding what you wrote—that perhaps this will cause distance from your children, sheyichyu—I am very doubtful whether there is any room for this concern; on the contrary, it is more likely that this is also their desire. As for your question regarding the three regalim, once you begin to show interest in suggestions, it takes time until one finds [a match] and discusses the details, etc., and in the meantime, the three regalim will pass—which would not be the case if you do not even begin to show interest.

Regarding what you wrote about whether to distribute your property, etc.—while there is room for this distinction, that you wish to give to tzedakah specifically through your own hand, as our Torah states, "a mitzvah is better performed by oneself than by one's agent," and see also the sicha of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, based on the saying "you shall see your world in your lifetime"—nevertheless, regarding your desire to distribute now what is appropriate to bequeath after a long life and years, this reasoning does not seem correct to me. We see in our times that this conduct has led to undesirable results. May Hashem, who sustains and provides for all with goodness, grace, kindness, and mercy, fulfill the needs of all those you wish to include in the distribution in a good way, and may you use your assets for matters of Torah and mitzvos for long, good days and years...

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

#### ***6,236***

**Note:** See Igros Kodesh of the Rebbe Rayatz, Vol. 8, letters 2,550 and 2,335.

## 6,237

[10 Iyar 5718]

...It is understood, and indeed simple, that since he has merited that Divine Providence has placed him in a beautiful portion—work in proper chinuch, in the purity of holiness, which draws the hearts of the students to our Father in Heaven—this certainly clarifies, refines, and elevates the student and the one being educated from level to level. Furthermore, it adds to the success of the educator and teacher himself. Just as with all of a person’s affairs—for it is said regarding every person, "In all your ways know Him"—this, too, must be done with joy and a glad heart. ## 6238

B"H, 11 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

It has been some time since I received a letter from you, although I inquire indirectly and receive news about you from your friends. Surely you will also write yourself regarding what is happening with you for the good.

In particular, regarding what I mentioned above—that sometimes the lack of writing stems from a lack of completeness in the matter of *simcha* and *tuv levav* (joy and goodness of heart) that should be present throughout a person’s entire life. As we have discussed many times, the command "Know Him in all your ways" applies to all twenty-four hours of the day. Consequently, the words of the Rambam at the end of *Hilchos Lulav*—that matters must be performed out of *simcha*—apply to all twenty-four hours of the day. And this is understood.

Especially now, as we find ourselves between the days of Pesach, the time of our freedom, and Shavuos, the receiving of the Torah with *simcha*, the aforementioned command applies even more so. And even though people sometimes justify their lack of complete *simcha* with various reasons—including some that have a basis not only in ordinary intellect but even in the intellect of *kedushah*—the fact remains that through a lack of *simcha*, nothing is accomplished and nothing is rectified. This is in contrast to the opposite approach. As is known from the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, a soldier going out to war begins his departure with a song (a march) of victory; this itself brings the victory closer and magnifies it. After all, each one of us is not alone, and the help of the *Ribono shel Olam* is with him. And "he who comes to purify is assisted"—in the plural, meaning many assist him.

My hope is that among all your affairs, you are also occupied with matters of *shidduchim*, naturally in an appropriate manner—that is, through friends acting as intermediaries—and that you are particular about the essentials but do not pay attention to the trivialities of the trivial. In such a manner of choosing, sometimes **most closely**, the trivial matters also fall into place. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success to bring good news soon regarding all of the above.

With blessings for a good arrangement, out of *simcha* and *tuv levav*.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

6,239

B"H, 11 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval, your letter from Motzaei Shabbos arrived, in which you write about the situation in your business and are contemplating what the final outcome for the year will look like.

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate on the matter of *midas habitachon* (the attribute of trust). The intention is not merely to be satisfied with studying it in *sefarim*, but rather it is meant **b’poel mamash** (in actual practice): when a moment arrives that is not as one would wish, one should be strong in *bitachon* that it is nothing more than a passing phase. As the verse says, "For Hashem your G-d is testing you." When the Ribono shel Olam sees that one has withstood the *nision* (test), one then sees even with physical eyes that it was nothing more than a *nision*—that is, a matter of a concealment that has no substance. Among the *eitzos* (pieces of advice) to hasten the improvement of your *parnassah* is to increase in matters of *tzedakah*. You should also ensure that your wife, *tichyeh*, adds to the money she gives for *tzedakah*, in addition to the fact that she surely maintains the good custom of *bnos Yisrael hakesheiros* (virtuous daughters of Israel) to give to *tzedakah* each time before lighting candles on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

***

Mrs. ... *tichyeh*,

Greetings and blessings!

Your husband, *shichyeh*, writes to me that, praised be the Hashem Yisbarach, you are already in the final stages of your eighth month. I wish to bless you that everything should go properly and easily, and that you should have a healthy, living child in its proper time, easily and well.

You surely know, and indeed act accordingly, to follow the custom of *bnos Yisrael hakesheiros* to give to *tzedakah* each time before lighting candles. In connection with your current state, and also regarding the business, the advice of our Sages, *zichronam livrachah*, is to increase in matters of *tzedakah* in general, and specifically before lighting candles. Hashem Yisbarach has promised that through this, not only will there be no lack in the coffers, but there will even be an increase.

With blessings for good news regarding all the above.

P.S.

Regarding what you write about speaking with the landlord to partition the second floor and lower the rent: if this can be done **easily**, you may do so. However, if it requires excessive *hishtadlus* (effort) and toil, it is not worth the trouble. The final outcome for this year will be a good one, and what is even more important—that the *parnassah* should be used for healthy, happy things.

## 6240

6240

B"H, 11 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Mr. Menachem Shmuel, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 4 Iyar, in which you ask:

Is it true what is said, that the Alter Rebbe’s intention in his introduction to Tanya, when he writes "from books and from authors" (*mipi sefarim umipi sofrim*), refers to the books of the Maharal of Prague?

This is how Chassidim explain it when studying the Tanya, based on what they have received from the elder Chassidim from generation to generation. However, I have not heard this from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, even though the tradition of Chassidim is generally authoritative.

It is worth noting that the phrase "from books and from authors" is also cited in the introduction to Part II of the Tanya, known as *Chinuch Katan*, and likewise in the text of the Tanya’s title page. I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that the words "Sefer Likutei Amarim... in a long and short way, with the help of Hashem," are the Alter Rebbe’s own phrasing, and [it appears] in *Pnei Moshe* (in reverse order).

Incidentally, the aforementioned phrase is also found in *Avodas HaKodesh* by R. Meir ibn Gabbai, Part IV, Chapter 1, and in the *Shelah* on several occasions* [It is found in one Chassidic manuscript: See Yerushalmi, Yevamos, Chapter 4, Halacha 11, "the master of the teachings, the master of the study," see there].

Regarding what you wrote about strengthening oneself in Chassidus, see the writings of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding what is discussed extensively on this matter, and in particular the *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus* and *Kuntres Toras HaChassidus*. The essence of this strengthening is in accordance with the statement of the Mishnah that "the deed is the essential thing." In this context, the intention is to study thoroughly and in actual practice, so that not a day passes without studying this Torah, and on Shabbos, with an addition.

Surely you are aware of the three daily portions—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and keep them, as we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that they are appropriate for every soul and are a *segulah* for many matters.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6141

6141

B"H, 12 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 7 Iyar, and in accordance with your request, this reply is being sent without waiting for its turn.

In it, you write regarding the proposal that you travel to Vienna in order to arrange the transfer of the remains of your mother-in-law’s grandfather, may she live and be well, to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

It is understood that there is a *hiddur* (a commendable enhancement) in having a family member accompany the casket from there to Eretz Yisrael. However, one must also take into account the expenses involved in such an undertaking. It is well known that there are several *yirei Hashem* (G-d-fearing individuals) in Vienna upon whom one can rely for matters such as these. Furthermore, on the airplane that will transport the casket from there to Eretz Yisrael, there will certainly be several reliable Jewish individuals traveling. Moreover, it will surely be transported without transfers from one plane to another—meaning that once the casket is loaded onto the plane, it will remain there until its arrival in Lod, where one of the family members will meet it.

In your letter, you mention the transport of the casket to Eretz Yisrael from Vienna by ship. This, of course, implies either an Israeli ship, where the journey would take place only on weekdays, or a non-Israeli ship.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6243
