With respect and blessings for success.

The verse states: "I am a companion to all who fear You..." and the Shelah (66a) explains: "Wherever a person sees a *chaburah kedoshah*, he should join them, such as a group... who are acquiring a *mitzvah*..." Enclosed is a check—my participation in the campaign for the aforementioned perfect construction.

## 6,244

B"H, 14 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received information regarding your person and the manner of your daily life. It is understandable that I am distressed if these reports are accurate—my intent being that I was told you are increasing in fasts, and furthermore, that even though your family members (may they live and be well) are requesting and pleading with you to consult a doctor regarding your health, you are not paying heed to their words, are not fulfilling the doctor’s instructions, and are not even willing to seek a doctor’s advice.

Surely it is superfluous to elaborate on the commandment we have been commanded, "And you shall guard yourselves very carefully," or to explain the words of the great teacher, the Rambam, in his book *Yad HaChazakah*, *Hilchos De'os*, that it is impossible for one to understand and contemplate wisdom while hungry or ill, etc. (for one’s body must be whole in order to serve Hashem; see there, end of chapter 3 and beginning of chapter 4). Regarding matters of health, the Torah has granted permission to the physician to heal, as is codified in several laws in *Shulchan Aruch*, *Hilchos Shabbos* and *Hilchos Yom Kippur*, etc. Especially concerning fasts, the ruling of our Alter Rebbe—the authority on the hidden aspects of Torah and the *Shulchan Aruch*—the authority on the revealed aspects of Torah—is well known: that in these generations, through an excess of fasts, one can come to illness or infirmity, *chas v'shalom*. Therefore, it is forbidden to increase in fasts; see the startling words in his *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, chapter 3.

It is my hope that these few lines, small in quantity, will suffice for you to change your conduct as is necessary, to visit a doctor, and to fulfill the doctor’s instructions in every detail. May the Ribono shel Olam strengthen your health, and may you be able to share good news regarding everything concerning you.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6246

B"H, 15 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Following your long silence, your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh was received. In response:

1) It is correct that in recent years, Anash have adopted the custom of reciting the maamar "Lecha Dodi" at weddings, which is printed in the *Kuntres Drushei Chassunah*, Chapter 9. This is based on the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, at that time (printed in several copies in the aforementioned Kuntres), that this maamar encompasses the teachings of our Rebbes, the Nesi’im, starting from the Alter Rebbe. As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, said then, this serves as an invitation for them to participate in the wedding.

From this, it is also understood that there is no room at all to shorten the maamar or to recite only a portion of it. This is especially true since the maamar does not delineate which part belongs to which Nasi; if one shortens it or recites only a part, it is unknown what is being omitted, and in any case, it is clear that something is missing.

Regarding places where the custom is to interrupt the maamar in the middle, it has already been stated that this custom should be abolished, as it is contrary to the honor of the Torah. Even though some offer a justification—so as not to embarrass those who do not have [the ability to recite the whole thing]—there was already an incident in Poland where my father-in-law, the Rebbe, instructed that in a place where they insist on maintaining the custom, the entire maamar should be recited first, and only afterwards should they begin again and then interrupt it.

Surely you will begin in good time to study the necessary halachos as preparation for married life, and for several reasons that are understood, this study should be done in *chavrusa*.

I was pleased to read in your letter about the good impression that your bride, may she live and be well, has made on all who see her. Our Sages have taught: "Anyone in whom the spirit of his fellow creatures takes pleasure, the spirit of the Omnipresent takes pleasure in him."

With blessings for good tidings.

P.S.
Surely you are keeping up with the known *Chitas* lessons, in addition to your fixed daily study of *Nigleh* and *Chassidus*, especially during these months as preparation for building a home—a home that will endure forever—where the more one increases the above, the more praiseworthy it is.

**There was already an incident:** See also above, letter 6189, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 6157

B”H, 15 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished Rabbi Menachem, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter of Monday, in which you write:

1) According to reports, one of the synagogues in your area is currently constructing a new building. It is rumored that they intend to include in the building plans a design without a *mechitzah*, allowing for mixed seating. You ask whether you should fight this, or refrain from doing anything, as some say that by fighting, the situation might only worsen.

Now, based on what you mentioned—that there is not yet a final decision (that they must sit in a mixed fashion)—it is clear that one cannot sit idly by. However, in such matters, our Sages have already said, "Be clever in fear [of Heaven]." Since the goal is for them to build a *mechitzah*, success is often achieved not by allowing the issue to enter the realm of a "fight," but rather through informal advocacy and conversation with those who have influence over the course of events. This must be done with caution, so as not to provoke in them a sense of "victory," which has caused many casualties. It is understood that the decision regarding the appropriate approach for the aforementioned synagogue depends on the temperament of those leading the synagogue and your relationship with them, as well as with those who can speak to their hearts so that they build the synagogue according to the will of the Creator, may He be blessed.

It is truly ridiculous, and contrary to simple logic, to pray and ask **from Whom** one is requesting something, while simultaneously acting in a way that is the opposite of the will of the One from whom you are requesting the favor and the fulfillment of your desire. This is all the more so—*kal v'chomer*—with a mortal being of flesh and blood: to present a request before him while adding, in the course of the conversation, "I am acting in opposition to your will, even in your own home, and despite all this, I am asking you to fulfill my request!" Anyone who acts in such a manner would be considered insane.

Regarding what you wrote—that some say the *mechitzah* is merely a custom—you surely know that articles and a booklet explaining the matter of the *mechitzah* and the prohibition have already been published, including in English. You can obtain them through the central rabbinical organizations in New York.

2) Regarding what you wrote about your state of health, the ailment you had in the past, and the doctor’s instruction that you must be in control of your spirit and free yourself from worries, mental tension, etc.

The well-known advice for the absence of worry is the *middah* of *bitachon*. The elaboration on how one explains the concept of *bitachon* to himself is explained in many places, including in the *Sefer Chovos HaLevavos*, *Shaar HaBitachon*. In truth, this is a direct result of the **foundations** of the faith of the Jewish people, for all are "believers, the children of believers." The faith is that the Holy One, blessed be He, oversees each and every person with *hashgachah pratis*, and that the Holy One, blessed be He, is the essence of good. In the words of our Sages, "Everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good." If so, what room is left for worry? It is only when one forgets the **essentials** of faith that worry can arise.

It should be noted that according to the above, this applies to matters that are in the hands of Heaven. According to the words of our Sages, "Everything is in the hands of Heaven, **except for the fear of Heaven.**" Therefore, in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, a person must worry about how to improve his ways to be suited to the purpose of his creation, as the *Mishnah* states: "I was created to serve my Maker."

It is my hope, even though you did not mention it, that you have fixed times for study in both the revealed Torah and in the study of *Chassidus*, and that you are increasing this from time to time, for we have been commanded to "ascend in holiness."

With blessings for good news regarding all the above.

P.S.
The secretary who writes in English is not currently in the city, which is why this response is in the Holy Tongue, but you may continue to write in English.

## 6248

B"H, 15 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—which took longer than usual to reach me—in which you write that you have moved to a new shop and, for the time being, are not seeing success in your livelihood, and that your profession is a tailor.

You are surely aware of the matter of separating *maaser* from one’s earnings. Especially when one is struggling with *parnassah*, one should increase *tzedakah*, but in any case, no less than *maaser*. It is best to distribute the *tzedakah* in several installments, and a propitious time for this is every weekday before morning *davening*. Furthermore, it is appropriate to have your *tefillin* checked. You should also ask a Rav whether your shop requires a *mezuzah*; if it does, you should affix a kosher *mezuzah* in the proper manner. If the shop does not require a *mezuzah*, then at the very least, there should be a *Siddur* and *Tehillim* present in your shop.

May it be the will of the Creator of the world and its Guide that He expand your *parnassah*, and that you increase your study of the holy Torah—the *Tiferes Bachurim*—during your spare time. May you also influence your friends to do the same, and the merit of the many will assist you.

With blessings for good news,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 6,249

B"H, 16 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 5 Iyar, in which you write that you have been accepted to Tzeirei Chabad and occasionally study Chassidus and listen to sichos.

It is obvious that this is not the way to study the holy Torah—in any of its parts—that the study should be "occasional" (see Yerushalmi, end of Berachos: "He who makes his Torah [study] occasional," etc.). That is to say, treating it like something one happens upon by chance, where the engagement with it is, at best, incidental. This affects not only the study of this specific part of Torah, but also impacts one’s study and success in all other parts of Torah, whatever they may be. As our Sages ruled, "Whoever says, 'This teaching is pleasant and this one is not pleasant,' etc." (Eruvin 64a)—even though he admits that the second teaching is just as much a teaching as the first, and it is understood that it is the word of Hashem—he claims that for him, it is not pleasant or suitable (see the gravity of this matter there).

My hope is that, at the very least, from now on you will establish a fixed time for the study of Chassidus, in accordance with the directive of our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya (the authority on the hidden part of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (the authority on the revealed part of Torah): a fixed time in one’s schedule, and, most importantly, a fixed place in one’s soul. Through this, you will gain not only in matters pertaining to Chassidus, but also in your study of the revealed Torah.

Regarding what you wrote about your future studies, you should present the details of the matter to three of your friends, and may Hashem grant them the correct insight on how to advise you.

I am sure you are aware of the three daily portions—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and at the very least, you should keep to them from now on.

With blessings for good news in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6250

6250

B"H, 16 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you ask:

Is it permissible for a seventeen-year-old boy to engage in deep contemplation? You do not specify what you are referring to, but it seems from the continuation of your letter that you are referring to matters concerning the *chovos halevavos* (duties of the heart) of a Jewish person.

It is simple, and it is a **psak din** in Torah, that not only is it permissible, but one is obligated to do so. This is as the Rambam rules in *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*, Chapter 1, Halacha 6, that the knowledge of this matter is a *mitzvah aseh*. Similarly, it is a *psak din* in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim*, beginning of Section 98, that one should not stand to pray (the *Shemoneh Esrei* prayer, which is **gimel pe'amim** [three times] every day, and one is obligated in it just as in all other *mitzvos* from the age of *ol hamitzvos*) without contemplation before the prayer regarding the greatness of Hashem, may He be exalted, etc. The essence of contemplation is not to think about the words, but to think about the concepts. In order to contemplate the greatness of Hashem, one must meditate and delve into the matters through which a person recognizes what the greatness of Hashem and its essence are. These are explained in many books, among them the books of Chassidus. You should endeavor to meet with the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, etc., Rabbi N. Shamaryahu Shonkin—Shikun Rabbanim, Romema, Jerusalem—and he will show you the appropriate places for the aforementioned.

2) Regarding your question on how it is possible to attain humility and fulfill the statement of the *Mishnah*, "Be exceedingly humble of spirit."

Study with focus the *drush* in the holy *Tanya*, Chapter 30, and ask the aforementioned Rabbi as well; he will provide you with understanding in this, and he will also point out other places where you will find further explanation, as well as regarding the other matters and questions in your letter.

I am certain you are aware of the three daily *shiurim*—*Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*—and in any case, you should keep them from here on in.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

Following the longest of intervals, your letter was received—without an indication of when it was written—(and also without the check you mention).

It is understood and simple that you must, after all, begin to occupy yourself with the true task of every Jew, in accordance with the statement of the *Mishnah*: "I was created to serve my Maker." This is achieved through spreading the "candle of *mitzvah* and the light of *Torah*," and the "light in *Torah*"—which is the *Torah* of Chassidus and its matters—in every place your hand can reach. This is especially true since you are in a place where, regarding the *Torah* of Chabad, very little has been done thus far in proportion to what is possible. This is despite the fact that people standing on the outside declare at every opportunity that so-and-so are there, who are "iron pillars of all Chabad matters." This is certainly true regarding a fundamental matter like the spreading of the *maayanos*, which our *Rabbeim Nesi'im* demand in every generation, and especially my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in this generation of ours, and *kal v'chomer*. May you bring good news in all that has been mentioned, both in private matters and in general matters, and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 6,252

6,252

B"H, 17 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 5/6, in which you write regarding adopting a child from a non-Jewish schoolgirl, and you rely on the principle that "a minor is converted by the intent of the Beis Din."

Heaven forbid to even think about such a thing. If you and your wife (may she live and be well) have decided to adopt a child, it must be from a Jewish man and woman, and the child must be born in accordance with Jewish law. With proper effort, such a child can be found. You might also look in North Africa among our brethren, the Sephardim, where all are upright Jews, and—thank G-d—there are large families, and the economic situation there is very difficult.

You do not write about the state of your home regarding Torah and mitzvos, but according to the instruction of our holy Torah that one must always increase in goodness, no matter how good the situation may be, there is always room for improvement. And Hashem is certain to add even more blessing and success in whatever you are in need of, together with all of Klal Yisrael.

Surely you are aware of the practice to recite the monthly Tehillim shiur—where the Tehillim is divided according to the days of the month—each morning after davening. Your wife is also surely aware of the good custom of the virtuous daughters of Israel to give charity each time before lighting candles on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov. In any case, you should act in this manner from now on.

With blessings for good tidings.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6,253

6,253

B"H, 17 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, distinguished, and learned, who engages in the needs of the community,
R' Chananya Yom Tov Lipa, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Monday, I have requested that you get in touch as soon as possible with Anash in Albany regarding the matter about which you write. Surely you are also in contact with them yourself. May it be the will [of Hashem] that from you and from them, the Name of the Most High be glorified, especially regarding the most exalted matter of the purity of the Jewish people, for purity leads to... [the coming of] Eliyahu HaNavi, who will announce our true redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

Regarding what you wrote about comments on your book—what can I do? Many preoccupations surround me, and the teaching of the Mishnah is fulfilled: "Do not say, 'When I am free I will study,' lest you never become free."

And regarding your mention that people have approached you for a *psak* from me—it is well known that this is not my practice, especially in matters that many have already discussed, as is also transcribed in your books.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that, since we are coming from the days of the festival of Pesach, the time of our freedom—freedom from the 49 gates of impurity—and are approaching day by day the receiving of the Torah, the tablets written with the finger of G-d, "engraved (*charut*) on the tablets" (read not *charut* [engraved], but *cheirus* [freedom], the complete freedom from the *yetzer hara*, not only that one should rule over it, but that it should even cease to exist from the world—see regarding this Tanya, beginning of Chapter 13 and Chapter 37, where its perfection and ultimate purpose depend on our actions and our *avodah*), may abundant bounty be drawn down into all the worlds through the rectification of our *nefesh, ruach,* and *neshamah* from every dross and blemish. For the rectification of the *nefesh, ruach,* and *neshamah* is through the study of Torah with *yiras shamayim* and the fulfillment of its *mitzvos*.

And this applies not only to oneself, but "Say and you shall say"—to warn the adults regarding the children. And not only in matters of forbidden foods, which is a matter of acting out of spite (see Horayos 11a: "He ate a flea..."), but also regarding the consumption of blood, which, according to its simple meaning, is beneficial for health (see Berachos 44b: "Every soul... is close to the soul..." and see also Ramban, Vayikra 17:11). And furthermore, even in matters of ritual impurity which are merely *gezeiras hakasuv* (decrees of the Torah), for "it is not the corpse that defiles... but I have issued a decree, I have enacted a statute" (see Yevamos 114a and there).

Through this, we will merit freedom from the nations of the world and the subjugation of kingdoms, in the true and complete redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6155

6155

B"H, 17 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the avreich Menachem Mendel Shalom, may he live,

Shalom u’vrachah!

After a long interval, your letter from Pesach Sheni was received, in which you ask how one should guide a person in the path of Chassidus.

It is understood that this depends on the soul-nature of the one being guided. For although it is simple that every person of Yisrael must be introduced to the matters of Toras HaChassidus, the opinions of people are not the same; therefore, one must proceed according to the spirit of each individual. See also the introduction to the Tanya. The general point is that guidance must begin in the manner to which that person is already accustomed. That is to say: if he is of the *baalei mussar* type, one should begin by introducing him to *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* by our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, or to *Kuntres Uma'ayon*, and the like. If he is of the *baalei haskalah* type, one should find topics for him in *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, and the like. In general, the book *Derech Mitzvosecha* is relatively easy to understand, and one can find various types of topics there. It is understood that for those who have no knowledge at all of Torah and its matters, the beginning of guidance must be through the *sichos* and *Likutei Dibburim*.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything about your daily schedule at this time, for surely you have *kevius itim* in both *nigleh* and Chassidus. I am certain you will fill this in on the next opportunity.

At an *eis ratzon*, I will mention you at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever you may need.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

**Menachem Mendel Shalom:** Vogel.

## 6,156

6,156

B"H, 17 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs,
Moreinu HaRav Mordechai, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Pesach Sheni, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein.

Regarding what you wrote about the transcription of the *maamar*: In my opinion, the style of the *maamar* is difficult. Even though several *maamarim* in the *Kehilas Milano* journal are written in this style, it is understood that for a conceptual subject—especially one involving a new topic—the style should be as accessible as possible. It is possible that the difficulty of the style is due to the habits of the transcriber, in which case it is hard to change; however, it is also possible that, on the contrary, a simple style can convey even deep concepts, especially when the intention is to spread the *maayanos* outward (*la'chutz*), and *kal v'chomer* [it is understood].

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***6,156***

**Moreinu HaRav Mordechai:** Perlov, Milan. Additional letters to him appear above in Vol. 13, p. 390, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 6,257

B"H, 19 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

And this is understood.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for good tidings regarding all that was mentioned.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

## 6,258

6,258

B"H, 21 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Daniel, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

After the longest of intervals, your letter of 5 Iyar was received. Since you do not mention anything regarding your health or your affairs, this is surely a sign that everything is in order.

Regarding what you wrote concerning Rabbanit Marcus, may she live, who has expressed her kind desire to donate two Sifrei Torah to Kfar Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established—this is a proper thing. And since our Sages have said, "It is a mitzvah to publicize those who perform a mitzvah," the Village Committee will surely create a memorial in an appropriate manner for the soul of her husband, the Rav, of blessed memory, in connection with the presentation of the Sifrei Torah to the synagogue in Kfar Chabad.

Regarding what you wrote about the writing of the word *petzu'a daka* (crushed/wounded), the instruction of our Alter Rebbe is known: to write it with an *alef*. My father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, once related that he himself saw a Sefer Torah which, according to tradition, was written by the Maharam of Rothenburg, and it was written there with an *alef*. Likewise, in the Sefer Torah in Prague that Ezra the Scribe proofread, it is also written with an *alef*. Therefore, the aforementioned Sifrei Torah should certainly be written according to the instruction of our Alter Rebbe, the author of the Tanya (the authority on the hidden aspects of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (the authority on the revealed aspects of Torah).

Regarding your question as to whether to correspond with your relatives in our former country—since you have waited until now, it is worthwhile to wait for a time when relations from Eretz Yisrael to there improve, unless you are able to write through someone who is currently in Poland, from where they could send the letter to your relatives.

With blessings for long days and good years, and for good tidings, may it be so.

## 6,259

B"H, 21 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Friday, in which you ask:

1) What is the advice for kavanah in tefillah?

The advice is hisbonenus before tefillah—at least for a few moments—regarding before Whom one is about to pray. It is appropriate to also learn by heart from the beginning of Perek 41 in Tanya up to the word "HaMelech" (page 72), and before tefillah, to review the content of this passage, either verbally or in thought. Likewise, on weekdays, one should set aside a few coins for tzedakah before tefillah.

2) What is the advice for Torah study and for being persistent in it?

The aforementioned hisbonenus is also helpful regarding Torah study. The essential point in both matters is the realization that Torah, tefillah, and all the mitzvos were given for the benefit of man, and therein lies his happiness, both materially and spiritually.

3) You surely know what is written in many of the books of our Sages and great leaders: that for kavanah in tefillah, it is helpful to pray from a Siddur, and in Torah study, one must articulate the words—that is, to study verbally, not only in thought.

You surely know of the takanah to recite the monthly Tehillim portion every day after morning tefillah—as it is divided according to the days of the month—and that one should keep to this, or at least keep to it from now on.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6262

B"H, 21 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Moshe, may he live, known as Dr. Taub.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter, which took longer than usual to arrive.

At an opportune time, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever you may need, and especially for a good arrangement, as we are commanded in our Torah, the Torah of life, to live with joy and gladness of heart. If every person requires this, how much more so a physician, who must heal those who turn to him. Indeed, even physical strength, in the literal sense, depends on one’s state of mind and spiritual fortitude; from this it is understood that a physician must himself be at a level where he can "moisten others" [i.e., influence them with his own vitality]. Since everyone is commanded to have joy and strong trust, it is certain that the possibility and ability are in his hands, and reality corresponds to this as well—for it is impossible that the Torah, which is the only truth, would command something that does not correspond to reality. Surely, for someone like you, further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

We are currently in the days between the festival of Pesach, the time of our freedom—freedom from all matters that distress and burden—and the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah. "Do not read *charus* (engraved) but *cheirus* (freedom)." May it be G-d’s will that you receive good tidings regarding your own affairs as well.

## 6,263

6,263

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter of May 7, in which you ask what you should do in order for your fortune to succeed and to be happy in life.

The Creator of the world and its Guide has already answered this question, as it is written in His Torah: "If you follow My statutes and observe My mitzvos and perform them, then I will grant..." and all the blessings mentioned in that parsha (Vayikra 26:3 and onwards). Furthermore, it is written: "And it shall come to pass, if you hearken diligently to the voice of Hashem your G-d... that all these blessings shall come upon you..." (Devarim 28:1, 2). The mitzvos mentioned are, of course, detailed in their specifics in the Shulchan Aruch and in many other places.

Regarding your question as to when you will marry, etc.—it is not the custom to seek out the future, for it is said, "You shall be wholehearted with Hashem your G-d" (Devarim 18:13). Rather, a Jewish man and woman must be strong in their bitachon in the Creator, may He be blessed and exalted, that He will grant them happy lives, provided that they, for their part, conduct themselves in accordance with His will, His Torah, and His mitzvos.

It is my hope that you are learning and conducting yourself as is fitting for a daughter of Israel—each of whom is called a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah—and that you will influence your friends in this regard as well. May Hashem, may He be blessed, grant you success and bring you good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned.

## 6,264

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the night of Friday, in which you ask for advice regarding your personal matters.

As a general rule, the advice given in such matters is the concept of "I have set Hashem before me always" (*Shivisi Hashem l'negdi tamid*). This is an explicit verse in Scripture, and furthermore, our teacher the Rema—the final arbiter in Israel—began all four parts of the *Shulchan Aruch* with this, to teach us that this is the beginning and foundation of fulfilling the Torah. You should study the beginning of Chapter 41 of the *Tanya Kadisha*, from the start until the second page, the word *hamelech* (the King). From time to time, while sitting in your house or walking on the way, you should review the aforementioned by heart, whether through speech or at the very least in thought. When you accustom yourself to the idea that Hashem is standing over you, etc., as explained there in the *Tanya*, this will, as a matter of course, refine not only the *neshamah* but also the body. Likewise, it is appropriate that you be fluent by heart in several chapters of *Mishnayos* and at least one chapter of *Tanya*. Every weekday, before *davening*, you should set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*. After *davening* each day—including *Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*—you should recite the daily portion of *Tehillim* (as the *Tehillim* is divided for the days of the month). All of this will be beneficial for your learning in general, and for matters of Torah and *mitzvos* in particular, in accordance with the words of our Sages: "One who comes to purify himself is assisted."

2) You also ask for advice regarding success in Torah study.

The matter has already been stated: "If one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do not believe him"—which means that the matter depends on him, and he has been given the strength for it. However, to the extent that you increase in *yiras shamayim* (fear of Heaven) alongside an increase in Torah study, the blessing of Hashem will increase in the aforementioned. As the *Mishnah* states: "Anyone whose fear of Heaven precedes his wisdom, his wisdom will endure."

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6155

6155

B”H, 22 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Tel Aviv,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the report regarding the activities during the month of Nissan, and as the summary indicates, a continuation will surely follow.

I also had the opportunity in these past days to review their *pidyonos* and reports from recent weeks and months. It is fitting to say regarding this, in the style of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that it is "a very fine plowing and a very fine sowing."

Since they have already been engaged in their holy work for some years, and they surely have kept the reports and *pidyonos*, it would be appropriate for them to dedicate a special meeting to conduct a sort of summary—at the very least in a general sense—of their past activities. The main point is to learn from this regarding future activities, with the central focus being that the plowing and sowing should lead to the growth of fruits and produce, and to the gathering and harvesting of those fruits and produce.

In other words, how to continue in a way that participation in a *farbrengen* and the like leaves an impression on the participants even for the days that follow, and how to maintain a connection with them even after the *farbrengen*, and so on.

There is another point regarding the above (which is surprising, as no one among *anash* has raised it), and that is: since there are currently many tourists in Eretz Yisrael—may it be built and established—from various countries, this is a unique opportunity to influence various countries from their very location in Eretz Yisrael. This is provided that they utilize all the days and all the opportunities to demonstrate and instill within them the matters of Chabad and its *maayanos*. Although it is understood that not all types of people are the same in this regard—concerning their receptivity to influence and impressions, and each type requires an appropriate approach—on the other hand, it is possible to approach every type, provided that they contemplate what the right way to do so is.

In general, it is difficult to write from here about the details and the fine details of all the above, and there is no benefit in doing so [moreover, it is even detrimental, in the spirit of our Sages' teaching: "A person prefers his own *kav* over nine *kavim* belonging to his fellow"]. If they create a plan of their own, *vet zich arbeten gishmaker* (it will work out more pleasantly) and so on.

I am sending this letter as an urgent dispatch, because in my opinion, the matter is of the utmost urgency. To my astonishment and regret, in the letters from *anash*, no one is raising the matter mentioned above—not only regarding influence on distant countries, but not even regarding influence on the tourists themselves.

As with all matters, extreme caution is needed here as well, to avoid the conduct of "a pot belonging to partners," which is especially damaging in this case. For it can be said that "my bowels are stirred" [in pain]—that one is a partner, yet at the same time decides that the other partner should do everything, and that he himself should do nothing.

May it be Hashem’s will that they succeed in their holy work to make Eretz Yisrael truly the Holy Land, also in a revealed manner and in the manner described above. For "out of Zion shall go forth Torah," etc.—meaning exactly the terminology of **Torah**. As the well-known teaching states (*Eichah Rabbah* 2:13): "If someone tells you there is wisdom among the nations, believe it; if someone tells you there is Torah among the nations, do not believe it," for this is unique to the Jewish people, and it negates the "nations of the land" in the literal sense, even to the point of negating the "nation" that is within the Jewish person (*Likutei Torah, Devarim* 90d).

The aforementioned work requires finding ways, every single day, how to perform it and how to utilize it for this purpose. It goes without saying that one must utilize the *yomei d'pagra*, days of *farbrengen*, etc., etc.

I am not writing specifically to the rest of *anash* and the branches; surely they will find ways to publicize the above, whether by sending a copy or by holding a meeting, and the like.

With blessings for good news and for the details mentioned above.

## 6,267

B"H, 23 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his communal work,
R' Pinchas Leibish Hertzel,

Shalom u’Bracha,

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 17 Iyar, in which you write about the farbrengens of the past months. May it be the will of Hashem that everyone increases their good deeds in spreading Yiddishkeit in general, and the wellsprings of Chassidus in particular.

Especially in light of what is explained regarding the concept of "in which [mitzvah] is one most careful," in the Iggeres HaKodesh of the Alter Rebbe, end of Epistle 7, that one must be careful; and according to the interpretation of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, to "illuminate" that specific mitzvah. In the vast majority of cases, one can see even with physical eyes which mitzvah that is, in which one must be most careful. In the case of many of Anash, they have surely already realized that it is their matter of chinuch on the foundation of purity in the institution of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and his father, the Rebbe (Rashab) — may the merit of these tzaddikim protect us. From this, it is understood, and it is also simple, that in this regard there must be—to use the language of the aforementioned Iggeres HaKodesh—a preference, a care, and an extra alacrity, with greater intensity and double-strength, far above the care taken for other mitzvos. When one contemplates the alacrity required for other mitzvos according to what is explained in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 21, and subsequently how there must be a "preference," etc., in all the aforementioned terms—there is no doubt that your activity and involvement in Yeshivas Toras Emes will be with an increase, etc., etc., many times over. As is explained in many places, since we have been commanded regarding this, the capability and the strength have certainly been granted for it, and the matter depends only on their desire to bring it from potential into actuality.

May it be the will of Hashem that you also influence your colleagues in this holy work, so that they, too, will contemplate this for themselves. Consequently, the holy institution will develop and grow, both in quantity and quality, with outstanding success.

For although success in general (see Torah Or, beginning of Parshas Vayeshev) is a matter that transcends the natural order, it is nonetheless understood according to what is explained regarding the concept of *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from above). Even though it is from above, it is dependent to a great degree upon the manner of *is'arusa d'letata* (arousal from below). As with all these details, this also applies to the matter of success. May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good news soon—good in its fullness regarding all that has been mentioned.

With blessings for good tidings,

6268

B"H, 23 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

And since every single Jew is commanded regarding this, it is certain that everyone has been given the strength to fulfill this command.

This is especially true since you have merited to be appointed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisroel, in the style of the chapter of Tehillim that one begins to recite each day, "Happy is the one whom You choose and bring near... that he may dwell in Your courtyards" [Tehillim 65:5], to serve with distinction in the Beis Medrash of Lubavitch in Lubavitch.

During these days of Sefirah, as explained in Chassidus, we count day after day in such a way that the earlier days do not fall away, Heaven forbid, but rather join with the others to be counted—not merely as a recounting of events, but as "shining and sparkling" (Zohar Vol. II, 136b). The concept is understood from what is written in the Siddur in the discourse *HaShamayim Mesaprim* at length.

May each one of us merit and succeed, with the help of Hashem, that our days should similarly join together, shining and sparkling with the sparks of the supreme point, as the Zohar states there, "shining ever brighter" through the "candle of mitzvah and the Torah of light," and the light within the Torah—which is the Torah of Chassidus and its matters.

With blessings for good tidings and for long, good days and years in every respect.

## 670

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs,
R' Nissan, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received with pleasure your letter of 22 Iyar regarding your visit to the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim together with the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing and learned, R' Chaim, may he live, Bik, and the results of the examinations, which were satisfactory.

May it be the will of Hashem that regarding the students—since the physical descends from the spiritual, and in physical matters it is said, "He who has one hundred wants two hundred, and he who has two hundred wants four hundred"—that as the students' knowledge and diligence increase, so too will their thirst and application in the study of the pure Torah of Hashem, both the revealed and the inner dimensions, grow. May it be permeated with the light and vitality of Chassidus, so that they may be in accordance with the will and intention of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im who founded and directed the Yeshiva; for the words of the Tzaddikim, and certainly their deeds, endure forever and continue to exert their influence.

I send my regards to you and your colleague for the good news, and most importantly, that surely through the examination you aroused in the students a "jealousy of scribes" [kinas sofrim], regarding which it is said, "it increases wisdom." In the language of the Zohar (Vol. II, 126b), "it increases the measure of wisdom." The Tzemach Tzedek adds an explanation based on the teaching of our Sages (Shabbos 152b), "Whoever has jealousy in him, his bones rot," which refers to the "worm of holiness" that rots the cedar—the character traits of the nefesh habehamis. This is similar to what is explained in Orchos Tzaddikim, Shaar 14, regarding the aforementioned teaching of our Sages, "the jealousy of scribes increases wisdom," for when you see a person who studies, etc., and likewise regarding all the mitzvos, etc. He also references Sotah 3a (Or HaTorah, Vayeitzei, discourse beginning "And Rachel envied her sister").

With blessings for good tidings—and there is no good other than Torah and mitzvos—may it be fulfilled with joy and goodness of heart.

## 6271

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished,
R' Levi, shlita,

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter informing me of the celebration of the Mitzvah of the Shas and Mishnayos society, marking the completion of the Mishnayos and its commencement.

May it be the will of Hashem that you go from strength to strength in our holy Torah, the Torah of life. This expression is not merely figurative; it refers to life in this world of ours—even though it is physical and material—a life that corresponds to the instruction of the Torah, of which it is said: "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today."

This is also the allusion in the conclusion of the Mishnayos: "The Holy One, Blessed be He, found no vessel that could contain blessing for Israel other than peace." This means peace between the soul and the body, and within the soul itself, peace between the animal soul and the second soul in a Jew, which is the G-dly soul, as explained at length in the holy Tanya. Through this, one draws down peace and unity into the world as well.

This is also alluded to in the beginning of the Mishnah: "From when do we recite the Shema in the evenings?" Even during times of darkness in the world, the Jewish people recite it. According to the teaching of our Sages, do not read it as *vayikra* (and He called), but as *vayakri* (and he caused to call out): "Hear, O Israel, Hashem our G-d, Hashem is One." We coronate Him above, below, and in the four directions—unity in space, which is alluded to in the word "One." Similarly, there is unity in time, as alluded to in the name *Havayah*—He was, He is, and He will be—which is the intent of this Name, as per the ruling in Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, section 5.

With respect and regards to all those participating in the study of Mishnah, and in the language of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory—with a blessing to receive the Torah, which is approaching, with joy and inwardness.

## 6170

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rav, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu HaRav David, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of Wednesday, in which you touch upon the question that many have discussed regarding the time of Motzaei Shabbos, and you conclude that from Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, section 293, paragraph 1, it appears that one must wait 72 minutes.

Now, it is known that the ruling of Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Baal HaTanya (who rules in the hidden aspects of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (who rules in the revealed aspects of Torah), is that the aforementioned waiting time is not uniform throughout the entire year or in all locations. See the *Seder Hachnasas Shabbos* by Rabbeinu HaZaken, printed in my Siddur. Therefore, in every location, one must know the calculation appropriate for its horizon, and even within this, there is a distinction based on the time of year itself.

What I have seen practiced here in New York is to wait approximately fifty minutes after sunset, but it is understood that I am not responsible for this. In general, the merit of delaying [the conclusion of] Motzaei Shabbos is well known, though in the synagogue it must be done in a manner that the majority of the congregation can manage. It is clear that this concerns a *hiddur* (a beautification of the mitzvah) and not a prohibition according to the letter of the law, and indeed, Shabbos is great, for it is equivalent to all the mitzvos.

With respect and blessing for proper health and for good tidings in communal matters and in personal matters, for the one is dependent upon the other.

*6170*

**Moreinu HaRav David:** Winchester, Chicago. Additional letters to him – above, Vol. 16, 6035, and as noted in the footnotes there.

**One must know the calculation:** See *Kuntres Nesivos Shabbos*, Vol. 2, footnotes 7; 14.

## 6173

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the avreich Hillel, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter of 16 Iyar, in which you ask:

1) Regarding what is explained in Iggeres HaKodesh by our Alter Rebbe, Epistle 19, interpreting the statement of our Sages that "a sage is superior to a prophet," in that prophecy is a matter of vision—like the literal sight of the physical eye—whereas the superiority of Chochma is a matter of intellectual apprehension (hasagah): Did Moshe Rabbeinu, beyond what he saw in prophecy, also apprehend those levels that the Arizal apprehended?

This is indeed the case.

And although on the face of it there is room to suggest otherwise—and all the more so from the revealed dimensions of Torah, based on the story of our Sages (Menachos 29b)—nevertheless, the truth is that he did apprehend the aforementioned levels. As is written in the books of Kabbalah and explained in the teachings of Chassidus, the level of Moshe Rabbeinu was the level of Chochma of Atzilus; that is to say, he apprehended at an infinitely higher level through the aspect of Chochma. However, there is room for further study regarding Mashiach; see Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah, Chapter 9, Halacha 2; Tanchuma, Toldos 20; Yalkut Shimoni to Yeshayahu 52:13.

And this is not the place to elaborate.

2) Regarding what is written there in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 9, interpreting the statement of our Sages that "Torah study is equivalent to acts of kindness," whereas in the footsteps of Mashiach it is different—you ask how the essential importance has changed.

This is analogous to the distinction regarding a mitzvah whose time is passing, or a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others; it is understood that when the time is near its end, or when there is no one else to do it, the importance of the mitzvah changes.

Although you do not mention it, I hope that you have fixed times for studying the teachings of Chassidus frequently. May it be the will [of Hashem] that this consistency be in accordance with the adage of our Alter Rebbe—the author of the Tanya (who decides in the hidden dimensions of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (who decides in the revealed dimensions of Torah)—not only consistency in time, but also consistency in the soul, which is the main thing.

Surely you are aware of the three well-known daily study portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya; in any event, you should observe them from now on.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 615

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the G-d-fearing, industrious, and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with the needs of the community, a man of many accomplishments, Rabbi Avraham, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

It was a pleasure for me to hear from Mr. and Mrs. ... may they live, about your activities in strengthening and disseminating Yiddishkeit within your community, in the beis medrash and the shul, and specifically regarding the core and internal matter of kosher education.

If this has always been a vital matter for the Jewish people in all places and at all times, it is all the more so in our current era, which is full of events and confusion of the mind, and in this country, the United States, where there is a good quality and internal trait to be found in the youth—innocence and faith. However, due to our many sins, in years past there were certain circles that exploited these traits in a direction contrary to the path of Torah and mitzvos. I was happy to hear from the aforementioned that Hashem has granted him the merit and success to see good fruit from his labor—the success of his work and his efforts—and that many members of the community hold him in high regard for this.

May it be Hashem’s will that you continue to gather strength for the holy Torah, the Torah of life, and its mitzvos. In accordance with the statement of our Sages, "He who has one hundred wants two hundred," may the success in your work awaken in you a desire and enthusiasm for even greater achievements.

On this occasion, I would like to encourage you—even though you are certainly already aware of this—regarding the setting of fixed times for study, including the inner dimensions of Torah, which in our generations has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. It is this that provides vitality and enthusiasm to the Jewish person in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos. Especially for one who has influence over many fellow Jews, any increase in one’s own vitality and enthusiasm is multiplied many times over by the increase that comes to those he influences as a result.

Regarding the transition from the general to the individual: I sensed from the aforementioned how much they are positively affected by the encouragement and strengthening they receive from you, whether through speech or through actions to lift their downtrodden spirits. Although it is my hope that their fortune will soon begin to rise and their situation will improve in certain respects, you will surely continue to strengthen and encourage them. After all, you are surely aware of the trials in Yiddishkeit that the aforementioned and their family have withstood. Furthermore, they have influenced and continue to influence the environment in which they are found, drawing others under the wings of the Shechinah.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 627

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Wednesday, in which you describe how secular studies are distracting you from *hasmadah* and *shekidah* in your holy studies, and specifically, as you put it, now that you are in the final stages.

From this, it appears that you are soon to finish your secular studies, although it is not clear whether this will be very soon, next month, or later than that.

Now, if you are finishing your secular studies in a month or, in any event, in the near future, the matter depends solely on you: to study *Torah Hakedosha* with *hasmadah* and *shekidah* in a manner that is "increasing and growing." Regarding this, we have been promised by our Sages, "You have labored and you have found." It would be best if you could study holy subjects in the aforementioned manner for at least two years, without distracting yourself with foreign thoughts of any kind. We see tangibly that study in this manner affects the entire duration of a Jewish person’s life on earth.

You are surely aware of the three daily *shiurim*—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and you should, at the very least, keep them from here on in. Furthermore, every weekday before morning *davening*, set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings for good tidings,

## 6,177

6,177

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5718

Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter of the 19th of Iyar, in which you write that you are feeling on the path to health and strengthening.

May it be the will of Hashem that you soon return to your full strength, both in the literal sense and in the deeper sense as explained in the maamar *Maskil L'Eisan* by the Alter Rebbe (printed in *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus*). We are currently in the days leading up to the receiving of the Torah, which brings healing to the world in general, and specifically to the Jewish people who receive the Torah. As is recounted in the *Mechilta*, at the time of the receiving of the Torah, all of Israel was healthy and whole. Based on the known principle that the receiving of the Torah—in terms of the specific days—occurs every single day, as indicated by the phrasing "the Giver of the Torah" in the present tense, it is understood that every Jewish person should be healthy and whole. In the words of the Rambam: "Maintaining a healthy and sound body is among the ways of Hashem..."

It is surely unnecessary to urge you to influence your son, may he live, to set fixed times for the study of the inner dimension of Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. Through every addition in Torah and mitzvos—and all the more so through an addition in the inner dimension of the Torah, which is called in the holy Zohar the "soul of the Torah"—there is a manifold increase in the blessings of Hashem, both in what is needed for the life of the body and the life of the soul.

With blessings for good tidings, and in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may we receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

## 6278

B"H, 26 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

After the longest of interruptions, your letter of 24 Iyar was received. It was a pleasure to read about the development of the Talmud Torah and the increase in the number of students; surely there is also an increase in the quality of their studies.

It is certainly unnecessary to remind you that at all times, the study of our Torah—in the language of Chazal, "study that leads to action"—must be the priority. This is all the more true in our current era. As the Mishnah puts it, this comes about when his *yiras shamayim*—the study of matters pertaining to the fear of Heaven—precedes his wisdom. It is understood that this does not refer to the quantity of time, for we sometimes see that even a few moments of study regarding *yiras shamayim* (or even just a few words spoken with warmth and *hislahavus*) can influence a student for a long time to come.

Regarding what you wrote concerning a student who has non-Jewish friends and how to relate to this:

In most cases, we see that if one provides him with Jewish friends, this naturally distances him from the aforementioned companions. Since he is among your students, surely it is possible to make an effort so that the other students draw closer to him, and consequently, he will not have free time for other friends, and for those mentioned in particular.

Regarding what you wrote about the debts he must repay, and that if he were able to borrow a sum, it would ease his burden—you do not specify the minimum amount that could help him. In any case, it is appropriate that he consult with *anash* on the spot regarding this matter.

With the blessing for the *Chag*, in the language accepted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe: to receive the Torah with joy and *pnimiyus*, and with good tidings in all the matters you wrote about.

## 6,180

6,180

B.H., 26 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and energetic Rabbi Menachem [Rackman], may he be well.

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter—which was delayed until now due to an abundance of pressing matters, for which I ask your forgiveness.

In accordance with the teaching of Chazal that "everything follows the conclusion," it was pleasant for me to read at the end of your letter that you are prepared and satisfied to increase your efforts regarding the dissemination of Yiddishkeit and its matters, illuminated by the explanations of Toras HaChassidus and its worldview.

It is surely unnecessary to point out to someone of your standing the unique possibilities you possess in this area, given that you lead a congregation of many families, where every single soul is an entire world.

Furthermore, you are a professor, which means you have a special connection with the students and young people in your class, and through them, with their peers as well. Surely, for the most part, their attitude toward you is that of a student toward one from whom they hear instruction—meaning, they accept your words as they are.

While this increases the responsibility of the mashpia and teacher, it also—and this is the main point—increases your ability to bring about positive change in the youth. Even if the change is small, it grows along with the student’s maturity. As is the well-known example: a small change in a seed can be a decisive factor when it grows into a fruit-bearing tree.

It seems to me that the field in which you teach is that of ethics and human character—a field that has a direct connection to the goals toward which Toras HaChassidus strives. And even if you teach a different subject next year, ultimately, in everything one can find a moral lesson and a teaching relevant to practice, to the life of a person in this world. Therefore, you can also serve as a conduit for instilling the desired influence.

There is another point, which, although in a specific area, also carries great influence. In years past, and surely in the future as well, you have been a member of the committee for the Claims Conference regarding the grants given for culture, education, printing, and so on. This is a broad field, and through your opinion and influence, you have the ability to ensure that your colleagues also express the desired view regarding supporting activities that are in the spirit of the holy Torah and the tradition of Israel, and to prevent assistance and cooperation with matters that are against Hashem, His Torah, and His mitzvos.

I have already said many times, and from time to time my recognition of this increases—and reality proves it more and more—that the public in the United States in these years is capable of receiving, and for the most part even demands, that they be told a clear truth, even if it is sharp and without compromise. Even those who are not prepared to make major changes to the right in their own private lives are prepared to assist in these changes regarding public life, provided that one shows them the way and proves to them that this is the path of truth.

As we approach the time of the giving of our Torah, when the Children of Israel became a treasured people above all nations, a kingdom of priests and a holy nation, the support of the Torah is what established and continues to establish Rabbis in Israel—Rabbis with the power to announce the complete and perfect Da’as Torah and to instill this perspective into the life around them, especially in their own congregations.

May it be the will of Hashem that everyone gifted with the power of influence, and especially those serving in a Rabbinic position, merit to fulfill this role in its entirety. And in the style of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: to receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

With respect and holiday blessings.

## 6,283

B"H, 28 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

The Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Kfar Chabad
May Hashem preserve them

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter of *Tiferes shebeYesod*, which contains several questions regarding the upcoming *farbrengen* of 12 Tammuz and its format.

I have already written this many times: in matters such as these, everything depends on the manner of preparation. That is to say, a detailed plan is essential well in advance, in a way that avoids the issue of "a pot belonging to partners" [where no one takes full responsibility]. Specific individuals must be responsible for specific aspects of the *farbrengen*. While it is understood that one should not intimidate those in charge, ultimately, the responsibility is not so burdensome that it requires fear and panic; it only requires preparation well in advance and in an organized manner.

Furthermore, we see that if one forces someone to accept a role or task, and even after being persuaded they do not truly agree but are merely embarrassed to refuse the requester, then the work and their efforts will have "that kind of appearance" (*aza oiszehen hot di arbet*). Since there is now enough time for an organized arrangement as mentioned above, and even time for consultation several times before beginning to put the plan into action, all those active in this should gather and discuss the matter. Afterward, they should hold an expanded meeting, and in accordance with the discussion and the results of that meeting, they should decide regarding your questions.

Regarding the expenses involved, I will encourage *anash* to participate in covering approximately one-third of the costs (this, of course, assumes it will not be a local *farbrengen*, but rather one on a broader scale).

Surely the Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Tel Aviv have forwarded to you a copy of my letter regarding compiling a summary of the activities from previous years, etc.

With blessings for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness, and for good tidings.

**Copy of my letter:** See above, 6,265.

## 6,184

B”H, 28 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 25 Nissan (and the follow-up) which concludes with the question of how one should ask the Creator, may He be blessed, for the needs of oneself and one’s household, and in this context, also for atonement regarding undesirable matters of the past, etc.

The answer to this is already stated in our holy Torah—the Torah of life, even in its literal sense in this world—as well as in the books of Chassidus and the books of mussar. The central point in this is complete regret for undesirable matters of the past and a firm resolution for the future—a resolution that one begins to implement immediately in daily life through a lifestyle guided by the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life. For it is a remedy for the great world, and for this small world, which is man, and it brings about the fulfillment of his needs and the fulfillment of his heart’s desires for the good.

However, at times the Creator and Guide of the world tests the Jewish person, as it is written: "For Hashem your G-d is testing you to know whether you love [Him]..." And it has already been said: "G-d made man upright" (meaning He provided him with clear and straight instructions in His Torah, and therefore it is a wonder and a surprise that) "they have sought many calculations," and inquiries, and hints that do not align with these instructions. Furthermore, one must add that since Hashem demands this from each and every one of us, it is certain that prior to this, Hashem grants the strength to fulfill the demand in its entirety (and furthermore, that) He demands this from us—the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He—with joy and a glad heart, as per the words of the Rambam in *Sefer Yad HaChazakah*, at the end of *Hilchos Lulav*.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6,785

6,785

B”H, 29 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc., R’ Ben Zion, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter from the 37th day of the Omer, and everything follows the signature, as you are, B”H, feeling well, etc.

May it be Hashem’s will that you return to your full strength, both in the literal sense and in the sense explained in the *maamar* "Maskil L’Eisan" by our Alter Rebbe (printed in *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus*).

Since you are a descendant of the cedars of the Torah of Chassidus, my hope is strong that you have fixed times for studying their teachings, in addition to conducting yourself in accordance with this Torah, and that you are surely increasing from time to time in all of this, as our Torah commands that we must always ascend in matters of holiness.

It is surely superfluous to point out that if in previous generations it was possible to suffice with Chassidic conduct or by reciting Chassidic teachings as a *segulah*, without delving into the depth of their understanding and comprehension—for at that time the world was not so deeply immersed in intellects contrary to the intellect of Torah, and Yiddishkeit was visible in the street, and certainly in the home—in our current era, when people are immersed in the schemes and cunning of external wisdoms (and not a small portion is the "wisdom" of heresy), in addition to the fact that the *Chabad* (intellect) of the mind is invested in matters of livelihood, and strange winds are blowing in the street, etc.—it is obvious that one must, in contrast, increase understanding and comprehension by studying the inner dimension of the Torah in depth. This is called in the holy *Zohar* the "Tree of Life," and it adds vitality to the study of the revealed Torah and the performance of its *mitzvos*, etc., reaching even to the physical life of a Jewish person, which is also holy. These matters are explained at length in many places, among them the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of our Alter Rebbe, the author of the *Tanya* (the arbiter of the hidden dimension of Torah), and the *Shulchan Aruch* (the arbiter of the revealed dimension of Torah) in section 26, and in the *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* by his great-great-grandson, the Rebbe Rashab. May it be His will that in this study as well, you will soon bring good news that you are feeling well and are increasing, etc.

With blessings for true health, for good tidings regarding all that was mentioned, and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 6,186

B”H, 29 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, in which you write that you are a teacher for children in Detroit, and that for some time now people have been urging you to move your residence to New York, where all matters of Yiddishkeit are more easily accessible, etc., and you ask for my opinion on this.

In my opinion, it is surprising that there is even room for doubt in this matter. For the education of the children of Yisrael on the purity of holiness is the work of Hashem, and there is no greater task than this, especially in our current era—a "generation of orphans." Happy is the portion of anyone who has merited to engage in this. On the contrary, one must gather strength and influence others to do the same, and this is certainly true in the outlying cities, where this is in the category of a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others. Precisely for the reason mentioned (that in New York all matters of Yiddishkeit are easier), the merit of each person who engages in this [in the outlying cities] is many times greater. Our Sages have promised that the measure of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is measure-for-measure, only many times over. Therefore, one who engages in the education of the children of Yisrael—each of whom is referred to as "You are children to Hashem, your G-d"—will certainly be rewarded by Hashem many times over with the success of his own sons and daughters, may they live, so that he will have from them an abundance of true nachas, a traditional Jewish nachas.

It is well known how my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the Nasi of Yisrael, acted: he chose several bochurim and avreichim from among his finest students and sent them specifically to the outlying cities. Over the years that have passed, they have already seen fruits and fruits of fruits, and this serves as a directive and a lesson for each one of us, as is understood.

It is my hope that these lines, though small in quantity, will suffice to clarify the matter, even though it is understood in any case. I have come only to add enthusiasm to the fulfillment of your aforementioned role. May it be His will that you do this with true peace of mind and proper health.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 6,287

B"H, 29 Iyar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding your question about one of your students who wishes to study in an institution where only *limudei kodesh* are taught, and you ask whether to assist him in this or to do nothing.

It is surprising that there is any doubt or question about this matter. For in matters of *Talmud Torah* and the like, if one does not do everything possible—that is, as one is required to do—in this case, it falls under the category of the most alarming *bitul Torah*, regarding which it is said [the severe consequences] (even though at the other extreme, for one who is absolutely unable to do more, he fulfills his obligation even by reciting one chapter in the morning and one chapter in the evening; see the explanation of the Alter Rebbe on this* regarding how there is no contradiction here). From this, it is understood that for anyone who yearns to study even one hour more of *Torah HaKedoshah*, it is incumbent upon every Jew to exert himself as much as depends on him to assist him. Especially when, as you write, the person in question is talented, or in the language of Chazal, *memulach* (sharp)**.

With blessings to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness.

...When he visited here... he related that his method in educating his students in the yeshiva is to explain to them that the curriculum of the yeshiva where they are currently studying is not the highest level, but rather is suited to their previous education or the demands of their parents. Since only a few hours are dedicated to the study of Torah, they should aspire and strive at the first opportunity to study Torah at the expense of other subjects. In this, he explained to them that his own son—he sent him to study in a yeshiva in the Holy City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established. And here, too, it is evident that there is no contradiction **at all** in his student traveling to study in a yeshiva where they study **limudei kodesh** the entire day, contrary to the argument that was presented to you.

## 6288

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan, the Third Month
Brooklyn, N.Y.
On this day they arrived at the Wilderness of Sinai, 5718

To all the participants in the Third Annual Convention of Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, may Hashem grant them life.

Blessings and peace!

As you gather for the Third Annual Convention of Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, I turn to you all with the ancient Jewish greeting: *Bruchos HaBaos* (Welcome), and I wish you: *Yehi noam Hashem aleichen* (May the pleasantness of Hashem be upon you), and may there be much success in the work of your hands.

According to the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov, heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, everything is by *Hashgacha Pratis*, and from everything one can and must learn something in *avodas Hashem*.

Thus, the very day appointed for your convention—Rosh Chodesh Sivan—serves as a lesson and a directive for the convention itself.

On this day, the Jewish people arrived at the Wilderness of Sinai, *vayichan sham Yisrael neged hahar*—they encamped there, opposite Mount Sinai. Our Sages of blessed memory relate that this arrival at Mount Sinai was *k’ish echad b’lev echad* (as one person with one heart), and that Hashem recognized this as a fitting preparation and proof that they were worthy of receiving the Torah.

The Torah is *nitzchis*—eternal—valid for all generations and all places. It is therefore understood that the preparation and the modes of *Matan Torah* are likewise eternal.

The day of Rosh Chodesh Sivan itself must serve as a lesson and directive for Jews in general, and especially for those who gather at this time with the purpose of strengthening authentic *Yiddishkeit*, to dedicate themselves—through *ahavas Yisrael* unified with *ahavas Torah* and *ahavas Hashem*—to unity among all Jews, **unity opposite the mountain**, to accept the Torah of Moshe from Sinai—*Toras Chaim*, a Torah that gives life and directs how to live, throughout the weeks, days, Shabbosos, and Yomim Tovim.

And just as at Mount Sinai the *Kabbalas HaTorah* followed the order: *Koh tomar l’veis Yaakov*—to the women, and only then *v’sagid livnei Yisrael*—to the men.

So too now, in the preparation to receive the Torah with renewed vitality and *hislahavus*.

Jewish women—with Chabad vitality, warmth, and light, as explained by our Rebbes—must realize the aforementioned to the fullest extent.

And this is also one of the primary tasks of Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad—to be the guides in this holy work.

May the *Ribono shel Olam* help you, in good health and with great success, to fulfill your task.

And this will certainly also add to the blessings of the *Oibershter* in all that each of you needs, together with all your family members, may they live.

With blessings for success and all the best,

**M. Schneerson**
