## 6,290

B.H., In the third month, on this day, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the founding meeting of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Montreal,
May they live.

Peace and blessing!

It was a pleasure for me to receive the letter in which you write regarding the aforementioned meeting and the election of the interim committee.

Surely you have already proceeded to draft a plan of concrete activities, and most importantly—that you have already begun these activities.

As is explained in my letter to the Tzeirei Agudas Chabad here, a copy of which is enclosed.

May it be the will of Hashem that the desire of Hashem shall succeed in their hands—to work with the energy and enthusiasm that are the hallmarks of youth, in strengthening and disseminating Yiddishkeit in general, and in strengthening and disseminating the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs in particular.

It is understood that these words are not directed only to those who are young in the number of their years on earth, but to all those who are young and enthusiastic with a living emotion—a heart sensitive to Hashem, to the mitzvos, and to the Geulah.

This ability is given to every single person of Bnei Yisrael, for through contemplation, even for a short while, on the command of our Sages that the words of Torah and the command of the Creator, may He be blessed, should be "new to you, as if you heard them on that very day."

And indeed, in every single thing there is the matter of the Creator’s command and His avodah, as the verse instructs: "In all your ways, know Him." This is explained at length in the Rambam, Hilchos Deios, and in the Tur and Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, section 231.

Thus, everyone—and especially those who are educated and follow the Chabad approach of contemplating the inwardness and the secrets of every matter and its intent—should stand in a state of renewed vitality and strength for action at every single moment.

As in the Mishnah, with which our Rabbeinu HaZaken begins his Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim: "He should strengthen himself like a lion."

And in greater detail and explanation in the second edition there (based on the Tur): "Be bold as a leopard, light as an eagle, swift as a deer, and strong as a lion to do the will of your Father in Heaven," etc. See there.

With blessings for success in your holy work in your immediate environment and also in the environment that, for the time being, is not yet close—work with breadth of mind, with joy, and with a good heart.

And for the receiving of the Torah—in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—with joy and with inwardness.

**M. Schneerson**

## 6,291

B"H, 2 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, in which you outline your activities in spreading the wellsprings, and that you review maamarim of Chassidus in the beis medrash—which is known as a fortress, etc.—and that many have been drawn closer to the philosophy of Chassidus.

Certainly, you should strive to bring them closer and closer. We have seen tangibly that from time to time, through matters referred to as the "atmosphere of Chassidus" (naturally, without encroaching upon the time designated for the study of Chassidus), this closeness is achieved in a shorter time and to a greater degree.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the distinguished individuals who are interested in changing their attire to something more modern—it is understood that there is no room to fulfill such a **demand**. For it reflects the state of mind of the person in question, or her family, or both together. If, at the very beginning of a matter, such conditions are set, it is understandable what may grow from this in the near future and beyond. Entering into a shidduch is not meant to be a search for a state of war regarding matters of Torah and mitzvos. In war, whoever the actual victor may be, it is impossible that it will not cause damage to both sides—especially since, as stated regarding the aforementioned, "one nation shall be stronger than the other nation; sometimes this one rises and sometimes that one," etc.

However, I must say that the question itself is surprising. For there are many who are G-d-fearing in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established—may they increase—and surely one can find among them those who are interested in the very opposite; that is to say, those who hold fast to the tradition of their ancestors, for this tradition is Torah.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding the matzah shemurah distribution campaign and the Lag B'Omer campaign. Surely you will fill this in in future reports.

With blessings to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 6,192

6,192

B"H, 2 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from 22 Iyar, in which you ask with whom you should be tested.

It is surprising that you ask this, for in a good and auspicious hour you have become a student in the *mechinah* of the holy *yeshivah* Toras Emes, which was founded and is directed by our holy Rebbes, may their merits protect us. Consequently, regarding questions of examinations, studies, and the like, you must act in accordance with the instructions of the administration of the holy *yeshivah* Toras Emes.

Regarding the timing of the *shiurim* for *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*:

In general, it has already been explained in the introduction to *Hayom Yom* that the recitation of the *Tehillim* *shiur*—as the *Tehillim* is divided according to the days of the month—is after *davening* *Shacharis*. As for the study of *Chumash* with the commentary of Rashi and the *Tanya* *shiur*, it is understood that it is better to do so in close proximity to the *davening* of *Shacharis*, and it is best to do so immediately. If, for some reason, this is not possible, one completes them even during the night that follows.

Regarding the customs of putting on *tefillin*, you should ask the elders of *anash* who are in the holy city of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established.

#### ***6,192***

**One completes them even during the night:** See also above, Vol. 5, Letter 1,502; Vol. 8, 2,867.

6293

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, etc.,
R' Mordechai, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from the end of Iyar, in which you raise the following points:

1) Regarding what was said in my name, that Tefillin sent from Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) — even if they were written there by a G-d-fearing scribe and the batim were made by trustworthy people — must be checked here upon receipt.

My reasoning and rationale is that it has happened many times that customs officials have opened the batim (fearing that diamonds or pearls were hidden inside). It is understood that when they sewed them back together, there was room for various errors, including those that invalidate the Tefillin.

2) Regarding the Chabad custom of being particular about using specifically Calabria esrogim.

What I have heard and what appears to me to be correct according to the revealed Torah, I have written to someone—a copy is enclosed. I also transcribed it in the notes of the Sukkos Kuntres of the year 5712, page 59, where a sicha of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on this matter is also noted.

As for what you noted from the words of our Sages regarding the verse, "You shall lack nothing in it" (Devarim 8:9)—even pepper—it is obvious that Eretz Yisrael is capable of growing the fruit of a beautiful tree (esrog), and it is no less capable than it is of growing pepper. However, this does not necessitate that in the present time, the most mehudar (beautiful) esrogim are actually found in Eretz Yisrael. The verse speaks of potential and possibility, which does not always manifest in actuality. This is especially so in light of what is said, "Sulfur and salt, a burning waste, all its land shall not be sown, nor shall it sprout, nor shall any grass grow upon it" (Devarim 29:22). Furthermore, regarding the esrog, the concept of hiddur (beauty) is part of the essence of the mitzvah, which implies that the hiddur of this mitzvah must be the ultimate beauty. There is no deficiency in "You shall lack nothing in it" if the ultimate beauty is found in the "fat of the land," which is Calabria, Greece.

With respect and blessing in the style of the Rav, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, to receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

P.S.

Regarding what you noted concerning Calabria, Greece, and your reference to the Yerushalmi—I have said for some time that this explains the source of our Sages' teaching that "the fat of the land" refers to Italia of Greece. The difficulty is that when Yitzchak blessed Yaakov with "the dew of heaven and the fat of the land," the complaint was, "And for you, my son, what can I do?" (Bereishis 27:37). There was no choice but to give Calabria, Greece, which had not yet come into the world at that time, and thus it was not in his mind when he blessed Yaakov. This plot of land was submerged (according to the Yerushalmi), and at the hour when Shlomo married the daughter of Pharaoh, Gavriel descended and stuck a reed into the sea, and a sandbar rose up, and upon it a city was built, etc. (Italia of Greece) (Shabbos 56b). Later on, I found that this is written in the sefer *Damasek Eliezer* in the name of R' Heschel of Krakow.

It gave me pleasure that I had arrived at this conclusion.

Regarding what was written to explain that the aforementioned Calabria is from the lands of the Keini, Kenizi, and Kadmoni—see Bava Basra 56a; Rambam, Hilchos Rotzeach, Chapter 8, Halacha 4, and elsewhere.

## 6,294

B"H, 4 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Shlomo Chaim, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

I am responding to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Sivan, which included the *pidyon nefesh* that will be read at an auspicious time at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

In it, you write regarding the discouragement and complaints of a certain individual. Surely, everyone does what is within their power to improve the situation; one is only responsible for preparing the channel and the vessel, for my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and his father, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, stand and arouse Divine mercy for the matters of Tomchei Temimim wherever they may be, and especially in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily. A *tzaddik* decrees and Hashem fulfills. However, down here, there must be a readiness to receive the influence, for ultimately, we are in a physical world where every matter must also have a foothold in nature. Even regarding matters of Torah and the inner dimensions of Torah—which in their own right transcend nature—it is still written, "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do."

Regarding what you wrote about those learning the subject of *hora'ah* (instruction), etc.—after asking for forgiveness, as in many of your letters, you point out the undesirable details that exist in this matter without suggesting the solution. Even though identifying the undesirable is necessary and correct, it is understood that this is not the ultimate goal. The benefit of a doctor is not that he identifies the nature of the illness, but that he heals it. The matter you write about—that many of *anash*, and especially the younger ones, are learning what is necessary for education in the purity of holiness—is essential. Just as when my father-in-law, the Rebbe, arrived here, he took the finest *avreichim* and *bochurim* from the *yeshivah* and sent them to the outlying cities to teach Torah from the very beginning, the *alef-beis*, so too, and perhaps even more intensely, is the situation now in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily (though there, it concerns the *alef-beis* of Yiddishkeit, as the literal *alef-beis* does not require teaching). This is especially relevant to the existence of the *yeshivah*, for if there are no kids—meaning, students in *cheder* under the influence of Chabad—from where will the goats come—meaning, students for the Tomchei Temimim *yeshivah*? And this is understood.

It is surprising that you do not mention the preparations for the festival of Shavuos within the walls of the *yeshivah*, and also, based on what is known from previous years, the time has already come to discuss the vacation days. For several years now, there have been various opinions on this, and consequently, matters have not been conducted according to an organized plan, which naturally increases the damage. And this is understood.

With the blessing in the style of the Rav, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 6,195

B”H, 4 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs,
R’ Schneur Zalman, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the day of the Hilula of Rashbi, along with the enclosed list; thank you for the effort. May it be the will of Hashem that you be able to share good news in the true sense of the word—and not merely to put my mind at ease, nor only by way of finding merit, although that too is a lofty matter (as the Mishnah speaks of the greatness of finding merit, and as our Sages of blessed memory stated that the mitzvah of “love your fellow as yourself” is a great principle of the Torah). However, it is simple that good news can be even more complete through a change in reality, such that there will be no need for finding merit at all. As I said to you here, the *mara d’asra* (local rabbi) is responsible even for the thieves in his neighborhood, and it follows naturally that a Rav can influence them. This is surely and *kal v’chomer* true regarding *anash* and *temimim*, in whom our Rebbes invested their inner and essential powers. Even regarding those who joined later, our Sages of blessed memory have informed us, “Draw near to the oil and you will become oily,” as indicated by the precision of the word *hina*—that oil permeates everywhere, and this is well understood.

And since we are in the days of preparation for the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, regarding which it is said, “Do not read *charus* (engraved) on the tablets, but rather *cheirus* (freedom)”—freedom from all matters that cause confusion—may you share good news, true good, in a revealed and manifest way, in all general and specific matters. And from your upcoming birthday, may you add strength in this, for long and good years, with goodness in all its interpretations.

With blessings in the phrasing of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, the Admur, to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness.

***

## 6,297

B"H, 4 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with communal needs, a man of noble character, scion of a distinguished lineage, etc., R' Shazar [Shneur Zalman] may he live:

Peace and blessing! Although in my correspondence with anash in the Holy Land (may it be rebuilt and established) I inquire about you and receive regards from you, it is nevertheless somewhat surprising to me that I have not received a letter from you for a long time. However, I am confident that, as in the past, you are now doing everything in your power—and more—regarding all matters of Chabad in the Holy Land, and especially regarding Kfar Chabad.

In connection with the approaching time of the giving of our Torah, I would like to offer you my wishes in the phrasing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the receiving of the Torah with joy and with inwardness (*pnimiyus*).

As with all matters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, who was precise in his language just as he had heard from his father, surely this is also the case with the phrasing of the blessing for the festival of Shavuos.

The precision in this, one might say, is that when a matter is done with joy and not through coercion, it is also done with *pnimiyus*. This is why the Chabad approach demands both *pnimiyus* and joy together; moreover, even within the joy itself, it emphasizes the *pnimiyus* therein, for then the joy penetrates into the very core of a person until it rises and manifests outwardly as well. In truth, in any matter of culture, the sign of true culture is when it acts upon the *pnimiyus*, and not like the world, which places the point of emphasis on the external, such as matters of etiquette and the like. This is in contrast to Chassidus Chabad, where the central point is that the mind should rule over the heart, and since this must be done with *pnimiyus* and completeness, it is inevitable that this mastery will be evident in the external as well.

With respect and with a blessing for a happy holiday and for good tidings in both general and personal matters, for one is dependent upon the other.

***

**6,297**

**R' Shazar:** Shazar. Additional letters to him: see above 6,182, and the references in the notes there.

**The precision in this:** See also Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 4, p. 1307; Vol. 5, p. 272.

## 6194

[Days of Sefirah, 5718]

1) Regarding the future, he should hear [the counting] from someone else.

2) He should count according to the way he began (which, in my opinion, is the **primary** [method] for him), and for added measure, also as they count here, with a pause between them and not consecutively (as that appears like a falsehood, and also because it is the opposite of the concept of Sefirah, which is a clarification and not a doubt; therefore, it is questionable whether he could recite a bracha even if he were to count two Sefiros every day).

He should ask the Rabbis for a ruling regarding **Chag HaShavuos**, because according to the above, Chag HaShavuos (which is determined **only** by each individual’s counting and not by Beis Din) must be one day earlier **for him** (Shabbos and Sunday).

*6195*

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 7, p. 295. It is a response to someone who traveled during the days of Sefirah from Australia to the USA, crossing the International Date Line. On the first night of his arrival, he recited a bracha and counted as they count in the USA (even though he had already counted that Sefirah), and after a pause, he also counted as they count in Australia. From the second night onward, he recited a bracha and counted only as they count in the USA, and he asked if it is correct to do so.

See also below, Letter 6215, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 699*

B"H, Isru Chag Shavuos, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Brownsville-East New York Ladies Auxiliary for the
Lubavitcher Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding your upcoming annual luncheon on Sunday, 20 Sivan.

I hope that your esteemed members and guests will attend this seudah shel mitzvah under the impression of the Yom Tov of Kabbalas HaTorah that we have just celebrated, which should influence one’s life throughout the entire year.

For the Jewish woman, the Yom Tov of Shavuos holds a special significance, which is highlighted by Megillas Rus. The Megillah is not named after Boaz—the Nasi of the Jewish people at that time, the descendant of Yehuda ben Yaakov—but rather after Rus. Through this, the Torah emphasizes for all times and in all places the important role that the Jewish woman occupies when she recognizes her responsibility to her home, to her surroundings, and to the Jewish people, and utilizes her capabilities in that direction. She then builds the true Jewish home, "like the home of Rachel and Leah," and lays the foundations for the Geulah Shleimah.

It is unnecessary to emphasize that one of the primary tasks of the Jewish woman, and in our time and place in particular, is to help educate the young generation in chinuch hakasher al taharas hakodesh. The importance of your work is self-evident; however, I hope that your activities will constantly increase and expand in all respects, in quantity and in quality. The Ribono shel Olam does not remain in debt, and every addition in this direction will certainly bring an addition in the Ribono shel Olam’s blessings to each and every one of you and your families, may they live, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings.

#### ***699\****

Printed in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 8, p. 275, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

## 600

600

B”H, 9 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R’ Avraham Moshe, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 25 Iyar, which was received in due time, in which you write:

1) Regarding what is stated in Likutei Torah, Behar 41b, that there are a multitude of levels in the taanug of the neshamah, even though only Gan Eden HaTachton and Gan Eden HaElyon are mentioned in the holy sefarim—meaning that [the others] have not been revealed to us. You ask for the explanation of this.

The explanation is simple: Gan Eden HaElyon and Gan Eden HaTachton were revealed to the souls of select individuals even while they were in the body, similar to the four who entered the Pardes, and the Heavenly Yeshiva, regarding which it is said, "Who can argue with Rabbah bar Nachmani?" (Bava Metzia 86a; see Likutei Torah, end of Parshas Tazria). This is not the case for levels higher than these, which have not been revealed. This matter is also understood from what the Alter Rebbe writes in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 19, that the attainment of the prophets is no higher than the mochin of Chochma clothed in Binah; see Likutei Torah there, that this is the concept of Gan Eden HaElyon, the Sefirah of Binah. See also Tanya, Chapter 39.

2) Regarding your desire to explain that according to the Rambam, Gan Eden does not yet exist, but will only exist in the time to come.

Heaven forbid to say such a thing. There are numerous statements of our Sages written regarding Gan Eden in the Gemara and the Zohar, and the matter is also explicit in the Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah, end of Chapter 8.

3) Regarding your wonderment at the statement of the Alter Rebbe that an angel has a body, whereas the Rambam says that an angel is a separate intellect.

See Likutei Torah, Berachah 98a, that the aforementioned is based on the words of the Ramban, founded upon the verse, "He makes His angels spirits, His ministers a flaming fire," except that he specifies that this is spirit and fire in a refined state*.

On this occasion, I would like to remind you to keep the three daily shiurim—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which we have heard many times from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that they are suitable for every soul and a segulah for many matters.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

* The Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, in the maamar "Padah BeShalom" (the second) of the year 5667, brings both opinions and adds, "It appears that the intention of the Rambam in saying that they are a form without matter is that they do not have the matter of Asiyah, but rather a spiritual matter." Based on this, it is understood why Etz Chaim, Shaar 5, Chapter 3, brings that angels are called separate intellects and also that they have matter and form. See also Likutei Torah, Shelach 46a.

## V'Sha

B"H, 9 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, R' Shaul Yissachar, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

After a long interval, your letter dated the day of the auspicious date was received. At a time of favor, I will mention you and your wife, may she live, at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the contents of your letter, and may it be G-d’s will that you bring good tidings in this.

We have just emerged from the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah. Regarding this it is said, "Engraved (*charut*) on the tablets"—do not read it as *charut* (engraved), but rather *cheirus* (freedom); freedom from all matters that cause confusion. May you be blessed with good tidings in a way that is good, visible, and revealed, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for good tidings.

P.S.

Regarding what you noted in the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe, *siman* 494, in his commentary on why we say "the time of the giving of our Torah" on Shavuos—that it is because, according to our calendar calculation, Shavuos always falls on the 6th of Sivan, the time of the giving of the Torah—and you raise a difficulty: the Jerusalem Talmud, at the end of *Maseches Rosh Hashanah*, explains that it is written in the Torah that Shavuos is hinted at as the time of the giving of the Torah.

It is understood that your complaint is not against the Alter Rebbe, but against the reality itself. As the language of our Sages explicitly states, Shavuos sometimes falls on the 5th of Sivan. In that case, it is obvious that there is no basis to call it "the time of the giving of the Torah," even according to what the Maharal of Prague wrote (in *Tiferes Yisrael*, chapter 27), which you quote in your letter, since according to all opinions, the 5th of Sivan—the fiftieth day of the counting of the Omer—is not the time of the giving of the Torah. Our Sages explicitly said that it sometimes falls on the 5th of Sivan. Therefore, we must say that the statement of the Jerusalem Talmud is by way of *asmachta* (a scriptural support), and "there is nothing that is not hinted at in the Torah." In this same manner, one is forced to resolve a stronger difficulty than the one you brought, which is the one cited in many places: that the matter of the Two Loaves offered on Shavuos is the concept of "Come, eat of my bread"—the giving of the Torah—yet the Two Loaves are offered even when Shavuos falls on the 5th of Sivan.

## 633

B”H, 9 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs,
R’ Chaim Eliezer, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the days of *Hagbalah*, with the *pidyon nefesh* that will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding your efforts in fulfilling your *shlichus* of *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah*. It is surely obvious that if, prior to the first *Matan Torah*—that is, in the year 2448—there was preparation for it in various ways, then after *Matan Torah*, the primary preparation for receiving the Torah is through the dissemination of the study of Torah. This is in accordance with the statement, “He gives wisdom to the wise,” and in its inner dimension, this is the concept of *Sefiras HaOmer* in the year 2448. As is explained in the *Ran* at the end of *Maseches Pesachim*, in the name of the *Aggadah* of our Sages, that the counting mentioned there was an indication of the yearning to receive the Torah. From that *mishnah*, we have the proof that the essence of the counting is the yearning to receive the Torah, which is the actual study of Torah in the present. And this is easy to understand.

And since we are now coming from the festival of *Shavuos*, the time of the giving of our Torah—concerning which it is said, “Do not read *charus* (engraved) on the tablets, but rather *cheirus* (freedom),” freedom from all matters that cause distraction—may you be given good tidings in a revealed and manifest good in all the matters about which you write in your letter and in the *pidyon nefesh*.

With blessings for health and good news.

## 605

B"H, 9 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 2 Sivan, in which you write that you have been engaged for some time, but a lack of financial means to secure an apartment is currently delaying the wedding, and you continue that if the matter involved a sum of a few thousand liras, perhaps you could manage.

I have already written regarding this to many yeshiva *avreichim* and *avreichim* who are G-d-fearing in general, that it is a regrettable and poor custom among the *avreichim* in Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—to insist on living in a cramped location and paying exorbitant "key money" for an apartment. Consequently, they delay the time of the wedding for a significant period, which is the opposite of the ruling of our holy Torah, the *Torah Chaim*. After all, there are many places in Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—where apartments are not as expensive as mentioned, and the holiness of Eretz Yisrael exists in those places as well. Even regarding the people of Jerusalem, if it has been said that it is permitted to leave Eretz Yisrael for abroad in order to marry, then all the more so is it permitted to move from Jerusalem—may it be rebuilt and established—to other cities in Israel (even if one were to assume that the district in which you live is strictly within the boundaries of Jerusalem). If only this custom would finally change from one extreme to the other; then wedding celebrations would increase immediately, and a home would be built in Israel without such a distressing and completely unnecessary distraction.

On this occasion, I will awaken you to the great necessity in our current times to set times for the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus, and for this to be a *kevius*—as per the adage of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, the authority on the *nistar* of Torah, and the *Shulchan Aruch*, the authority on the *nigleh* of Torah—not only a *kevius* in time, but also a *kevius* in the soul.

Awaiting good news regarding all of the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,
Secretary

## 607

607

B"H, 10 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

You surely know that one of the fundamental principles of Jewish faith is the concept of the immortality of the soul—that the soul is eternal. Therefore, it is forbidden to increase mourning, Heaven forbid, beyond what is written in the Shulchan Aruch. It is obvious that if this interferes with learning in general, and specifically with learning with diligence and persistence, then it is clear that this comes from the Yetzer Hara, which tries to prevent every person from serving their Creator as instructed by our holy Torah. Furthermore, if, Heaven forbid, one listens to the enticements of the Yetzer Hara, it also causes the opposite of *nachas ruach* for the soul of the departed, since the Yetzer Hara is using her situation to weaken the person in their study of Torah; and this is easy to understand.

You must increase your diligence and persistence in the study of Torah, for this is the true *koras ruach* for the soul, and it is also the channel and vessel for receiving the blessings of Hashem for the entire family, for each person according to their standing and situation.

It is appropriate that every day, after the morning davening, you should recite the daily portion of Tehillim as it is divided for the days of the month.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 619

I spoke about this at a farbrengen, that the expression "Torah Temimah" (complete Torah) must be taken literally. If one detracts from its completeness, it is no longer Torah at all (at most, it is merely deep wisdom and intellect).

For the essence of **Torah** is instruction and a necessary command. It is not merely a notification that **if** you do not want a certain matter, you must reject another matter that is its cause.

## 616

B.H., 11 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R’ Yisrael Cohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of the 44th day of the Omer, in which you write regarding the rationale for creating a compilation from the holy Zohar, similar to the compilation of Ein Yaakov regarding the Shas, and you ask my opinion on this.

It is difficult for me to express an opinion on such a matter, because the approach of Chassidus Chabad is that the Zohar, and the books of the inner dimension of Torah in general, must be **studied** just like the study of the revealed dimension of Torah. This is especially true in our current era, where, in the words of the Arizal, it is a mitzvah to reveal this wisdom. Even for one who is unable, due to various circumstances beyond his control, to engage in the aforementioned study, there is still a spiritual benefit (*segulah*) in merely reciting the letters.

—Which is also similar to the revealed dimension of Torah, as is well known from the words of the Shelah in his introduction (the final section), that even the recitation of the names of the Five Books of Torah, the Prophets, etc., is a *segulah*.—

However, it is clear that one must strive as much as possible to disseminate the **study** of the aforementioned. See the startling words stated regarding the magnitude of the punishment for preventing this study—from which one can also understand the magnitude of the reward—in the introduction of R’ Chaim Vital to *Shaar HaHakdamot* (based on the words of the Zohar and the Midrashim of our Sages). From there, it is understood that it is specifically study in a manner of understanding and comprehension that brings the Redemption. This is in accordance with the well-known words of the Baal Shem Tov in his *Iggeres HaKodesh*, that when he was in the chamber of Mashiach, the response was: "When your wellsprings spread outward."

Despite all this, since any matter of disseminating Torah is a great thing, I do not wish, G-d forbid, to express an opinion that might discourage another direction. Therefore, you should turn to the great elders of Israel in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and consult with them regarding this.

Now, all of the above concerns others. But it is clear that regarding yourself, since you have been stirred by this matter, you must increase your fixed times for **studying** the inner dimension of Torah, as mentioned above, in a manner of understanding and comprehension. This is also brought in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, at the end of section 50, in the *Magen Avraham* regarding the study of the Oral Torah. It is also well known that the saying of our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya (who is the *posek* of the hidden dimension of Torah) and the *Shulchan Aruch* (the *posek* of the revealed dimension of Torah), is that there must be a "fixed time" not only in terms of time, but also in the soul, and that is the main thing. And it is understood.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, may he live,

Secretary

## 611

B"H, 11 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, in which you write your reasoning for visiting your country of origin, etc.

Generally, for some time now, such suggestions have not been acceptable to me regarding those born in that country—that is, those who were at some point their subjects. However, according to the information received recently, and especially from those who have done as you suggest and have gone there for a very short period, seemingly there is no room for concern. Therefore, it is worthwhile that you meet with Maru [name], who knows more details from his brother’s visit there in recent weeks. If the information regarding this is satisfactory, then, for good measure, you should present the matter before three of your friends from Anash, and through the power of the many, they should decide the matter for the good, in a way that is visible and revealed, especially since there is also the mitzvah of honoring parents involved, as you write. Perhaps it is better not to travel as a representative of any party, for although regarding yourself this is a merit, regarding those who are there, it is a matter of question, whereas if you travel as a private individual, it is different. It is also understood that you must ask your relatives there if they think the trip is advisable at all.

Although I have already written this many times, it has not yet reached the count of one hundred, as per our Sages of blessed memory, so I am repeating it once again: your attitude toward the matter of shidduchim is distressing and also puzzling, as I have written to you regarding this before. An approach to the entire matter can be in one of two ways: a) that there is a choice to do it or not, or at the very least to delay it for more time and more time, and consequently one chooses what is more comfortable; b) that the matter is necessary to be done, and as soon as possible, and the choice is only regarding how to implement the matter immediately. After asking your forgiveness, it seems that for the time being you have decided on the first approach, and from this have come all the complications.

And since we have just come from the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, regarding which it is said, "Engraved (*charut*) on the tablets"—do not read it as *charut* (engraved) but as *cheirus* (freedom), freedom from all matters that cause confusion—may it be Hashem’s will that you bring good news, in a way that is visible and revealed, regarding all that has been mentioned.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6163

B"H, 11 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Yehuda Zarchia Mordechai Leib Chaim, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter regarding the cornerstone-laying ceremony for the Yeshivas Chabad in Kfar Chabad, the place where Hashem has commanded the blessing. This strengthens the hope that you will continue to do everything in your power for the success of this endeavor, as I wrote in my letter for the aforementioned ceremony: with your money, your body, and your soul, as explained there.

Regarding the theme of the day, one should connect this to the well-known saying of the Baal Shem Tov that we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe: "Torah that is not accompanied by *melacha* (work) will eventually be nullified." *Melacha* here means *hisaskus* (engagement/involvement). Any Torah that is not accompanied by *melacha*—engagement in *ahavas Yisrael*—every piece of Torah that does not lead to *ahavas Yisrael* is not Torah. Seemingly, the words of our Sages are explicit: "Whoever says, 'I have nothing but Torah,' does not even have Torah" (see *Likutei Torah, Re'eh 23c*), meaning it must be accompanied by *gemilus chasadim*. However, the Baal Shem Tov’s teaching emphasizes two points: a) that this must apply to *every* piece of Torah, and b) that it requires *hisaskus*. As explained elsewhere regarding the concept of "business" (*esek*), this does not mean one who sits in his store waiting for someone to come and ask if he has merchandise to sell. On the contrary, he leaves his place, engages, exerts effort, and searches for where to sell his merchandise, persuading the buyer in all sorts of ways, etc. The analogy is understood.

Regarding our matter, when the great principle of the Torah—*ahavas Yisrael*—is established as the foundational basis, it will not be difficult at all to engage with one’s money, body, and even soul in the aforementioned matter, which is Torah and *ahavas Yisrael* combined.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and for the progress of your community in Torah and *mitzvos*, going from strength to strength.

## 614

B"H, 14 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter containing a *pidyon nefesh*, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you wrote about your weakness and the disturbances during your sleep, there is room to say that both matters stem from a lack of order and the absence of fixed times for eating, drinking, sleeping, etc. It is well known how much our Rebbes demanded, emphasized, and were particular about an orderly lifestyle, and they explained that a lack of order prevents success in the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos*. This is especially true in a case such as yours, which relates to your *meleches hakodesh*—the work of Zevulun that precedes Yissachar. Regarding the manner of this work, the verse states explicitly, "Rejoice, Zevulun, in your going out," and the rest is understood.

It would be appropriate for you to consult with a doctor to calm your agitation regarding these matters, and ask him to set fixed times for your eating, drinking, etc., and you should endeavor to keep to them as much as possible. May Hashem send His word, heal you, and strengthen you.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, for your success in your *avodah* in holiness, and for appropriate preparation to utilize the upcoming vacation.

## 616

B"H, 15 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the activists and friends of the Bais Rivkah schools in general, and the participants in the sixteenth annual banquet of the Bais Rivkah schools in particular,
May Hashem preserve them and may they live.

Peace and blessing!

I am writing this letter on the day when (31 years ago) the Rebbe, my father-in-law, was arrested in his struggle and for his work to uphold Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos, and to spread them—his struggle against the immense forces that sought to extinguish, Heaven forbid, every spark of Yiddishkeit. His extraordinary mesiras nefesh, however, was ultimately victorious, and he was liberated on 12–13 Tammuz.

The banquet of the Bais Rivkah schools is taking place in the interim, when the decision hung in the balance.

Although in free countries a Jew does not need to risk his life to fulfill his duty in spreading Yiddishkeit in general, and specifically in the field of authentic Jewish education for our youth, the situation of Yiddishkeit in many respects is no less critical than in those years. In the field of chinuch habanos—the kosher education of Jewish daughters—the greatest effort is especially required. And as is well known, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, dedicated much time and effort to create and expand the Bais Rivkah schools.

You have the great zechus to continue, uphold, and expand this great and responsible work. Now, however, the demand is much lighter—not mesiras nefesh, but mesiras haratzon. "Make His will your will"—you should desire to act in this with the same will as one desires one's **own** affair. The Bais Rivkah schools are **your own** affair.

I hope that you will, with a firm will and inner joy, give your fullest material support and also moral assistance to the Bais Rivkah schools, and influence others to do the same.

And the Ribono shel Olam will surely fulfill the promise and grant you success in your own personal and family matters as well, both materially and spiritually.

With blessing for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 6116

B"H, 17 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., Rabbi Dovid Tzvi, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

I was pleased to receive the news that this coming Sunday the *chanukas habayis* of your shul, Congregation Ahavas Torah, will take place.

May Hashem Yisbarach help the shul justify its name—not only in its internal affairs, as is fitting for a kosher shul and a house of G-d, but also, which is no less important, that the influence of the shul should be felt by the members and *mispalelim* even when they leave the shul. In truth, the real purpose and *kavanah* of a shul is that the closeness a Yid feels to the *Bashefer* during the time of *davening* and learning should permeate his daily life as well, even when he is occupied with matters of *parnassah* and the like; that in everything and everywhere, *ahavas-Torah* and *yiras shamayim* should be felt.

This is also the inner *kavanah* of the words of the Torah that are read this Shabbos, on the eve of the *chanukas habayis*: "At the command of Hashem they would encamp, and at the command of Hashem they would journey." Whether in a time of rest or in a time of wandering—when one wanders out of the shul and finds himself on the road—it should always be "at the command of Hashem."

I hope that there are certainly *shiurei-limud* in the shul, especially in the area of the daily matters that every Yid needs to be familiar with.

With blessings to all the *mispalelim* and members, them and their households, may Hashem grant them life.

## 6117

B"H, 18 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Yitzchak, may he live,

In response to your letters of the 9th and 13th of Sivan, in which you write regarding the name for the summer camp: I am certain that in the meantime you have received the letter from here proposing that all summer camps in all regions be called by a common name, "Gan Israel, under the auspices of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, [Name of] Branch."

In general, it is a matter that requires consideration whether to emphasize at every turn and in every matter that this is a Chabad project. For in many matters, the primary intention is to reach the widest possible circle and to influence them with pleasant words, and the aforementioned phrasing might intimidate certain circles of people. It is understood that it is not known here whether this is the case regarding the summer camp, but in any event, this point should also be considered when discussing matters of publicity and the like.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all that was mentioned, and for success.

## 617

B"H, 20 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn

The Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

Regarding your inquiry concerning the building plans in connection with the laying of the cornerstone—where there is an opinion to include an additional building, while others oppose this due to the additional expense:

This phrasing is not at all understood. After all, you are currently at the **beginning** of the fundraising process. The question of the aforementioned expense will only be on the agenda after a very substantial sum has been collected and a portion of the buildings has been started and completed. Only then will you have to decide whether to also include a hall, etc.! From this, it is understood that if including the hall in the plan makes the fundraising easier, etc., then it should be done.

## 619

619

B”H, 20 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 14 Sivan, in which you mention with concern that there were times you turned to me with your questions and did not receive an answer, and apparently this seems strange to you: To my mind, a yeshiva should be run by its own administration. Difficult matters should indeed be asked of me across the sea, but one should not begin by asking across the sea about matters that must be resolved locally.

This is the case regarding the content of your current letter. After all, every student is a world unto himself; one cannot set hard-and-fast rules or establish a single line of conduct for the entire group. Furthermore, regarding each individual student, one must take into account the influence this will have on the other students. [Indeed, the contradiction in your own letter is understood: you write that they are Chassidim and it is impossible to control them, yet there are the Laws of Torah Study by the Alter Rebbe, many letters from our Rebbes, and much more.] Rather, it is understood that each student must be addressed individually.

Regarding the practical application, as mentioned above, you must decide—not by discussing the group as a whole, but by discussing each one individually, while taking into account all the factors involved.

## 6220

B"H, 21 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Shmuel Elazar, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, the eve of the time of the giving of our Torah, in which you write the main points of your work—the work of Heaven—among the students of the Mechinah of Toras Emes.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you add courage and strength in this, and not only with revealed powers, and not only with hidden powers, but even with essential, primordial powers. For the matter and purpose of the giving of the Torah and the receiving of the Torah is in such a way that "the Torah and the Holy One, Blessed be He, are all one," and [it is] the superiority of Torah over the mitzvos, the essence of which is 1) **revelation**, 2) **the Essence** [in which is also the superiority of the wisdom of the Torah, "from wisdom it emerges," over the Keter, the matter of the mitzvos, "I have spoken and My will was performed"], as is explained at length in the maamar of this year's Chof-Daled Teves. And likewise, this is the case every single day, and as the expression "the Giver of the Torah" is in the present tense. Especially since the merit of the many assists him, and as our Sages of blessed memory said, "And from my students [I have learned] more than from all of them."

Blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 621

621

In response to your letter of Tuesday, Parshas Beha’aloscha.

The proposal that you accept a teaching position in a yeshiva ketana is correct, for surely your intention is toward an educational institution based on the purity of holiness. If so, this is both physical livelihood and spirituality combined. You will certainly be able to arrange your schedule in a way that increases your consistency in the study of Nigleh and Chassidus; there is nothing that can stand in the way of willpower. This is especially true when you also exert influence in your surroundings to strengthen and disseminate Yiddishkeit, for then the merit of the many assists you. It is surely unnecessary to elaborate that the purpose of this dissemination is as instructed in the parsha, “When you kindle the lamps” — these are the souls of Yisrael, as explained in Likutei Torah by our Rebbe HaZaken — and as instructed by Chazal, “until the flame rises by itself,” and the rest is understood.

## 622

B"H, 21 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—a *pidyon nefesh*—in which you write about your holy work and that you are living a life of hardship.

May it be the will of the *Ribono shel Olam*, Creator of the world and its Guide, that He expand your livelihood in material matters. And surely, on your part, you will expand your livelihood in spiritual matters—that is to say, through your efforts in strengthening and disseminating Yiddishkeit. As our *Mishnah* teaches, "Such is the way of Torah..." and regarding the "life of hardship," you will fulfill this through "hardship" in spiritual matters—namely, by fulfilling the instruction, "And let my soul be as dust to all," feeling the pain of humility and lowliness, as the *Mishnah* states, "Be exceedingly humble of spirit."

It is appropriate that you check your *tefillin* and the *mezuzos* in your home to ensure they are all *kosher* according to *halacha*. Furthermore, study a *shiur* in *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, especially on those days when you are engaged in *meleches shamayim*, the writing of *STaM*.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6,323

B"H, 21 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Regarding what you wrote, that it is currently difficult for you to daven with kavanah, even though you were accustomed to doing so in your home country in the past:

This is surely one of the enticements of the yetzer hara. Therefore, you should pay no attention to it at all; exert yourself in davening, and before davening—and also after davening—recite at least one chapter from the Tehillim of the "Sweet Singer of Israel," as it is well known that these are a segulah for such matters.

It is appropriate to have your tefillin checked, as well as the mezuzos in your home, to ensure they are all kosher according to the law. Furthermore, every weekday, before the morning davening, set aside a few coins for tzedakah.

## 6,424

B"H, 21 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, a *pidyon nefesh*, in which you write that in your opinion you are not succeeding in your business—or, to use your own words, that you have no *mazal*.

It is well known that our Sages have stated that "there is no *mazal* for Yisrael," for the Holy One, Blessed be He, who creates the world and directs it, **He** is the One who oversees each and every Jew regarding everything he and his household require.

From this, it is understood that you must increase your involvement in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, and that all members of your household should do the same. Through this, the blessings of Hashem will be increased in all your needs in general, and in matters of *parnassah* in particular.

Regarding *parnassah* specifically, the advice of our Sages is well known: "Salt your wealth so it may remain," which means that you should increase your giving of *tzedakah*, and distribute that *tzedakah* in many small portions. A propitious time for this is every weekday morning before *davening*.

It is also appropriate that you have your *tefillin* checked, as well as the *mezuzos* in your home, to ensure that they are all *kosher* according to the law.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 625

625

B"H, 22 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Wednesday, in which you write about your state of mind and your opinion that you are not capable of the matter, etc., and that you have almost reached a state of despair, etc.

It is unnecessary to elaborate that all matters contrary to the Torah are **within the power** of a Jewish person to nullify, and consequently, it is also **obligatory**. If, as you write, you have reached a state of despair and feel you are not suited for family life, this is nothing more than the enticements of the *yetzer hara*. Therefore, it is understood that you must fight against them in accordance with the will of the Creator [and furthermore, it is explained in the holy *Zohar* that even the *yetzer hara* intends that one should **not** listen to him; see *Zohar*, Part II, 163a]. The matter depends solely on your will; and if, according to your words, the matter is difficult, this does not mean that the matter is impossible, for "according to the camel is the load."

It is appropriate that you have your *tefillin* checked, as well as the *mezuzos* in your home. Every weekday, before morning *davening*, set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*, and keep up with the three daily *shiurim*—*Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*—which we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, navg"m, zya*, that they are for every soul and are a *segulah* for many matters.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

#### ***625***

**Not capable of the matter:** Supporting a family.

## 626

626

B"H, 22 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Monday, in which you write about your situation and how it seems you cannot overcome it, and the resulting consequences—how you left the walls of the yeshiva for a time and subsequently returned, and are now in a state of despair, etc.

It is understood that there are two points of wonder here: a) Why the surprise at the situation, after our Sages have already informed us, "Once twenty years have passed..." etc. b) Since we have been promised that "according to the camel is the load," and that "none shall be cast away from Him," it is **certainly** possible to overcome any situation that does not align with the command of our Torah, the Torah of life.

From the above, the conclusion is also understood: that you must occupy yourself with the appropriate energy in matters of shidduch, and as soon as possible, to build a home in Yisrael upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos. When one truly desires this, one naturally prays to Hashem from the depths of the heart for the success of these efforts, and does everything necessary in this regard—both through natural means, and primarily through and in relation to increasing one’s involvement in Torah and mitzvos. Through this, the *siyata d’shmaya*—which is the essential factor here—is magnified, as it is written, "And from Hashem comes a prudent wife." Then, one sees the success granted by Hashem even with physical eyes.

It is appropriate that you have your tefillin checked, as well as the mezuzos in your room. Furthermore, every weekday before morning davening, you should set aside a few coins for tzedakah, and establish fixed times for the study of Chassidus, which is the revelation of the inner dimension of the Torah in our current era. This should be done specifically in a manner of *havana v’hasaga* (understanding and comprehension), as this is also a rectification for the well-known sin related to the *mochin* (intellect), and the wise will understand.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

[May you also increase your strength] in the performance of mitzvos with *hiddur*, and in the matter that is the "spinal column" of all the mitzvos—namely, the *avodah* of *tefillah* (see *Likutei Torah*, *Balak* 70d), first and foremost, as this matter is explained in *Kuntres HaTefillah* and in many other places. ## 6208

B"H, 23 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of [date], in which you write regarding your relationship and current situation, as well as that of your children, may they live.

At a time of favor, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever you may need.

It was pleasant for me to read in your letter about your son’s interest, may he live, in the Chabad movement. It is my hope that you, the writer, are also interested in this, and that for both of you, this interest is in the proper order—meaning, it leads to action consistent with the teaching of our Sages, "Great is study, for it leads to action." Indeed, the Chabad approach and its conclusions are relevant to **everyone**, right down to the conclusions for daily life. As is well known, the saying of the founder of the Chabad Chassidic path—the author of the Tanya and the Shulchan Aruch—is that Chassidus is not for a specific circle, but is the inheritance of the entire nation; and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

I hope that you participate in the farbrengens of Anash that are held on the festivals and holidays in your area, and that you also have fixed times for in-depth study of the teachings of Chassidus. There is nothing that can stand before the will in this regard as well.

Surely your son, may he live, will also write here at the appropriate time, and please convey my regards to him. You should certainly also share with him the content of what is written above, as these words are directed to him as well. Thank you in advance.

With blessings for whatever is needed and for good tidings.

P.S.
In my secretariat, they do not write in Yiddish, which is why this response is in Lashon HaKodesh. However, you may continue to write in Yiddish in the future, as I am able to read that language.

## 6,329

B"H, 23 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter —which lacks the date of writing —you express much complaint and describe your personal situation in the darkest of colors.

It is surprising that for the moment, you have forgotten the words of Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Baal HaTanya —who rules on the hidden aspects of Torah—and the Shulchan Aruch —who rules on the revealed aspects of Torah—in his holy Tanya, that any matter of despair or sadness is among the enticements of the Yetzer and its stratagems to distract a person from the avodah of the Creator. It is also explained there that "according to the camel is the burden," and to every person is given the ability, the strength, and the possibility to walk in the path of Torah and mitzvos and to go from strength to strength.

Regarding what you wrote about a light and a lantern to illuminate the dark path—the path is not dark at all. For the matters are clarified in their details in the Shulchan Aruch and in the sefarim of Chassidus, and even regarding the most minute details about which the Yetzer casts doubt, there are many pieces of advice. Two primary pieces of advice are:

1) It is a well-known saying of the Mitteler Rebbe: to have a good friend with whom to speak about spiritual matters, for then there are two nefesh elokis souls against one nefesh habahamis.

2) The test of from which side the stratagem comes: in every matter that is beneficial and leads to actual avodah, any hindrance that may arise—even if the hindrance is from the most lofty thing—is only from the stratagems of the nefesh habahamis (see Hayom Yom, 23 Sivan).

May it be the will of Hashem that immediately upon receiving this letter of mine, you divert your mind completely from sighing and increase your actions.

And if, as the saying of our Rebbes goes, one action is better than a thousand sighs, then certainly several good actions are better than the order of sighs. In a short time, you will see that you were completely mistaken in the description of the situation in your letter, provided that you study with consistency and diligence, keep the order of the yeshiva, and influence your friends—may they live—to do the same.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
Surely you are aware of the three daily shiurim—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and in any case, you should keep them from now on.

## 630

B”H, 23 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Following a very long hiatus, your letter of 9 Sivan was received. At an opportune time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may his merit shield us, for each one according to their needs, as per the content of your letter.

Regarding what you wrote concerning your strained financial situation and the possibility of traveling abroad for a period of time on a mission for a religious department—from which it appears, according to your letter, that the salary would suffice not only for current expenses and livelihood, but would also leave funds to pay off previous debts:

From what I have heard, those who travel on such missions have the ability to conduct themselves in spiritual matters in accordance with their conscience. **If this is indeed the case,** and your wife, may she live, agrees to such a trip, it is appropriate to look into the matter. This is especially true since there is also spiritual sustenance involved, in that you would be able to disseminate Yiddishkeit in the spirit of our ancestors in the places to which you travel.

Regarding what you wrote about the disappointment you feel when observing the class in which you have invested so much effort: From what I hear from an outside perspective, it is clear that you possess talents in the field of education. Therefore, it is one of two things: either you are not evaluating the results correctly and are seeing them as less than the reality (which is better than you describe), or you are not utilizing your talents in the appropriate manner. Regarding this, it is said, "In a multitude of counselors there is salvation." In any event, you should utilize your talents in education, and it seems that the proposal in the first paragraph also involves matters of education in the place to which you would travel.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding your activities within the framework of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, although I am certain that you are involved in this as well. May Hashem grant you and your wife, may she live, success in all the above.

Regarding the news about the condition of your wife, may she live: May Hashem fulfill her days of pregnancy properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child at the proper time, in a healthy and easy manner.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above.

## 633

B"H, 23 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—without the date of writing—in which you write that you have been accepted to Camp Gan Yisroel, but do not provide details regarding this.

May it be the will of Hashem that everything works out in the best possible way for yourself and for the benefit of others, such that the camp lives up to its name, Gan Yisroel—"for you have striven with Elokim and with men"—and you will be able to [achieve] what is explained in Chassidus regarding this matter.

Regarding what you write about changing the *nusach* of *davening*: This is a correct matter. Since, according to what is explained in many places, it is possible to change from *Nusach Ashkenaz* to *Nusach Sefard*, or from *Nusach Sefard* to *Nusach Ari*, but not the reverse, your decision must be clear: that the change will be permanent, and from now on you will *daven* according to *Nusach Ari* (which, according to the Chassidic tradition, was selected by our Rebbe, the author of the *Tanya*—the authority on the hidden aspects of Torah—and the *Shulchan Aruch*—the authority on the revealed aspects of Torah—from sixty different versions).

Surely you are aware of the three well-known daily *shiurim* of *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*, and in any case, you should keep them from now on.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 634

B”H, 24 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R’ Efraim, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 20 Sivan. In the margins, you will find a response regarding the points raised in your letter.

It is surprising that you do not mention your commitment to setting fixed times for the study of Chassidus. Surely you have increased this since your last letter, as there is an explicit command to “increase in holiness,” especially regarding the study of Torah, which, as the holy Zohar states (Vol. I, 12b; see Torah Or by the Alter Rebbe, discourse *Mi K’Hashem Elokeinu* and its explanation), must be done in a way of *le’afsha lah* (increasing it). I am certain you will provide an update on this in your next correspondence.

With blessings for good news.

***

**In his notes:**

1–2: In Tanya, Chapter 39 and the beginning of Chapter 40, and in his Shulchan Aruch, Laws of Torah Study, Chapter 4, Section 3, it is explained that when the *kelipah* brings down one’s Torah study, one must perform *teshuvah* to restore and elevate it. In that case, one does not need to study the same material again, for this is the essence of *teshuvah*—to elevate the matters and the *nitzotzos* (sparks).

3: Regarding the manner in which Amram took back Yocheved and the reason for it, the Midrashim are divided: a) Through Miriam’s argument that “your decree is harsher, etc.,” from which it is understood that the reunion had to be public in order to nullify his decree, so that everyone would follow suit (Sotah 12a; Pesikta Rabbati, Chapter 43). b) Through a command from Above to Amram, done in private (Zohar Vol. III, 19a). The words of the Ohr HaChaim (Bamidbar 3:39) follow the holy Zohar, as he writes in his commentary.

***

## 6375

B"H, 24 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R' Elyakim Yehuda, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of Sunday.

At an opportune time, I will mention you and all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for each individual’s specific needs, in accordance with the content of your letter.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you that just as every Jew is an emissary of the Omnipresent, blessed be He, to disseminate Torah and mitzvos and thereby illuminate the darkness of the world—as it is written, "For a mitzvah is a candle and Torah is light"—how much more so is this the duty and privilege of one who has influence over the youth. Surely, among your students are many of the children of Israel; even though the subject matter you teach them is not directly related to Torah and mitzvos, you can certainly utilize your aforementioned influence for this vital matter. I refer to drawing the hearts of these students closer to our Father in Heaven by bringing them closer to the actual fulfillment of mitzvos, as it is written, "Fear G-d and keep His mitzvos, for this is the whole man." The merit of the many will assist you in succeeding in this endeavor. And according to the measure of the Holy One, blessed be He—which is "measure for measure," but multiplied many times over—you will be blessed by Hashem with an abundance of true, traditional Jewish *nachas* from your children, may they live.

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***6375***

**R' Elyakim Yehuda:** Geller, Suffern.

## 636

B"H, 24 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 2nd of the month, in which you write regarding the rationale for renting a suitable location to establish a Talmud Torah, and that you have already found a storefront suitable for this purpose, and you ask for my opinion.

Now, although according to the law of the Torah there is no issue of "encroachment" (*hasagas gevul*) regarding a Talmud Torah—and the law is ruled as such in the Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, end of section 245—in practice, it is relevant to first clarify whether there will be opposition in the neighborhood, in the event that there is another institution of this nature in the immediate vicinity. It is possible that this opposition could be expressed through undesirable means, and it is certainly possible to clarify this matter diplomatically.

Regarding what you wrote about your plan to organize a Talmud Torah for up to eighty students, since the neighborhood is home to hundreds of Jewish families—may they increase—it is understood that you must act with alacrity in clarifying all the details, so that by the time of registration or the start of classes, all these matters will already be arranged.

Regarding what you wrote about a license—it is understood that this must be clarified with the appropriate offices. May it be the will of Hashem, who feeds and sustains all with goodness, grace, kindness, and mercy, that He provide you with your livelihood and the livelihood of your household—may they live—in the best possible way for them, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6,337

6,337

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Eliyahu Leib, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

Following a very long hiatus, your letter was received, in which you write regarding the situation in the graduating classes of the school where you have merited to work in holiness, and that in your opinion, it is difficult to influence them to continue in Chabad schools.

Now, it is understood and simple that everyone who has the ability to do something in this regard must make the effort—with the necessary vigor—time and time again. Indeed, our Sages warned regarding such matters: "You shall surely rebuke" (*Hocheiach tochiach*)—even one hundred times. That is to say, even if, G-d forbid, the rebuke did not succeed the first ninety-nine times, there is still hope that the hundredth time will tip the scales for the good. The analogy is understood.

However, since this problem is a common denominator in all the schools of the Reshet, you should consult with the principals of the other schools. It would be best to request that the Reshet administration organize a joint meeting of all the principals, and following that, to enter into discussions with the administration of the Chabad yeshivos and Chabad institutions that could serve as a continuation for the aforementioned students.

At a time of favor, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and the merit of your involvement and efforts in the holy institution named after him will stand for you and your entire family for everything you require.

6. Another point, which is also most distressing, is that no attention is paid at all to what happens to the graduates of the Reshet schools after they finish—that is, whether they continue their studies and in which school, or if they are occupied with earning a livelihood and the like, and what their conduct is like. Rather, that is only a path and a means to make them Jews as they ought to be, to draw their hearts closer to our Father in Heaven, and to make them students of Torah and observers of mitzvos.

## 637

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 20 Sivan: It is surprising that you do not mention any progress in matters of Torah and mitzvos, especially in light of what I have already written to you—that if every individual Jew is commanded to fulfill the Torah and mitzvos in their entirety, then how much more so is this required of those serving in the army, from whom an added measure of holiness is demanded. Furthermore, their conduct influences the entire collective and its security, as it is written (Devarim 23:15): "For Hashem, your G-d, walks in the midst of your camp to save you and to deliver your enemies before you; therefore, your camp shall be holy, that He see no unseemly thing among you, and turn away from you." From the positive, you understand the negative: that one who does not conduct himself with holiness while in the army is, through this, opposing "Hashem, your G-d, walks in the midst of your camp," and is opposing the salvation and the delivery of the enemies before the army. And is there any betrayal more alarming to the security of the army than this?

It is my hope that these lines, though few in quantity, will suffice not only to influence his own conduct in accordance with the above, but that he will also influence all his friends—may they live—in this same direction. There is a presumption that propaganda [outreach] does not return empty, provided that the words come from the heart, for then they enter the heart of the listener.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
Surely you are aware of the significance of the festival of the Redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz. You should endeavor to participate in one of the farbrengens being held during these days in Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt speedily.
