## 6393

B"H, 15 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and accomplished, whose work is the work of Heaven, R' Chaim Shaul, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 11 Tammuz, with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you wrote concerning a candidate to teach a class at the Yeshiva Achat [Achei Tmimim] under your administration — it is understood that this depends on his talent, his ability to adapt to the students, and so on. However, as you wrote, there is an additional factor: he teaches at the Reshet school, which requires consultation with them, for it is obvious that one must not cause any detriment, Heaven forbid, to these schools.

May it be Hashem’s will that you bring good news regarding all the matters mentioned in your letter. Naturally and simply, this also applies to the state of the holy Yeshiva. It is surprising to read of the "low spirits" you describe regarding this matter on the eve of the days of redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz. Surely you are familiar with the interpretation of the verse, "And these days are remembered [and also] performed," and that the words of the *tzaddikim*, their actions, and the influence they generated endure forever. Even in this, the *avodah* must be carried out with joy and goodness of heart, which naturally brings a strengthening of *bitachon*. As was also recounted at the *farbrengen* of 12 Tammuz here, the words of the Rebbe Rashab to his son, my father-in-law the Rebbe, on 12 Tammuz 5655, explaining the *Iggeres HaKodesh*, "She girds her loins with strength" (*chagrah b'oz motneiha*). He concluded: *Oz* is *mesiras nefesh*; *mesiras nefesh* is "like this and not otherwise." This is how it must be regarding the Yeshiva, which must exist and develop: "like this and not otherwise." When one approaches it this way, the paths to achieve it are found more easily, as can be seen tangibly.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

6394

B"H, 15 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Tuesday, 13 Tammuz, the day of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael:

At an auspicious time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the resting place of the *baal hasimcha*, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever they may need, in accordance with the content of your letter.

Regarding what you wrote about your son, *shlita*, and how his sleep is very light and he wakes up almost every night, etc.:

There is room to suggest that he is lacking something in his nutrition. When this deficiency is filled, his nerves will surely strengthen, allowing him to sleep more restfully. Additionally, you should check the *mezuzah* in the room where he sleeps, and also be meticulous regarding the kashrus of the food and drink that he is given. Through all of this, his situation will surely continue to improve.

Since Divine Providence has placed you in the beautiful role of educating the children of Israel in education that is pure and holy, any increase on your part in this work—which is work for the sake of Heaven—will increase many times over the blessings of Hashem in your personal affairs and those of your family, *shichyu*. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings,

P.S.
You are surely aware of the three daily study portions—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which are appropriate for every soul and are a *segulah* for many matters. In any case, you should keep to them from now on.

696

696

B"H, 15 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the participants of the farbrengen of the auspicious days,
The days of redemption,
12 and 13 Tammuz, 5718, in the holy community of Toronto,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Shalom u’vracha!

I received with pleasure the letter dated the eve of the third day, the day that was doubled for good, 13 Tammuz, the day of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—also in deed, meaning the completion of the matter.

The greatness of the concept of the "seal" and the "completion" of a mitzvah is also understood from what is written in the Yerushalmi, Rosh Hashanah, end of Chapter 1, that it is greater than the matter of Shabbos; see there.

And it is also understood from its value regarding the concept of "for the good" (Rosh Hashanah 18a), and "the measure of good is greater than the measure [of punishment], etc."

And since these days, when they are remembered, are also re-enacted year after year, it is certain that the farbrengen at this time of favor has awakened a flow of the influences and draw-downs that were present in those days, in this present time.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that these draw-downs and influences continue throughout the days coming toward us for good, in spiritual matters and in material matters, and especially regarding the development of the holy institutions named after the one whose day we celebrate.

And all those who participate in farbrengens of this type are assured of an increase in blessing and success also in their own personal matters and those of their families, may they live and be well.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 6,397

B"H, 15 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 11 Tammuz, in which you write regarding your situation concerning the debts you incurred in connection with purchasing your apartment some time ago, and you are wondering how to extricate yourself from this distress.

However, it is understood that the initial thought you mention—to sell your apartment now and take a smaller one—is, aside from the fact that, as you yourself mention in your letter, it involves significant losses and, as experience has shown, does not actually resolve the distress of debt, is also—and this is the main point—that after living for some time in an apartment such as your current one, moving to a smaller apartment leads to a lowering of spirit, etc., and is obviously contrary to the movement toward the good in this regard, as our Sages of blessed memory said: "Three things broaden a person’s mind."

Therefore, you should endeavor to obtain a loan for a longer term and with more favorable repayment conditions. Through this, you will be able to slowly emerge from the distress that is on the outside and in external matters, without touching your apartment on the inside and the broadening of the mind associated with it, as mentioned above.

May it be Hashem’s will that you exert the necessary energy in the three things mentioned in the aforementioned statement of our Sages of blessed memory, regarding spiritual matters, as explained in Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 6 (22b): "A beautiful dwelling—his heart; beautiful vessels—his limbs; a beautiful wife—his soul." See there, for through this one attains true broadening of the mind.

It is my hope that you set fixed times for the study of the inner dimension of Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus, and specifically according to what is explained regarding the necessity of this in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 26, by our Alter Rebbe, the author of the Tanya (the authority on the hidden aspects of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (the authority on the revealed aspects of Torah), and in greater detail by his great-great-grandson, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in his book Kuntres Etz HaChayim. Among the foundations of their holy words are the words of Rav Chaim Vital in his introduction to Shaar HaHakdamos, where the language of the holy Zohar on this matter is also quoted.

You are surely aware of the three daily study portions—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that they are appropriate for every soul and are a segulah for many matters.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 6398

6398

B"H, 15 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
R' Yitzchak, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In addition to the telephone message I received regarding your safe return from your travels, I was pleased to receive your letter describing your trip in greater detail. It also contained the joyous news that you succeeded in retrieving the manuscripts of your father, of blessed memory. May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam that He fulfill your heart's desires for the good, that you may be able to publish them, and may He grant you success in your efforts, in accordance with what we discussed—that you should act with the greatest possible measure of influence upon our fellow Jews, so that they will desire to study such a sefer, for then they will also be able to understand it. For there is nothing that can stand before the will. This is not like in previous years, when it was necessary to bring such Jews from across the sea; rather, they should be natives of the place. There is a presumption that outreach—ta'amulah—does not return empty, especially when the outreach is combined with practical action.

Regarding what you conclude in your letter about the fear of our fellow Jews in the Soviet Union and the doubts regarding their future there: My faith is clear that an increase in Yiddishkeit in the United States, in the spirit of Torah and tradition, must inevitably influence them there as well. For regarding spirituality, geographical boundaries and distance do not create a barrier, especially since all of Klal Yisrael is a single entity. Just as we see in a physical body that when one adds strength to one of its limbs—and certainly to several of them—it must inevitably bring strength to the other limbs and vitality to the entire body, so too, when one adds vitality to the Yiddishkeit of the United States in matters of Torah—Toras Chaim—and in its mitzvos, of which it is written, "and live by them," and especially since the Yiddishkeit of the U.S. now constitutes the most important part of the entirety of the Jewish people, it must inevitably bring strength to all our fellow Jews wherever they may be, even those behind the Iron Curtain. This is especially true according to the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that even a partition of iron does not separate between Israel and their Father in Heaven.

In connection with the days of redemption, 12-13 Tammuz, which we have just passed, I am enclosing a booklet regarding those events. Although you are surely aware of the general matter, you will certainly find interesting details within it.

Thank you for delivering the seforim to our fellow Jews there.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all that was mentioned, and many thanks for the Sefer Sha'arei Toras Eretz Yisrael which was received just now.

I hope that your son and son-in-law, may they live, who were here, arrived home in peace.

***

**R' Yitzchak:** Rabinowitz.

**From your travels:** To visit Russia.

**Manuscripts of his father:** The Gaon R' Ze'ev Wolf Rabinowitz, author of the sefer "Sha'arei Toras Eretz Yisrael" mentioned below.

The manuscripts were later printed (Jerusalem, 5721) under the title "Sha'arei Toras Bavel."

## 6,400

B"H, 16 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings! Your letter regarding your learning with Mr. ... [may he live and be well] was received some time ago. Surely you are continuing with this, and also endeavoring to draw him closer to the matters of Chabad by having him participate in a farbrengen and the like—what is generally referred to as the "atmosphere of Chassidus." I look forward to hearing about the progress of these matters.

Regarding what you wrote concerning a study schedule, the general point here aligns with the teaching of Chazal: "in the place where his heart desires." Since the Torah is "broader than the sea," containing Halacha, Aggadah, etc., one can certainly find areas that his heart desires. It is surely unnecessary to explain that, in any event, one of the subjects must be the teachings of Chassidus Chabad, which is also "broad as the sea" as mentioned above, and there, too, he will find matters that his heart desires. You should also encourage him to read and study the sichos. His comprehension is surely more than sufficient for him to read them on his own; he should only bring difficult points to you, or to any of those who are engaged in the study of Chassidus on a regular basis.

Awaiting good news,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 610

610

B"H, 16 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It has been quite some time since I have received any letters from you. While there is a *limud zechus* (a defense) due to the tragic event that occurred, it is a well-known principle that while a *limud zechus* may justify a person regarding matters of reward and punishment, it does not accomplish anything in practice. It does not fulfill what a person must achieve for themselves, for their relatives and family, for those close to them in a wider circle, and ultimately for Yidden in general. Yet, this is the very purpose of every person and their true desire: not to be satisfied with being "exempt" (even in the best sense of receiving reward), but to strive to accomplish in every possible way, as mentioned above.

If this is true for everyone—even those who one might not know if they are capable of accomplishing anything at all—then it is *a fortiori* true for those who have already acted and have been seen to succeed, whose deeds have brought good to an entire circle of people in many areas. This is even more true, and to a much greater degree, in your case, as you have seen the positive outcome of your work in the field of N'shei Chabad.

I am writing all this because I assume that the lack of receiving news from you is due to a lack of involvement on your part. Therefore, I wish to add another point: the aforementioned event regarding the passing of your brother, the esteemed chossid, a man of fine character, etc., of blessed memory, should add to your efforts and activities, for all Yidden believe in the immortality of the soul.

This is so well-founded that even non-Yidden believe in the truth of this.

It is simple that one’s connection is not to the flesh and bones, but to the *neshamah* [which one sees through its effect on the body]. Therefore, the truth is that even after there is a change in the connection between the *neshamah* and the body, one can—through *maasim tovim*—cause *nachas ruach* to the *neshamah*. On the contrary, this happens to a greater and deeper extent, for the *neshamah* (after departing the body) no longer has the limitations of the body. Consequently, it is reached by matters that it could not have had while in the body due to the body’s restrictions, and it is even reached by actions performed in the most private of settings.

I hope that what has been said above will be sufficient to illuminate how your conduct should be now. If until now you have been involved in matters that are *tov l'shomayim v'tov labrios* (good for Heaven and good for people), there is now an added necessity not only to continue the work but to increase it in both quantity and quality—both in your own actions and in influencing others to act. This will cause the aforementioned *nachas ruach* to the *neshamah* of the departed.

May it be the will of Hashem that, coming now from the *Yimei HaGeulah* of 12-13 Tammuz—when we saw how Torah was victorious and nullified the darkness of *galus*—there should now be a continuation of a *geulah* from all matters that cause confusion. May you, with proper health and peace of mind, increase in good deeds to illuminate the darkness of *galus*. I hope that in the return mail I will receive good news from you regarding all that has been mentioned above.

With blessings.

## 6404

6404

B"H, 19 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished,
R' Avraham Zusha, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I acknowledge receipt of your *pan* along with the enclosure. May it be His will that for many more years you continue in matters of Torah and *mitzvos* in general, and in the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah* in particular—especially in accordance with the words of our *Rabbeinu Zakein*, the author of the *Tanya* (the authority on the *nistar* of Torah) and the *Shulchan Aruch* (the authority on the *nigleh* of Torah), regarding how the primary *avodah* of Hashem in these times, in the *ikvesa d'Meshicha*, is the *avodah* of *tzedakah*, etc., and that our Sages did not say "Torah study is equivalent to *gemilus chasadim*" except in their own times, etc. (*Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 9).

It is understood that even according to the *nigleh*, there is no difficulty with the statement of our Sages that "Torah study is equivalent to *gemilus chasadim*," for a *mitzvah* whose time is passing, or one that cannot be performed by others, takes precedence over Torah study (*Moed Katan* 9b).

And in the *ikvesa d'Meshicha*, "prices will rise," and "the son of Dovid will not come until the *prutah* is finished from the pocket" (see *Iggeres HaKodesh*, end of section 10).

May it be His will that the fruits of the aforementioned, which one eats in this world, should be drawn down and have an effect regarding the limbs in general, and specifically the level of the feet (*Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 9), of your eldest son, Yechiel, may he live. May you also share good news regarding him.

With blessings for proper health and for good news in all the aforementioned.

## 675

B"H, 19 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings! ...Regarding the matter at hand, it is my understanding that in the very near future, the examinations will take place for those studying in the teachers' course under the direction of the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' M.A. Zilberstrom, who is also among them. It is certainly unnecessary to urge him, but I intend for him to pursue this with the appropriate vigor. The main thing is that he should acquire all the necessary knowledge and be able to utilize his talents in *hashpaah*, having also obtained official certification. For the initial approach requires the testimony of a diploma, and only afterward does the listener recognize the merit of the *mashpia* even without the diploma. And since it is known here that, according to the law, one who holds *semichas rabbanus* also elevates the level of his authority, it is my hope that he will not neglect this either. Especially since, if I recall correctly, we once spoke about the fact that if he were to have official certification, he would be able, in time, to utilize his talents in *hashpaah* for the dissemination of Yiddishkeit, as mentioned above; for a *rabbanus* diploma will evoke a greater sense of respect among the listeners, and this is well understood. May it be His will that he brings good tidings regarding all of the above.

With blessings for good news,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 616

B.H., 19 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Monday, 12 Tammuz—the day of the liberation of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—in which you confirm receipt of my letter and write further details regarding your son and family, may they live: At a time of favor, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in accordance with what you have written.

Regarding what I wrote—that one can rectify the past by influencing one’s grandchildren, may they live—it is understood that this is one of the primary ways to do so. However, one should not be content with this alone. Following the directive of "Love your fellow as yourself," one must help all those who are involved in this work in any way possible, and generally ensure that the concept of *taharas hamishpachah* penetrates wider circles.

It is well known that the power of *tikkun* and *teshuvah* not only removes punishment, Heaven forbid, but actually adds success, as is known from the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, that *baalei teshuvah* are greater than *tzaddikim gemurim*.

I hope that you are keeping the *takkana* of reciting the monthly *shiur* of *Tehillim*—as the *Tehillim* is divided into the days of the month—each day after *davening* in the morning. Also, [that you are reciting] the chapter of *Tehillim* corresponding to your age (meaning, from the day of your *bar mitzvah* one begins reciting chapter 14 each day after *davening*, and each subsequent year, the next chapter of *Tehillim*).

With blessings for good news regarding all of the above, and regarding your participation in the *farbrengen* of 12 Tammuz, which surely took place in your city. May it be His will that this serves as a beginning for good news.

## 6157

B”H, 19 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the day of redemption, 13 Tammuz, as well as the telegram that preceded it. I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the contents of your letter.

It is surprising that you have acted contrary to the customary and logical practice—that after visiting here, there should be more frequent correspondence than before. In your case, the trend is the opposite: since your return from here, you write much more rarely than before, and your letters are much shorter. Yet, the reason that others would surely inform [me of news] existed even then. It is well known that the Rebbe Maharash said: "It will come from another place, but you will lose the merit." And his son, the Rebbe Rashab, concluded: "To be worthy of being a messenger from the Holy One, blessed be He, to do a Jew a favor"—and surely, good news is included in the principle that is a great rule in the Torah: "Love your fellow as yourself."

With blessings for an expansion of mind and livelihood.

#### ***6157***

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 12, p. 205; completed based on the secretariat’s copy.

## 6,408

6,408

B"H, 19 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following the longest of interruptions, your letter of 26 Tammuz was received, as well as the telegram that preceded it. The fact that the interruption was so long is astonishing. If you would argue that the reason for the silence was that there was "nothing new," then for members of Chabad, this wonder is even greater. To speak wittily: since there is "nothing new under the sun," the task of *anash* is not the toil that is "under the sun," but rather something higher than that—see *Tanya*, beginning of Chapter 40. As the saying of the *Tzemach Tzedek* is known: "We are the workers of the day, to create light."

May it be the will of Hashem that, since we are coming from the days of redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz—the redemption of our *Rebbe Nasi*, the head of Israel, and "the body follows the head"—each and every one of us will be redeemed immediately from all matters that cause confusion, and will be able to serve Hashem with joy and a glad heart.

With blessings for good news.

## 610

B"H, 19 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

R' Dovberish, may he live.

Shalom and blessing! After a very long hiatus, your letter of 15 Tammuz was received.

## 6412

B"H, 21 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the distinguished Chassid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs,
R' Gershon
May he live, and his wife, the Rabbanit Gessie, may she live.

Peace and blessing! In response to your two letters, and surely in the meantime you have received my letter responding to your previous ones.

Regarding your notification of the certificate for the pension, may it be the will of Hashem that the adage of our Torah, the Torah of life, be fulfilled in this as well: "This, too, is for the good."

As explained during the farbrengen, this is even higher than the concept of "Everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good." The latter implies that the results will be good, whereas "This, too, is for the good" means that the matter itself will also be good, not merely that the results will be good. This is understood from the events brought by our Sages, of blessed memory, in connection with the aforementioned. Based on this, it is also understood why the first adage is in the Holy Tongue (representing *pnimiyus*—internal dimensions), whereas the second adage is in Aramaic (representing *achorayim*—external dimensions), not in the revealed [state], and this is easy to understand.

With blessings for good tidings, in good health and with peace of mind.

#### ***6412***

**R' Gershon:** Chen, Haifa. Additional letters to him: see above, Vol. 13, p. 369, and the references in the footnotes there.

**As explained:** See also above, Vol. 14, p. 220, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 614

B.H., 22 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter dated 15 Tammuz, in which you write regarding what you experienced during your tenure in the rabbinical position in the holy congregation in Eretz Yisrael...

May it be the will [of Hashem] that the success which has shone upon you until now will awaken within you even deeper inner strengths and even greater energy to continue in your holy service, to instill in all the members of your congregation the absolute truth of the word of Hashem: that they are a "kingdom of priests and a holy nation." The essence of this is that throughout the entire day and night—not only during davening, the study of Torah, and the performance of a mitzvah—a person (for you are called *adam*) is serving in the holy. For it must be that "in all your ways know Him," as is explained at length by the Rambam in his *Yad HaChazakah*, in the Rambam’s *Shemonah Perakim*, and cited as a halachic ruling in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim*, section 231. And it is a certainty that words which come from the heart enter the heart of the listener. The heart is the king over the limbs, ruling over them and influencing them to conduct themselves in accordance with its instructions; and the wise will understand.

Regarding what you wrote, that the aforementioned was achieved only through struggle, friction, etc.—this is indeed the order of our world. As the *Etz Chayim* phrases it—cited in *Tanya* (end of Chapter 6)—all the deeds of this world are difficult and evil, and the wicked prevail in it, etc. [And yet, it is specifically in this world that the Torah was given, for "it is not in heaven," and it is precisely through this that the argument of those who received the Torah—"Do you have an *yetzer hara*? Did you go down to Egypt?"—was overcome.] However, at the same time, we have been promised that the truth, the good, and the holiness will stand and emerge in open victory. Since the Ribono shel Olam desired to have a dwelling place in the lower realms, His will shall certainly be fulfilled. This depends only on the actions of the person, who is the "emissary of the Place," as the Mishnah states: "I was created to serve my Maker," to establish a dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed, in this world of ours—a dwelling place adorned with beautiful vessels, etc., similar to what is brought in *Tikkunei Zohar*, *Tikkun* 6 (22b): "A beautiful dwelling—his heart; beautiful vessels—his limbs; a beautiful wife—his soul." Through this, all matters are drawn down into the portion of the world that belongs to this person. See also *Tanya*, Chapter 37, on how this is a preparation and a part of the general redemption of the entire world.

From all of the above, it is understood that what you wrote at the end of your letter—that your personal life does not satisfy you, etc.—is not consistent with what was stated above. For the **purpose** of man is to serve his **Maker** and fulfill His will. One who has been gifted with the power to influence others—this is his primary task. For "love your neighbor as yourself" is a great principle in the Torah. And since one mitzvah leads to another, and especially in the aforementioned communal work, our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe says (*Torah Or*, at the beginning) that through *tzedakah* (and your work is indeed *tzedakah* that gives life to both the soul and the body), one’s mind and heart become a thousand times more refined. This means that even if, as you write, the time at your disposal has decreased compared to before—as you complain in your letter—the success increases a thousandfold. According to what is explained in the *Hagahos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, this is a literal thousandfold, not an exaggeration. That is to say, in one hour you succeed in what previously required a thousand hours.

Regarding what you wrote about the study of Torah, my words have already been stated: it is **most** necessary in our current era to study the *halachos* required for daily life, for, alas, there is a staggering lack of knowledge in this area, in all circles, even in the highest levels—and the wise will understand. Likewise, it is necessary to study the weekly *parsha* and to participate in the study of the *Shas* that is completed each year by a group. All of the above is a matter that is relevant to every soul.

With blessings for good news in all the above, with true peace of mind.

## 615

B.H., 23 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn

To the Honorable Rabbi, the Honorable Chossid, G-d-fearing, meticulous in mitzvos, etc.,
Rabbi Sh. Y. [Zevin]
May he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings! I acknowledge with thanks the receipt of your book, *Ishim V’Shitos*, second edition. I have also received news during this time of your participation in the farbrengens in Jerusalem, the Holy City, and in Kfar Chabad, and of the renewal of the Tanya shiur that you have begun.

May it be the will of Hashem that for many more years you will increase soldiers for the Torah—the *Torah Temimah*, both the revealed and the hidden—and in such a way that they will be *temimim* (whole/complete). This is the true meaning of *temimus*: that in the revealed, it should be evident that it is one with the hidden, and in the hidden, that it is one with the revealed. According to what is explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Epistle 26, and in many other places, the matter of *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah* (spreading the wellsprings outward) is not merely a mitzvah that is time-dependent, but is a necessity. And as we see tangibly, it is a vital necessity, for it concerns the fulfillment of the mitzvos regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them" in actual practice—especially in our current era, which is full of trials, concealments, and hiddenness. This is as our Sages say regarding the footsteps of Moshiach—that due to our many sins, these have been fulfilled not only in a way of subtlety and the subtlety of subtlety [similar to what is explained in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, end of Chapter 7, that the matter of *avodah zarah* also includes turning a blind eye to *tzedakah*, anger, or one who possesses arrogance, and many similar things in the Gemara], where one might think it possible to fulfill the obligation of the words of our Sages mentioned there. Rather, the generation has not merited to the point that the promise descends level by level until, etc.

May it be the will of Hashem that there be fulfilled what was explained in the *maamar* that was repeated at the farbrengen of 12 and 13 Tammuz this year, regarding the interpretation of our Sages: "He raises the destitute from the dust"—when they descend to the level of dust, and "your seed shall be as the dust of the earth," then the time has arrived for the fulfillment of the prophecy, "and you shall spread out" (*u'faratzta*), and the "Breaker" (*ha'poreitz*) shall ascend before us—this is our King Moshiach.

With appreciation and blessing for good tidings in general matters and in private matters—and it is understood that matters of physical health are included among private matters, and indeed take precedence, as per the words of the Rambam, *Hilchos Deios*, end of Chapter 3.

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.

A question recently came to my attention regarding someone who crossed the International Date Line in the middle of the days of *Sefirah*, and consequently, a day was added to his count. He was in doubt regarding the counting and the blessing during the days of *Sefirah* after crossing the date line.

I pointed out to him that the question is even more relevant regarding his *Chag HaShavuos*. In my humble opinion, regarding his counting and the blessing: although there is no doubt that he must continue specifically according to his own count—for it is absurd to double a single count—and he can also recite the blessing, nevertheless, "from being good, [one should not refrain from doing better]," etc. He should hear the blessing from someone who is here and intend to fulfill his obligation through him [since the blessing is on the essence of the mitzvah, not on the number of the day; therefore, there is no contradiction in the fact that for the one reciting the blessing it is the thirtieth day, while for the listener it is the thirty-first].

Regarding *Chag HaShavuos*, since it does not depend on the days of the month and does not depend on a *Beis Din*, but rather occurs immediately after the completion of the count of seven weeks—and the aforementioned person has counted 49 days according to the Torah, and they are complete for him—he must celebrate *Chag HaShavuos* according to his count, i.e., one day before the local residents here. However, because of the bewilderment of "the world," I instructed him to find at least two more *morei hora'ah* (halachic authorities) whose opinion would also be as stated above.

Since you are in contact with your work on your books, and it is apparent that you have reviewed many *Sheilos U’Teshuvos* from the *Acharonim*, surely if you find any discussion on this, please inform me, naturally with the addition of your own opinion. Thank you in advance.

By the way, regarding this same matter, concerning the blessing of one who is in doubt as to which day of the *Sefirah* he is on, which was also brought in your book *Moadim L'Halacha*, chapter on *Sefiras HaOmer*, where you quote the opinion of the *Sheilos U’Teshuvos Dvar Avraham* that one should not recite a blessing on a doubtful count because the very essence of the counting is "clear knowledge of the day," and there is no room to recite a blessing if there is doubt—I found something similar in the periodical *Shaarei Tzion* [apparently the year 5695 (the title page is missing in this copy that I have)], mentioned in the name of Rabbi R. Y. Weingrad. While this is logically sound, it is absolutely contradicted by this reasoning: if you say that this is the law, then in every place where the messengers did not arrive (at the time when they would sanctify the months based on visual sighting), they never fulfilled the mitzvah of *Sefiras HaOmer* (properly), and it is obvious they did not recite a blessing over it, for on the sixteenth of Nissan they did not yet have clear knowledge, as they celebrated the second day of *Yom Tov* because of the doubt, and consequently they could not recite a blessing. And regarding the counting itself—they **did not** have clear knowledge. Consequently, the "completeness" of **all** 49 days is also lacking. How is it possible that such a puzzling matter is not mentioned in the *Shas*? I do not have the *Sefer Dvar Avraham* at hand, and I do not know if he addressed this point.

In the second edition of your book, I saw the addition regarding Rabbi Meltzer, of blessed memory. Some time ago, it was told to me that during the years he lived in Jerusalem, the Holy City, he engaged in the study of Kabbalah, and not only that, but he did so in *chavrusa*. I am interested to know if this rumor is true, and if it is true, it is a pity that he did not mention this in his article. For even if it is not directly related to the subject of your book *Ishim V’Shitos*, it is well known the saying of the *Tzaddik*, the *Chossid*, the *Gaon*, etc., Rabbi Hillel of Paritch, when they asked him the reason why he was so careful in mitzvos, and he answered: "So that when I do everything, a word of Chassidus might be attached to it," and the rest is understood.

## 6,516

6,516

B.H., 23 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, man of spirit, G-d-fearing, man of action, possessor of good character traits, etc., R’ Nissan, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha! I received with pleasure your book, *HaTorah VeHaOlam*, Part Three — regarding the topics of the day, the coming weeks and months.

As with your previous work, so too with this one: words of *hisorerus* toward Hashem, His Torah, and His *mitzvos*. May it be the will [of Hashem] that these words achieve their effect in revealing within the hearts of Jewish men and women the source of living waters that lies within their own souls. This is in accordance with the intent—that this source be revealed in thought, speech, and action in daily life, for this is the whole of man.

Happy is the portion of one who causes this and brings it about, in the manner of the well-known interpretation in *Chassidus* regarding the inner meaning of the *Mishnah*, "Two are holding onto a garment." The "garment" is the *ohr makif*, the spark of goodness found within a physical object. Two come and perform a *mitzvah* with that physical object, and thereby they refine the spark, redeem it from captivity, and bring it out of exile. Each of the refiners claims that it was through his *avodah* that the spark was refined and that it is entirely his, etc. [See *Maamar* "Rabbi Omer," 5700, and in the *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, end of Chapter 12].

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you succeed in all that was mentioned, and that for many more years you will strengthen the forces to permeate the world with the light of Torah—a complete Torah, both the external and the internal, the Torah of truth without changes and without compromises. For it is the same in every place and at every time, until the Torah and the world are unified. And may the declaration of the first Hebrew be fulfilled: "Abraham was one," for his *avodah* was: "And he called there in the name of Hashem, the G-d of the world (*E-l Olam*)," and not "the G-d of the world (*E-l HaOlam*)," for they will recognize in the world that there is nothing else besides Him (*ein od milvado*). [See *Likutei Torah*, *Tavo* 42d, 43c].

With respect and blessing for health, and for your wife, may she live.

P.S.

With astonishment mixed with pain, I learned of the results of the meetings between the representatives of the young [rabbis] and the leadership of the *Vaad HaRabbanim*, which did not lead to actual unity. In our times, the lack of unity increases division. My pain and my astonishment are founded and understandable based on the *sicha* with the esteemed Rabbi, etc., Bik, may he live, who surely conveyed to you the main points of it. The primary point is that the aforementioned young men are **for the time being** hanging between heaven and earth in a spiritual sense. They are under pressure, specifically from the "left," which demands that they descend to the earth—and not just to physicality, but to materialism. And, unfortunately, the pressure is not only in promises for the future, but also in threats for the present and the very near future. If they are not integrated as soon as possible into a framework that will at least protect them from descending downward, it is difficult to be held responsible for the consequences.

There is another point regarding the *Vaad HaRabbanim*: surely it is known to anyone who observes the situation that its influence and control over the public are not increasing; on the contrary. The recent conventions of the young rabbis prove this. When there is a possibility to increase the influence of the *Vaad HaRabbanim* and weaken those who fight against its influence (some openly, and even more behind the scenes), this possibility is being pushed away with one's own hands. It seems that at least some of the reasons are not *lishmah*.

## 6,517

B"H, 25 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

The Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, Tel Aviv Branch
May Hashem preserve them and keep them alive.

Peace and blessing! I have been informed that in about two weeks, a global gathering of representatives of Israeli youth from several countries will take place in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) [I believe the exact time is 28 Tammuz, in Jerusalem (may it be rebuilt and established)]. It is appropriate that you consult with one another immediately regarding how to utilize this opportunity for the affairs of Chabad, and specifically for the central point of *hafatzas hamaayanos*. I believe I have written many times that such opportunities are *hashgacha pratis* to influence many countries and many lands with incomparably greater ease. After all, those who are in need of *birur* are being gathered and brought to a place where the one who can perform the *birur* is located; one only needs to awaken them from their slumber and sleep so that they utilize this opportunity to its fullest.

What I wrote above regarding sleep and slumber is in connection with the fact that some time ago, there was a global gathering of Bible scholars and scientists, where it is simple to assume that each of them would have been interested in learning about the Chabad approach, or at the very least, receiving some of its books. Yet, it appears that all the *anash* activists in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) did absolutely nothing—a total zero—to utilize the aforementioned opportunity. I searched for ways to find merit for the absolute lack of activity in such matters (which require no contemplation to recognize the potential hidden within them), and I found only one merit: *az es iz kaynem nit ayngefallen trachten vegen dem* (it simply didn't occur to anyone to think about it). And the merit for this very fact is understood from the other end: The explanation from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is well-known—how is it that a maidservant or a bondwoman can arrive at the logic of the Tannaim, Amoraim, Rishonim, and Acharonim—the most profound logic—which, on the face of it, is completely beyond her level? It is because when a matter is truly relevant, even a maidservant or a Canaanite slave can reach, with their most limited intellect, the depth of the intellect of the aforementioned. And from the positive, you hear the negative, as in all matters of Torah...

May it be the will of Hashem that our arrival now, from the days of redemption of 12 and 13 Tammuz, *zol durchbrechen* (should break through) even the double and redoubled darkness mentioned above, with kindness and mercy specifically.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6,818

B"H, 25 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 21 Tammuz, regarding the puzzling question of whether you are obligated, for the reasons you write in your letter, to offer yourself as a *korban* for, etc.

It is surely understood that a *shidduch* and marriage are not at all a matter of bringing a *korban*, but rather for the purpose of building a *binyan adei ad* in Yisrael.

Regarding the proposal you write about, you should present the matter before three of your friends who are in that location, at least one of whom should be a *rav*, so that the matter may be understood also according to *din* regarding *chazakah*.

It is my hope that since you conclude your letter by mentioning that you are a descendant of the great Admurim of Poland and Galicia—and you even name some of them who belong to the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, which is the teaching of Chassidus—you surely have *kevius itim* in the study of this Torah. It is known that the inner meaning of *kevius itim* is not only in time, but—and this is the main point—*kevius itim* in the *nefesh*. Even those who in the past had arguments that it was impossible to reveal and publicize this wisdom, many of them already recognize the **necessity** of this study. See regarding this in *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Rebbe, the author of the *Tanya*—the *posek* in the *nistar* of Torah—and the *Shulchan Aruch*—the *posek* in the *nigleh* of Torah—*Siman* 26, and in the *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* by his great-great-grandson, Admur Moharashab *n.e.*, and elsewhere. It is understood that the command of our holy Torah to "increase in holiness" (*ma'alin b'kodesh*) applies to this as well.

It is appropriate that you have your *tefillin* checked, and also that you keep, *bli neder*, the three well-known *shiurim* of *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

6119

6119

B"H, 26 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned individual, engaged in communal affairs, R' Yitzchak Dovid, may he live.

Peace and blessing! In response to your letter of 11 Tammuz, the eve of the day of redemption—the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael.

At a time of favor, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may the merit of the tzaddik protect us, in accordance with the content of your letter.

Regarding your questions:

1) Regarding the erecting of a tombstone: In the Diaspora, there are those who follow the custom of waiting twelve months, while in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, the custom is to erect it after thirty days. In my humble opinion, there is no need to wait a full year, especially in Eretz Yisrael, where the custom is as mentioned above. Indeed, even in the Diaspora, many challenge the custom of waiting a year, as is explained in various places (Minchas Elazar, Vol. 3, sec. 37; Kol Bo on Avelus by Rabbi Grunwald, and others).

2) Regarding the name Mendel: It is well known that the name Menachem Mendel has the same gematria as Tzemach Tzedek. I have followed this practice myself since my youth, writing "Mendel" in accordance with that gematria. However, it is simple that every person may hold their name as they wish, and it depends on their signature, and in many cases, also on how they request to be called to the Torah. In your specific case, one should certainly look at the signature and act accordingly.

3) Regarding what you wrote about the number of Kaddish recitations: It is correct that there should be sixteen Kaddish recitations in a twenty-four-hour period. One should connect this with what is explained in the holy Zohar (Vol. 1, 62b) regarding the function of Kaddish for an hour and a half, according to which sixteen Kaddish recitations correspond to the twenty-four hours of the day. As for your question of how this is possible on Shabbos and the like, it is surprising, as you seem unaware of our custom to study Mishnayos after every prayer—i.e., three times a day.

4) The custom for a mourner to lead the prayers on Friday night for *Mizmor LeDovid* is not our custom. In general, regarding the customs of Yahrtzeit and Kaddish, please consult the *kuntreisim* listed below.

5) Regarding the study of Mishnayos: What I have heard is to use the letters of the name of the deceased, but not the names of their parents.

6) Regarding your question about a repeated letter in a name: Does one chapter suffice for all the repeated letters, or is a number of chapters required equal to the number of letters? Although I have not found this explicitly stated, based on the explanation that the name is the conduit connecting the soul to the body—from which it is understood that every letter of the name is a part of that conduit, similar to what is explained in *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, beginning of Chapter 12—it follows that one should study a separate chapter for each letter. However, in my opinion, one need not be particular about using different chapters; one may repeat the same chapter several times.

7) Regarding your question as to which is preferable: the letters of the name or study in order: These are separate matters. The letters of the name, as mentioned, relate to the connection of the soul and body, and as explained in other places, to the drawing down of the soul from its source. Study in order, however, is a mitzvah that is fulfilled completely by completing a tractate or a *seder*, etc. It is worth noting the discussion in *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah* there regarding the supernal power and the general vitality, etc., especially since the order in the Oral Torah is itself Torah, as is understood from the words of our Sages in many places: "A Tanna comes from such-and-such a tractate."

8) Regarding what you wrote about reading from the Torah and being called for *Maftir*: I heard two instructions from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding this when I was in mourning after my father, may his memory be for a blessing. However, for a private reason, I only read from the Torah at Mincha on Shabbos and on Mondays and Thursdays.

9) Regarding what you wrote about the order of study: In my opinion, two types of study are especially appropriate for such a time: the study of Mishnayos, which are the "letters of the soul," and the study of the inner dimension of Torah, the "Tree of Life." Through this study, one will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth, and "Hashem will wipe away tears from all faces," etc., as explained in the words of Moshe Rabbeinu in *Ra'aya Mehemna* (Zohar Vol. 3, 152b). The inner dimension of Torah is the Tree of Life, as explained in the holy Zohar and as the verse implies: after the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, death was decreed upon the world, and one would "reach out his hand and take also from the Tree of Life and live forever." The virtue of our Torah—the Torah of life—is that the matter is made to accord with the supernal will, such that one transforms even the Tree of Knowledge into the Tree of Life, turning darkness into light and bitterness into sweetness.

10) Although you do not mention it, you should certainly set aside charity before the morning prayer and also before the Mincha prayer, as is understood for weekdays. This, too, is especially relevant to the aforementioned, based on the teaching "Charity saves," etc., the inner meaning of which is that even after passing, it is a form of salvation. This is also understood from the Jewish custom, which is Torah, that when mentioning souls, one mentions the matter of charity, as is known from our Sages in *Midrash* on the verse in the end of *Parshas Shoftim*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above. It is surely unnecessary to remind you of the halachic ruling of our Torah—the Torah of life—that "whoever is lenient in matters of mourning, the halacha follows him," and see also *Orach Chaim*, end of the laws of Lulav.

## 6220

B"H, 27 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn

Mrs. Shoshana, may she live,

Peace and blessing! After a long interval, your letter from 15 Tammuz was received. Its content concerns the inscription for the matzeivah. You explain that there is a family tradition regarding the matzeivah of the deceased’s grandfather, but you do not mention the text of the inscription on the matzeivah of the deceased’s father, the son of that grandfather. It is understood that the deceased surely took part in composing it, and if it was done according to that tradition, it serves as a precedent for the matzeivah of the deceased as well.

However, in my opinion, one should add to the title of the deceased’s father the term "HaRav HaChossid," and also "he was among the greatest Chassidim of Admur Moharash and Admur Mohar Shalom DovBer, zatzuklaleh nivga"m ziya." My intention is that the names of the Nesi'ei Chabad, the Nesi'ei Yisrael, be mentioned on this matzeivah, and this is easy to understand.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that your letters from here on be only regarding matters of joy, a complete joy.

With blessings for good tidings,

P.S.
You do not mention in your letter the state of your health or that of your family members, may they live—surely this is a sign that things are in order.

It is understood that the text of the inscription must be with the agreement of the descendants, may they live, of the deceased.

And surely—and this is the main point—they should contemplate the matter of the matzeivah: this is a stone monument, and the inscription is engraved upon stone. But the descendants of the deceased are a "living monument," and their actions and conduct in their daily lives (not only on the day of the Yahrtzeit and the like) are the "living inscription" upon that living monument. The text of that inscription depends upon them, and them alone. In the phrasing of our Sages, of blessed memory: "A son is the leg [extension] of his father."

## 6,221

B"H, 27 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in communal needs, R' Gedalya, shlita,

Peace and blessing! ... Regarding what you wrote concerning the text in *Shaar Rosh Hashanah v'Yom HaKippurim* by the Mitteler Rebbe, that the trousers of the Kohen Gadol reached down to the heels.

Some time ago, this was brought to my attention. In searching through the manuscripts, the aforementioned maamar has not yet been found. However, I did find a maamar from the Tzemach Tzedek on these same topics, which also explains the matter of the garments, and there, the words regarding the length of the trousers are not present.

Regarding what I said about the precision of the phrasing, "One should not stand to pray except from..."—as opposed to the phrasing (which is seemingly **the simple** style) "One stands to pray from..."—this addition emphasizes the precision of the matter and its necessity. I brought a proof that this phrasing is sometimes found, yet it is still only *l'chatchilah* (the ideal way), as is the ruling of the Rambam (*Hilchos Tefillah u’Birchas Kohanim* 8:2). I am surprised at your honor, for on the contrary, it was from there that I saw it—based on the words of the Tosafos in that sugya (*Menachos* 83b) and the *Lechem Mishneh* and *Kesef Mishneh* (in the first explanation) on the Rambam there.

And even if you were to say it is as you wrote, within the category of *l'chatchilah* itself there are many levels, similar to the concept of a mitzvah performed according to its standard, *mehadrin*, and *mehadrin min hamehadrin*. The addition mentioned above to the simple phrasing adds, at the very least, to the level of *l'chatchilah* (as is written explicitly in the *Kesef Mishneh* in the second explanation—which is apparently the source from which your honor is raising the difficulty).

In truth, there is no need for proofs regarding a matter that is simply the **literal** interpretation of the words. As the distinction mentioned above, the phrasing "One stands to pray from..." does not contain a special emphasis on what happens if the stated condition is not met, whereas the phrasing "One should not stand to pray except from..." clearly contains such an emphasis. And this is simple to understand.

It is my hope that you also gathered in your camp during the days of 12 and 13 Tammuz, the redemption of our Rebbe, the Nasi of our generation, the head of Yisrael—and the body follows the head—that he may redeem each and every one of us, speedily and immediately, from all matters that cause distraction, both physically and spiritually, so that you may be able to serve Hashem with joy and a glad heart.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

***

**6,221**

**R' Gedalya:** Hertz, Sydney.

**Shaar Rosh Hashanah v'Yom HaKippurim by the Mitteler Rebbe:** 33a. See also *Maamarei Admur HaEmtzai, Devarim*, Vol. 4, p. 139.

## 622

B"H, 27 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter arrived with some delay, and I have noted its contents regarding the possibility of arranging a shidduch for your son, may he live.

I have observed among the avreichim here and elsewhere that when one begins to speak with them about such matters, it immediately leads to a distraction of the mind, and very often it is to no avail, as a significant amount of time passes before a suitable suggestion is found and the matter comes to fruition. Given the young age of your son, may he live, this concern is all the more pressing. Therefore, in my opinion, once you feel the time has come to consider marriage in a practical sense, and there is an actual suggestion at hand, then you should consider whether to propose it to him immediately.

## 6,423

B"H, 27 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs and is a man of many accomplishments, a person of fine character, etc., R' Aryeh Leib, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I learned from the press that you have reached the milestone of seventy years. I send you my blessing that Hashem may lengthen your days and years in goodness and pleasantness, and that you may utilize the talents with which you have been gifted by Divine Providence, and utilize your influence to their fullest extent, in accordance with the Torah principle that "Yisrael, the Torah, and the Kudsha Brich Hu are all one." This should be expressed not only in theory, but by drawing this into your day-to-day life.

Just as everyone acknowledges that the Creator is the true and absolute reality and that no compromises are possible in this regard—for logically, either one believes that "He is, and there is nothing else besides Him" with complete faith, or if the faith is not complete, it is not this matter at all—the same applies to the Torah, in which no compromises are possible. Likewise, regarding the Jewish people: although it is known from the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that "a Jew, even if he has sinned, remains a Jew," this does not mean that the sin is of no consequence or that the Ribono shel Olam makes compromises or is lenient. Rather, one must perform teshuvah, and "he will return and be healed."

Since, from the age of seventy onwards, you are entering the years of *gevurah* (strength), may it be His will that you be like an overflowing spring, fighting the battle of our Torah—which grants strength and *gevurah*—without fear, for there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With respect and blessing,

#### ***6,423***

**R' Aryeh Leib:** Gelman. Another letter to him—above, Vol. 4, 885.

## 6,224

B"H, 27 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Tammuz, in which you write that you are thirty years old and have not yet married, and that a match has been proposed with a young woman whose father’s name is the same as yours, and you have become doubtful regarding this in connection with what is explained in the Will of Rabbi Yehudah HeChassid.

Since you have been delayed so long in marriage, and provided the young woman in question is G-d-fearing and will conduct herself as is fitting for the daughters of Israel (strictly observing the laws of family purity, keeping Shabbos, and the kashrus of food and drink, within the entirety of the mitzvos of the children of Israel), then it is appropriate that you assemble three rabbis who are authorities in halachic ruling. They should issue a ruling that an additional name be added for you, and you should be called to the Torah and sign your name using this additional name as well. It is best that the additional name be placed first. In this way, the aforementioned Will does not apply to this situation at all, provided that the conditions are made after you have been established with the new name for thirty days.

It is understood and simple that in any case, and especially in your situation where you are in need of a special blessing, you must be strong in the observance of Torah and mitzvos as required, and increase in this, as our Sages said: "We increase in matters of holiness." Through this, the blessings of Hashem and your success will be increased, especially regarding the matter of building a home in Israel, an everlasting edifice built upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos.

It is appropriate that you have your tefillin checked to ensure they are kosher according to the law, and that every weekday, before the morning davening, you set aside a few coins for tzedakah.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 6225

B"H, 28 Tammuz, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, honorable, and distinguished one, who performs his work as a task of Heaven,
R' Yaakov Yosef, may he live, Shochet u'Bodek.

Peace and blessing! In response to your letter of 23 Tammuz.

Regarding what you wrote about submitting an application for citizenship once again: in general, this is the correct thing to do. However, according to the words of our Sages, the time is not appropriate at the beginning of the month of Menachem Av, but rather [it should be done] on the day [of the 15th] or after the 15th of Av.

Regarding what you mentioned about the month of Cheshvan: it is my impression that it is not the custom among anash to hold a wedding during this month.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything about conveying the regards from here to anash in London. It has been discussed many times, and it is also mentioned in several stories of Chassidim, that on a trip such as yours here, one must make an extra effort to ensure that it also brings benefit to the many. Especially in your case, this does not require great effort or exertion; organizing a farbrengen and coming to share points from what was discussed in the maamarim and sichos involves no exertion at all. On the contrary, it is satisfying even to the nefesh habehamis, for after all, after having been together for several years with the nefesh elokis, it is impossible that the very proximity would not have an effect upon it. This is especially true when, each according to his standing and situation, the nefesh elokis within him exerts effort regarding the nefesh habehamis within him, and particularly among the talmidei hatmimim. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 6228

B.H., Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Ben Zion, known as Dr. Dinur,

Shalom u’vracha,

I am writing to acknowledge with thanks the receipt of the offprint of your article, "The Historical Character of Russian Jewry and the Problems of Researching It," which you sent to me through our friend, R. P. Althoyz, on Erev Rosh Chodesh Tammuz. It was received during the days connected to the days of redemption, 12-13 Tammuz, when my father-in-law, the Rebbe, was liberated. It is well known how much his life was dedicated to Russian Jewry (and through it, to the entirety of the Jewish people), to the extent that even upon his arrival in Poland and the United States, this remained one of the primary threads in all his activities, including his work regarding the Judaism of the United States and the Jewish people as a whole. The influence of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in his communal work as an individual—who was, in the terminology of Chassidus, the "head" from which vitality is drawn to the "limbs"—was profound.

The events of those days, in particular, set a turning point in the course of the spiritual life of the Jews in Russia and of the Jewish people as a whole.

I am aware that according to various Marxist and scientific theories, it is not accepted that an individual can influence the collective in a way that determines significant change. But in our era, one should not be shaken when encountering a "miracle." Especially regarding the Jewish people—each one of them is a brand plucked from the fire, a living miracle.

Furthermore, the results of science in the last few decades have led to the conclusion that there is no absolute **certainty** regarding the "natural" laws that have been invented or established, but rather only **possibility**. Moreover, one cannot judge the whole by the individual, meaning that a law applies to the **majority** of cases and does not necessitate that it be so in **all** cases; there can be an exception to the rule that is the opposite of the rule. Parenthetically, it is a wonder that in those very countries where Marxist theories prevail—where the aforementioned assumption that the individual cannot determine the collective should be widespread—in practice, in many of them, a cult of personality has spread to the greatest degree, to the point that in certain countries, a tyranny reigns that is completely contrary to reason.

By way of a pleasant thought, considering that the institutions and affairs of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, exist now in all corners of the world, there is no room at all to say that his sun has set. For the sun is always in its reality, merely passing from one place to another, from one hemisphere to the other; and since his works are alive and existing everywhere, his light shines and acts constantly.

I believe you mentioned or wrote to me that you are engaged in writing Jewish history and in a new publication of some of his books and maamarim. My hope is that your *girsa d’yankusa* (the learning of your youth) will stand by you—namely, those years when you were in close proximity to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and in the environment of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim. There is nothing that is completely nullified, and all the more so regarding matters connected to our eternal Torah, as it is illuminated inwardly by the light of Chassidus. Surely, their impression will be evident in the books and compositions that are about to emerge from your pen.

By the way, it is a wonder what you wrote on page 109 of the aforementioned booklet and in the note there regarding the editions of the Tanya that appeared in Russia in eight editions, etc. Please see the indices printed as an addendum to the Tanya, published by Kehot. [Sent to you in a separate package from the latest printing].

With respect and blessing.

***

As is the way of the Jewish people to add a personal touch to every matter, I take the liberty of commenting on the content of your article, even though it is seemingly outside my field. It is this:

When speaking about Russian Jewry as a unified matter and including within it—as is done in the aforementioned article—all those territories that were under the Russian government, this is, in my opinion, a contradiction in terms. For many parts of the Judaism within this territory were not united at all; there was only a mechanical connection between them—that is, they were under the jurisdiction of one government. What is more relevant is the affinity, and in many matters more than an affinity, to the Judaism in other countries. For example, the Judaism of the Caucasus, which until the middle of the First World War lived a life unto itself, not within the framework of Russian Jewry at all. Likewise, the Judaism of Poland, which, in addition to the above, had a shared life in almost all matters with the Judaism of Galicia, and not with the Judaism in the other parts of Russia. According to the above, it is understood that on several points that you discuss in your article, one cannot generalize and judge from the data of one part of Russian Jewry regarding another part of Jewry when speaking of those parts that had only a mechanical connection, as mentioned above.

And of course, it must be added that precisely after the period you discuss—I mean after the beginning of the First World War—many of the partitions between the aforementioned parts of Jewry were removed through the expulsion of the Jewry of Poland and Lithuania into the interior of Russia. On the other hand, there was the absolute cessation of relations between the Jewry of Poland and the Jewry of Galicia. Similarly regarding the Judaism of the Caucasus, in which, incidentally, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and especially his father, the Rebbe, played an active role. At the beginning of the First World War, and to a greater extent at its conclusion, they sent several shluchim to the Judaism of the Caucasus and strengthened ties with them in religious matters, and through this, also in several economic matters.

Furthermore, the most central place in recent periods for Russian Jewry and Jewish history in general was occupied by its influence outside the borders of Russia. In this, it is primarily distinct from the Judaism of the residents of Morocco, Turkey, Hungary, and the like. However, regarding life on the spot—or in other words, internally—the Judaism of Hungary and Galicia, as well as the Judaism of Morocco and others, were at the highest level, and in some points perhaps higher than Russian Jewry, especially at the beginning of the period you discuss. Therefore, regarding the four fundamental phenomena you explain in your article as having determined the special place of this Judaism in the life of our people, they require study and research into the history of the aforementioned parts of Jewry—Hungary, Morocco, etc. Surely, in some points, and perhaps even in an important part of them, they were at a level no lower than in Russia, and perhaps even more developed. For example, the foundation of life rooted in the tradition of the generations and crystallized in its way of life, etc., in which our aforementioned Sephardic brethren are more distinguished than the Ashkenazim.

Based on the above, in my humble opinion, one should add to the three character traits of Russian Jewry a primary and fundamental trait: the influence and involvement in the life of the Jewish people in all parts of the world, whether in writing (printing matters), personal contact through shluchim, immigration, and the like.

## 6,429

6,429

By the Grace of Hashem, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Dr. Reuven Meir,

Shalom u’Bracha,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 23rd of Tammuz, and I thank you for the trouble you took to describe the patient’s condition...

According to the greatest experts in this field here, and based on many cases they have treated, if the illness has been chronic for several years and all treatments have already been attempted without success, their opinion leans toward surgery.

It is understood that it is up to you to decide whether the case in question falls into the aforementioned category, as the patient is under the care of the institution you direct.

With respect and blessing,

In accordance with the directive of our Sages, of blessed memory, "And you shall be clean before Hashem and before Israel," I am also responding to the second matter in your letter and the tone you directed toward me, expressing surprise at how I wish to exert influence from across the ocean, etc., and concluding that "Israel is indeed a new country, but..."

It is obvious that I have no desire to infringe upon the honor of Eretz Yisrael or the personal honor of anyone, especially those who are unknown to me. However, regarding the lobotomy treatment that has been introduced in recent years, as with any scientific matter—and especially any medical treatment—it is impossible that there would not be changes from year to year in the doctors' approach to this treatment, as well as in the method of its execution. As the number of cases examined grows, these changes will become more grounded and, presumably, will persist for a longer time. Surely, you are aware of all this—much more so than I.

Based on the above, it is understood that for any treatment that cannot be reversed later, such as surgery, one must—as you yourself phrased it in your letter—use it only after **every** other attempt has been made. That is to say, only in a case where it is absolutely necessary and it is impossible to wait, even in a situation of "sit and do nothing." Therefore, we have seen that even in the United States, this surgery is performed sparingly, and even then, only after several years of treating the patient. In the vast majority of cases where a lobotomy is performed, it is because there was no possibility of superior supervision (due to a lack of financial means). And after all this—and this, too, is surely known to you better than to me—even if the surgery is successful, although you mention in your letter that "almost all returned to normal life," such cases where they return to normal life here are extremely rare, if such cases have occurred at all.

To use your own phrasing, that you do not "want to be a partner to murder," in the aforementioned surgery, it is not merely a surgery on the body, but also a surgery on the mental life of the patient. If you will, it harms a part of their mental life—meaning that there is also a partial murder involved, at the very least, except that in a situation of no choice, one chooses the lesser of two evils.

All of the above explains my position regarding the aforementioned treatment, which is based on the instructions of our Sages, of blessed memory, in our Torah, the Torah of life, that even for a temporary rescue, one must make every possible effort. This is especially true in the case of mental illness, where many matters are still unclear, both regarding the causes of the illness and the method of its cure, and even more so in recent years, where fundamental treatments and major changes are introduced in this field quite frequently. Therefore, every effort is worthwhile to postpone the lobotomy treatment for as long as possible—until there is absolutely no other choice.

I ask for your forgiveness for writing to you in a field that is your own. May it be the will of the Healer of all flesh, Who performs wonders, that you succeed in fulfilling your role completely. And the merit of the many will assist you.

## 6330

B"H, 1 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings! A strange rumor has reached me that someone has raised a hand against you in connection with your holy work in chinuch. And as I have been informed, the one who raised his hand claims to be acting out of zeal for holiness, etc.

Surely your spirit has not fallen, for in the inner dimension of the matter, it is not against you that he raised his hand (though even then, the words of our Sages regarding the nature of one who raises a hand against a fellow Jew are well-known). In this specific case, he has effectively raised his hand against me. And if you wish to say more—at its core, it is against me, and you are merely my shaliach. And just as the aforementioned did not make an impression on me to weaken the work in general, my hope is strong that it will not cause any weakness in you regarding your work; on the contrary, you will add strength and hisorerus in this. May Hashem grant you great success, and through this, may you be granted an increase in everything you need, from soul to body.

With blessings for good news regarding the above.

## 6,432

B"H, 3 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 26th of Tammuz.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever you may need and for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires in all the matters about which you write.

Regarding what you wrote concerning thoughts that hinder your concentration while learning: it is well known that one of the pieces of advice for this is to learn from inside the text. Even when you are deeply engaged in thought and analysis, the *sefer* or *kuntres* should remain open before you on the subject at hand. The same applies to *davening*.

Regarding what you wrote about thoughts concerning your future: it is well known that the text of *Birchas HaMazon*, which is from the Torah, states: "He who sustains the entire world in His goodness, with grace, with kindness, and with mercy." From this, it is understood that by increasing your consistency and diligence in the study of Torah and the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*, the blessings of Hashem are increased in general, and this includes the matter of arranging your affairs favorably when the time comes for that. The verse states explicitly: "If you walk in My statutes" (and Rashi explains, based on the Sifra, that this means you must be *amelim*—toiling—in Torah, specifically toiling) "and keep My *mitzvos*... then I will give..."—and so on, with all the blessings mentioned in that *parsha*.

I trust you are aware of the three daily *shiurim*—*Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*—and in any event, you should observe them from this point forward.

With blessings for good tidings.
