## 635

635

B”H, 5 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write regarding your son, may he live.

As I understand it, the real reason [for his difficulty] is that it is hard to be under supervision all day and to be connected to a set schedule, for as it appears, he did not have this at home. From this, it is understandable that one must see to it, through ways of pleasantness and ways of peace, that he remains there until the *zman* of studies begins. It is certain that as time goes on, it will be easier for him to adjust, and this can have a lasting effect for the entire year—to be able to accept discipline and integrate into a schedule, not only during school hours, but also at home, which for a child is the most important thing.

Psychologically, one must also accept that once he knows that it has been decided that he must stay there, he will also make up his mind to stay. Conversely, it appears from your writing that through telephone conversations, he hopes to free himself from the camp and from discipline in general.

Regarding what you write about the medical treatment—since this is a new matter, hopefully it will be done with the utmost caution, meaning that the check-in every few days should be the minimum of "a few" and not the maximum.

May it be Hashem’s will that regarding all of the above, you should report good news, and together with your wife, may she live, in good health and with peace of mind, you should have true *nachas*—which is Chassidishe *nachas*—from your children, may they live.

With blessings for good news as mentioned above.

6356

6356

B”H, 5 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings! I read with astonishment in your letter to... as if, G-d forbid, there is any *kapida* (resentment) toward you, etc.

It is understood that there is no basis for this whatsoever. As I have written to others, I see no benefit in *kapida* at all. It may be that at times there is pain caused by undesirable conduct, or from the fact that one is not utilizing the *bracha* and *hatzlacha* that Hashem gives. It pains the heart that matters could be better than they are, and yet, due to trivialities, one fails to utilize the *brachos* of Hashem.

From this, it is understood that *kapida* is something entirely the opposite, and certainly something more than *kapida*. However, the pain mentioned above has a place in your matter, but it has no connection to reading into my letter things that were not written, or to the idea that the response is being delayed because of this (which, in most cases, is due to many preoccupations).

By this, I mean what I believe I have already written to you: the matter of the *sheitel* in your home. As I have already hinted to you, the situation does not change, and certainly is not rectified, by turning a blind eye to it—and before Hashem, all hidden things are revealed. The pain in connection with this is understandable, according to the holy *Zohar* (cited in the *Acharonim*, *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim*), Part 3, 126a: “It is required for a woman to be covered with the modesty of the home” (from which it is understood how much more so outside the home), “and if she does so... her children will be elevated in stature, etc., and she will be blessed with everything—with blessings from above and blessings from below, with wealth, with children, and with children’s children.” See it there carefully.

I wish to emphasize once again that there is not a shred or trace of a matter of *kapida* here, but rather frustration and pain. This is only magnified when one considers the so-called *mesiras nefesh* that the desired conduct requires, compared to the loss involved—and even more so when taking into account the place where you are currently located, where such good conduct can influence many Jewish families to begin to emulate it and go from strength to strength.

May it be the will of Hashem that, ultimately, each of us will see how the *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* bestows *bracha* and *hatzlacha* in both material and spiritual matters, and that we make all the necessary *keilim* to receive and utilize this *bracha* to the fullest extent.

And coming from the month of *Geulah*, the month of Tammuz—the *Geulah* of our Rebbe, *Nasi* of our generation, and “the body follows the head”—may each and every one of us be redeemed immediately, in a complete and speedy manner, from all matters that cause confusion, and may we be able to serve Hashem with joy and a glad heart.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 6337

B"H, 5 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings! In response to your letter of Thursday.

At an opportune time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for each one’s respective needs, as appropriate to the content of your letter.

Regarding what you wrote about the difficult financial situation of your father, may he live and be well: surely he has several acquaintances and friends in his place of residence, and he should consult with them regarding what type of livelihood is suitable for his current situation. However, together with this, he should engage in matters that increase Hashem’s success and blessing. I am referring to the advice of Chazal, "Salt your wealth by decreasing it"—to increase in tzedakah and to divide the sum to be given on many occasions. The most auspicious times for this are every weekday before morning davening. Furthermore, every day—including Shabbos and Yom Tov—after morning davening, he should recite at least one chapter from Tehillim. It is even better to follow the monthly cycle, as Tehillim is divided for the days of the month. If it is possible in their location, it is proper that your mother, may she live and be well, should give every day—at the very least—a piece of bread or some other food to a poor person in need of it. This is a form of tzedakah where the benefit is immediate, and through this, the blessing of Hashem, may He be exalted, comes sooner, as per the words of Chazal (Taanis 23b).

Regarding what you wrote about your father’s, may he live and be well, ailment and the medical treatment and its results: he should seek the opinion of a specialist in the field, for in recent years it has been discovered that the treatment can affect the kidneys, and therefore it is being replaced and modified.

Since you are the one bringing the request and are drawing closer to the good path, you should increase your own involvement in Torah and mitzvos. Through this, Hashem’s blessings will be added in what is needed for you and in the fulfillment of your request, especially regarding what was mentioned above.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
It is proper to have the mezuzos in your father’s home checked, as well as their tefillin. And you (the writer) should be diligent in reciting the daily portion of Tehillim every day after morning davening.

## 6,338

B"H, 6 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter regarding your son, may he live and be well, the contents of which describe how you have arranged a shidduch for him and have taken upon yourself the expenses involved, even though this is beyond your means, and you are asking for assistance in this matter.

Regarding your statement that this is beyond your means: since our Torah is a Torah of life, which teaches that a father is obligated to marry off his son, and it also informs us that the Holy One, blessed be He, does not deal tyrannically with His creatures, it is certain that the expenses required by Torah for the fulfillment of this obligation are within a person's ability—even if, for the moment, one does not perceive this ability with physical eyes.

As for the second point, according to the statement of our Sages, "Whoever receives a *prutah* from Iyov is blessed, for he was a man upright and straight, G-d-fearing and shunning evil." This applies similarly to our Rebbes, the *Nesi'im*—as I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Nasi* of Israel. Our Sages were precise in their language, saying a *prutah* (a small coin), for in this, the quantity is not what determines the outcome, but rather from whom the *prutah* comes. Enclosed, therefore, is a check from one of the funds of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Nasi* of Israel, and we rely on the assurance of our Sages that their aforementioned statement will be fulfilled, and that this *prutah* will bring blessing in obtaining the necessary means.

I trust you are observing the three daily *shiurim*—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and in any case, you should keep them from here on.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 6,339

B"H, 6 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, in which you write that you are in your second year of yeshiva but have not gained much, and that lately you have not been learning because you are wasting time, etc., and therefore you are in doubt as to how you will manage and what you will do in the near future—and you write your reasoning regarding this, being at the age of sixteen.

It is understood, and indeed simple according to the instruction of our Torah, Toras Chaim, that you must continue your studies in yeshiva with persistence and diligence. All the reasons you mentioned are merely the enticements of the *yetzer* [hara], which misleads a person with all sorts of schemes, solely to prevent him from conducting himself in accordance with the instructions of our Torah, Toras Chaim.

Regarding what you write—that you are wasting time, etc.—our Sages have already declared: "If one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do not believe him." Therefore, if you truly desire it, not only will you not waste your time, but you will succeed in your learning more than usual. These very years of your youth are the days of happiness; I mean that if one utilizes them as they should be, they pave the way for a person’s true happiness—spiritual and material happiness alike. As mentioned, know clearly that the matter depends solely on you. If you truly make a firm and appropriate decision regarding this, then even though it may seem to you that starting in this manner is difficult, from time to time you will realize that the difficulties are in part imagined, and even the part that is real is not so difficult to overcome, as the well-known saying goes: "There is nothing that can stand before the will."

You surely know of the three daily *shiurim*—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and you should at least keep them from now on.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6440

6440

B"H, 6 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings! In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, in which you write regarding the proposal for your son... shlita, with a certain young woman... noting that she has an older sister who is not yet engaged, but their parents have hinted that the older one will soon be engaged, at which point they will finalize the matter with the younger one regarding the aforementioned proposal.

Since the matter of *shidduchim* is a "building of eternity" (*binyan adei ad*), it is understood that one should not rush or pressure to hasten the aforementioned by a few days. Rather, one should set a specific date, and until that date, wait for the engagement of the older sister. This date can be a few weeks away, as we are in any case in the month regarding which our Sages said in *Maseches Taanis* (29b, at the beginning) that one should "diminish" (*lishtamit*) in Av. For several reasons, it is not advisable to bind the other side to the fact that they are obligated specifically to this proposal; and conversely, you should not bind yourselves either, as it is possible that during these weeks there may be other proposals worth considering.

It is surprising that you do not mention your participation in the *farbrengens* of *anash*, nor in the *shiurei Torah* taught in public, and most importantly, your activities in *hafatzaat hamaayanot*. After all, this is a *mitzvah* that one performs with one's own self, especially for those whose fathers were involved in this, and the merit of their fathers assists them.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, for the good in personal matters—for a Jewish man and woman—is dependent upon the good in general matters.

#### ***6440***

Published in *Likutei Sichos*, Vol. 20, p. 571, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

## 641

B"H, 6 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, in which you write that you have been offered to travel abroad as a shadar (emissary for fundraising).

It is somewhat surprising that this is even being considered, as it is impossible that you are unaware of those who have already tried this, and that it is not a suitable path for a refined soul. From this, it is understood that such offers should only be considered as a last resort, and surely, chas v'shalom, that is not your situation.

Regarding what you wrote about whether to leave your position at [the institution] to become a teacher in the Reshet (the Chabad school network), and that your wife, tichyeh, agrees to this:

It is generally known what my opinion is, as I have written to many: anyone who is qualified to work in the field of Torah education, happy is his portion and the portion of his household, both materially and spiritually. Regarding a specific individual and a specific offer, it is understood that one must clarify the details and decide accordingly, and based on the above, one should lean toward the better path, which is education that brings the hearts of the sons and daughters of Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6,442

B"H, 6 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, written on behalf of a group of religious young women, regarding whether you should move to a settlement where religious guidance is insufficient in order to teach in the religious school there, or remain in your current locations in the cities, where religious education is already available. You conclude by stating that you believe there will be a religious atmosphere in the aforementioned settlement that will influence you for the good.

It is understood—and this is certainly true regarding Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu—that engaging in education on the foundation of purity and holiness is a great and lofty mitzvah. All those who have been gifted with the appropriate talent for this work should dedicate their time and energy to it.

However, it is also understood that an educator must be an educator and a mashpia, not one who is influenced and educated by others; for if the latter were the case, the potential results and damage, chas v'shalom, are unimaginable.

Since a person is biased toward themselves, one should not rely on their own assessment and evaluation of their soul as to whether they will withstand the test in the place where they intend to teach—specifically, whether they will remain steadfast in the path of our Torah, the Torah of life, and, on the contrary, influence the environment.

A person must explain the matter in detail to those who know them and their character, and who also understand the nature of the place and the environment in question; they will then instruct them on how to decide.

The conclusion from the above is that, certainly, in a group of people—as our Sages of blessed memory said, their opinions are not the same—there is no room for a uniform decision for all members of the group. Each one is a matter to be judged on its own merits, in accordance with what has been stated. Surely, in the holy city of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established, you will be able to find many who are truly G-d-fearing, who understand the chapter of education and the nature of the human soul, and each one of you should consult with them regarding her own situation.

As you requested, this letter is being sent without waiting for the regular turn, due to the urgency of the matter, and I am sure you will inform us of the results. May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam, who oversees each and every one with Divine Providence, to guide each one of you on the path that is truly good for her.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 6,443

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings! ...Regarding what you wrote in response to my question about *hafatzas hamaayanos*, that it has already been suggested several times to the esteemed Rabbi, may he live, that a special person is needed to come to their camp, etc. — the greatest astonishment is understandable here. For do they truly say to themselves that they were sent to [that location] in order to slaughter a certain number of cattle and fowl, or in order to pray and deliver a sermon specifically in a certain place? As is the well-known example of a servant who was trained to be a pearl-driller but occupies himself with selling bread and meat. Even though bread and meat are necessary, for this, there is no need for the investment of the revealed and hidden powers that were invested in them. This could be done by many others, for whom our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, did not sacrifice themselves to educate specifically within the walls of *Toras Emes* and by drawing down a multitude of light. And although it is understood that the impression of this investment is noticeable in any matter, even in the selling of bread and meat, this is only a *makif* (encompassing) matter, and it is obvious that it is not a primary matter. Especially since they themselves see tangibly that they have been in this place for several years, and Divine Providence has not brought any other *Temimim* or *Anash* there, even though it is clear that *hafatzas hamaayanos* must reach their camp as well.

It is understood that it is within your authority, and also your merit, to convey the above to the *Rav Mara D'asra* as well, since the words are directed to him too. On the contrary, according to what is explained in many places, the responsibility of the *Mara D'asra* is even greater than that of the *shochet*, although the responsibility of the latter is also great, as per the well-known explanation of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe: "A *shochet* is not a cattle-butcher," etc.

And since we are coming from the month of the *Geulah*, the month of Tammuz, in which occurred the *Geulah* of our Rebbe, the Nasi of Israel, and the body follows the head, may it be the will of Hashem that each and every one of us be redeemed immediately from all matters that cause confusion, both physically and spiritually, with a revealed victory over them—as in those days, at this time. And may they be able to serve Hashem with joy and a glad heart, and in the central point—in *hafatzas hamaayanos* (until it reaches) *chutzah* (the outside).

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

***

**As per the well-known explanation:** See also above, Vol. 13, Letter 4,442, and the references in the notes there.

## 6444

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual engaged in communal affairs,
R' Chaim Zusya, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—in which you describe how you have been involved in various matters, yet for the time being, the results are not satisfying to you, etc.

The explanation lies in your own words: that you have been involved in "various matters." It is self-understood that, consequently, you have not been sufficiently involved in any single one of them. In normal times, it would suffice to be involved in one area of material affairs and similarly in spiritual matters. It is understood—and it is also simple—that in a period of years that are not normal, in the *ikvesa d'meshicha*, as our Sages have stated regarding this, it is necessary not to limit one's activity to only one area in spiritual matters, and likewise regarding material livelihood. However, together with this, it is understood that one must focus primarily on one matter, in accordance with the words of our Sages: "In which [mitzvah] was your father most careful?"—that in this endeavor, one should be more involved, while in one's other activities, one should be involved in the usual manner, or even less than that. [My intention is only to arouse and encourage others so that they will engage in this as if it were their own profession, and from time to time to demand of them to increase their strength in their work, and to demand many times—in the style of our Sages, "even one hundred times"—but without forgetting one's own primary endeavor.]

And if, at the very least from now on, you arrange things in the manner described above, you will surely see success, not only in the primary endeavor but also in those matters in which you are only arousing, demanding, and initiating. May it be His will that this happens soon.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.

It is understood that since the current situation is that you have already begun several matters, and consequently people are relying on you, the intention of the above is not that you should immediately neglect all matters except for one or two—as there is a great concern that the other matters would then be abandoned, since until now they have been accustomed to you bearing the burden. Rather, you should continue to draw in, for each and every one of the other matters, one or two people suitable for it, and impress upon them that it is necessary for them to take this upon their own shoulders, since you are lacking in your primary activity due to your involvement in this or that matter as well. It is to be hoped that within a not-too-long period of time, you will find dedicated activists for many of those areas, in the same manner in which you have acted until now, as mentioned above.

#### ***6444***

**R' Chaim Zusya:** Vilimovsky, Tel Aviv. Further letters to him—above, Vol. 16, 6066, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 6047

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings! Through the intermediary of my relative, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned man, who engages in the work of Heaven and is involved in communal needs, R' Moshe Zalman Shneurson, I received your question:

In connection with the changes that have occurred in recent years, it has occurred to you to sell your house. Through this, you would be able to pay off your debts and give a sum to your children, may they live, to help them settle into another apartment. You conclude by saying that if there is no money left for an apartment for yourself, you are not concerned and are prepared for that as well, and you ask my opinion on this.

Based on what we see tangibly regarding the results when, at your age, one must live with others and be dependent on their assistance—even when it involves the most devoted children, where even if everything is fine at first, the relationship changes over time—it is understood that I do not agree with the aforementioned arrangement. (And even if we were to say that the debt is extremely burdensome and cannot be paid off except by selling the house, there must be a suitable apartment ready for you. That is to say, there should be no time where the money is squandered, even for a very important matter, since the money should already be invested in an apartment for you, in a way that you can live an independent life and see, even in the natural order, that you are not dependent on the help of flesh and blood. And this is obvious. Based on the above, it is understood that an even better arrangement would be to find a better way to pay off the debts.)

Since it is mentioned in the aforementioned letter that your loan involves interest, you have surely done this according to a *heter iska*. If, G-d forbid, you have not, you must immediately upon receiving this letter rectify it in the appropriate manner as instructed by a competent Rabbi.

2) Regarding your request for a blessing for Mrs. [Name], may she live and be well.

At a time of favor, I will mention her at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever she needs, and especially for the improvement of her health. It is understood and also simple that the parents of the aforementioned must increase their involvement in matters of Torah and *mitzvos* as much as depends on them, for this increase is the channel and the vessel for the drawing down and receiving of the blessings of the Healer of all flesh, Who performs wonders, including regarding their daughter. It is understood and also simple that the conduct of the parents in their private matters according to Torah and *mitzvos* is relevant and influential.

In a special way, it is understood that their conduct in public and in matters that concern the many and the merit of the many is even more relevant, as the Mishnah states regarding one who has merit and causes the many to have merit, and the opposite, G-d forbid. May it be the will of Hashem that you find the appropriate words, and that the words will come from the heart and, consequently, enter the heart of the aforementioned and achieve their effect.

It is proper to check the *mezuzos* in your home to ensure they are all kosher according to the law, and also that you should observe the custom of the daughters of Israel to set aside money for *tzedakah* before lighting the candles every *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6 Tammuz

B"H, 11 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Dovber, Shochet and Bodek, and his wife, Mrs. Rachel, may she live:

Peace and blessing!

After a very long hiatus, your letter was received, including the highlights of the farbrengens during the auspicious and redemptive days of 12 and 13 Tammuz. It is understandable that I am pained by what you wrote regarding the infrequency of farbrengens with the yeshiva avreichim, for various reasons, as is understood. Given the importance of the matter, it is worthwhile to look into how this situation can be corrected and improved. There is nothing that stands before the will, especially since, in the depths of their souls, the avreichim themselves desire this, as is explained in Chassidus in many places.

Regarding preparing talks for the gatherings of N'shei U'Bnos Chabad: one can utilize the talks and tapes that have already been published over many years—there are already nearly 300 numbers—from which one can draw rich material. This is especially true when one processes it and adds a little, as much as possible, according to the level of the listeners and what is understandable to them. Since reading from the inside, as you wrote, does not have the desired effect, and since the work itself is of the utmost importance, it is certain that it can be accomplished. One only needs to try in various ways until the right method is found to realize this. This is especially true when taking into account the reward that Hashem gives for this: that one receives the fruits in this world and in true nachas (which is Chassidishe nachas) from one's children. May Hashem help you to report good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings for success.

## 6447

B"H, 11 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 7 Menachem Av, in which you write about what you have experienced until now, the emotional upheavals and the changes in your state of mind, etc., and that with the help of Hashem, through various efforts, your mind has become settled and you are studying at the preparatory program of the holy Yeshiva, founded and directed by our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, may their merits protect us.

It is surely unnecessary to emphasize that you should strengthen your trust in the Creator of the world and its Guide, knowing that everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good. With true tranquility, joy, and a glad heart, you should study with diligence and persistence, and be meticulous in the performance of mitzvos.

Regarding the conflicts you mention, the best path is not to enter into arguments, G-d forbid. In the style of our Sages, be among those who hear but do not respond; this is the paved path for minimizing friction and conflict, as mentioned above. The true point is that the very act of studying with joy breaks through barriers and nullifies concealments and hesterim.

The details of how to conduct yourself in this regard naturally depend on many particulars and sub-particulars. Therefore, you should explain your situation in detail to your shiur teacher and your mashpia; they will advise and instruct you, especially since it appears from your letter that they have helped you in the past, and their help has brought great benefit.

You are surely aware of the three daily shiurim of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya; in any case, you should keep them from here on out.

With blessings for the study of Torah with joy and a glad heart, and for the performance of its mitzvos in this manner,

## 6,448

B"H, 12 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Nissan, may he live.

Peace and blessing! In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Shemini, in which you write regarding your birthday on the 13th of Menachem Av.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that this year be one of success for you in your avodah in holiness—specifically, the establishing and developing of the Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch Yeshiva in Europe, which Divine Providence has placed in your capable hands to manage. May the verse "He redeemed in peace" be fulfilled in this avodah, such that all matters are conducted in ways of peace—which is the vessel that holds the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam—and "many were with me", meaning that even those matters that seem to conceal and obscure not only fail to conceal or obscure, but actually stand with me and assist. Consequently, it is understood and simple that there will be an increase in your personal matters and those of your household, may they live, also in the aforementioned manner of "in peace" and "many were with me," for one thing is dependent upon the other. This is especially true regarding matters connected to our Rebbes, the Nesi'im. Although all the above requires an *is'arusa d'lesata* (arousal from below), as explained in *Likutei Torah* for this week—"And I beseeched Hashem... and I saw the good land," yet he did not succeed [in entering], only "And now, O Israel, listen..."—his prayer was nonetheless effective, at least in part. This teaches that not only in matters of Torah—"bread from Heaven"—is there *hashpa'ah* (influence) from above through *is'arusa d'le'eila* (arousal from above), but even in matters pertaining to *tefillah*, there is an additional awakening from above. And the *pnimiyus haTorah* (inner dimension of Torah), and specifically the teachings of Chassidus, is the intermediary that unites (and like all that unites, it transcends the two things being united) Torah and *tefillah*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 6,449

B"H, 13 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and industrious, engaged in communal needs, R' Peretz, may he live.

Peace and blessing! I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 11 Menachem Av. I thank Hashem for the good news regarding the release of your eldest son, Shmuel, may he live and be well. According to our Sages, may it be that whatever good happens to a person is for long, good days and years. May it be His will that soon you will also share good news regarding the other matters about which you write.

Regarding your question as to whether you should exert effort to have your eldest son move to Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, from Poland, or whether he should remain in Riga for the time being to pursue [the necessary] efforts, etc.:

Since the details of the situation there and the possibilities for the efforts required to move from that country are not known from here—and furthermore, because changes are liable to occur in this regard, and it is impossible to inquire there to clarify this in his name for reasons that are understood—it is not advisable to intervene from here in the aforementioned. In this instance, "sit and do not act" is preferable, and they should rely on the understanding of those who are present on the scene.

Thank you for the good news regarding the recovery of [name omitted]—may it be His will that you also share good news regarding her, as well as regarding the general matters, by which I mean his Torah study and his participation in farbrengens at auspicious times. Regarding what you write, that this is currently "in miniature" (*b'ze'er anpin*), the response—in the spirit of wit—is that *Ze'er Anpin* is the extremity of the light of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He (Torah Ohr, end of Parshas Terumah). My intent is not merely a witty remark, but also the inner dimension of the matter: that even in a *ze'er anpin* setting, as you write regarding his study, one must infuse it with such great light that it reaches the level of *Ein Sof*. Consequently, it will influence the participants—even though they are few in number—to increase their influence in their surroundings, to the point that, in total, it will be much greater than the influence of many who are present at a farbrengen that lacks light. It is understood that the aforementioned depends primarily on the one who is farbrenging.

With blessings for good news in all the aforementioned.

650

## 651

B"H, 14 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings! I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Shabbos Chazon. At an auspicious time, I will mention all those you wrote about once again at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever they may need.

May it be Hashem’s will that, since we have emerged from the "straits" (*meitzarim*) in terms of time and are now on the eve of the 15th of Av—a time when one emerges from all doubts, as related by our Sages at the end of Maseches Taanis (and in Tosafos and Eicha Rabbah)—this should serve as a good beginning for emerging from all "straits" in every sense, both materially and spiritually.

However, since this emergence depends on Hashem, the Counsel of Good (unlike the period of the "straits," regarding which it is said, "From the mouth of the Most High, evil does not emerge"), the salvation of Hashem can happen in the blink of an eye—in the well-known phrasing, "in a single hour and a single moment"—and on this very day,* the true and complete redemption of the individual and the collective is possible.

And if you were to say that the redemption of the collective depends on the redemption of the individual and his actions to the extent that it is within his power, this is indeed understood from what is explained in many places. It is a definitive ruling in our Torah, the Torah of life and the Torah of truth. In the words of the Rambam, every person should view the entire world as half-meritorious and half-guilty; if he performs one mitzvah, he tips the entire world to the side of merit and brings about salvation and deliverance (Hilchos Teshuvah, Chapter 3, Halacha 4, summarized in relation to our matter).

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6,553

B"H, 14 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 11 Menachem Av, in which you write regarding the state of your health and the advice of the professor to travel for a period of time to the seashore, etc.

This is the correct course of action, for the Torah has granted the physician permission to heal. It is understood that this should be done with joy and a glad heart, especially in accordance with the verse, **"From Hashem are the steps of man established"** (and as explained by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, that Divine Providence guides a person, yet one must act) "and in His way he delights"—meaning that he should carry out his mission there with *cheifetz* (desire/will). As explained in Chassidus, *cheifetz* is the inwardness of the will. We do not know what the future holds, and certainly, in the place to which you are traveling, you will be able to accomplish in matters of Yiddishkeit in general, and in the dissemination of the wellsprings (*hafotzas hamaayanos*) in particular. However, it is understood, as mentioned above, that this must be done with joy and a glad heart, for through this, your physical health will be enhanced, and your success in your mission in that place will be increased.

It is surely superfluous to emphasize once again that your mission must be carried out in conjunction with observing the doctor’s instructions—that is, without compromising your physical health in the literal sense at all. Since both matters are a mitzvah (for having a healthy and whole body is one of the ways of Hashem), you can certainly do both together; on the contrary, one mitzvah leads to another.

As you requested, this response is being sent without waiting for the regular turn.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

#### ***6,553***

**And as explained:** See also above, Vol. 12, Letter 3,834, and the references in the notes there. Below, 6,583.

## 6,454

B"H, 14 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 5 Menachem Av, in which you write that initially you wanted to study with diligence in order to utilize your time to the fullest, but in the meantime, a letter arrived regarding the study program, and this diminished your enthusiasm for your studies, etc.

It is puzzling what connection there is between the content of the letter and a decrease in enthusiasm. After all, the time at a person’s disposal must be utilized in the most efficient manner. Those whom Hashem—the Creator and Guide of the world—has gifted with talent must utilize it to the fullest. This means that if a certain subject can be learned in a short amount of time, there is no place whatsoever to drag it out over a long period. Certainly, the remaining time can be utilized for additional activities, whether in study or in influencing one's environment, and the like. This is also understood from what is explained in *Kuntres U'Maayan*, that even a person of great intellect must study specifically in a manner of "you have labored," with persistence and diligence.

Therefore, it is my hope that you will utilize your time and talents to the full extent of the ability granted to you in this regard. There is an additional advantage to this: the very act of doing so increases one's capacity, as is known from the analogy of physical limbs—that by exercising them as much as is necessary, their capacity for the future increases...

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 655

B"H, 15 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 11 Menachem Av, I am writing to reply promptly. Your interpretation of why you have not yet received a response to your previous letter—suggesting that perhaps I am dissatisfied with the timing you proposed—is entirely incorrect [and it is surprising, for after I have already informed you that the delay in responding is due to the multitude of pressures, everyone comes to interpret various strange and unusual hints and sub-hints].

In general, there is no place at all for your phrasing "barely managing to arrange the wedding," for these are two opposites. A wedding must be with joy, and joy breaks through boundaries to the point of absolute expansion, which is the complete opposite of matters of "pressure." Furthermore, it is understood that there is no room for the second half of the month of Tishrei, as I have not seen this practiced.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you and your family—may they live—regarding all the matters about which you write. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all the above, as well as in general matters, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed, and in a manner that is ever-increasing.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 650

650

B"H, 18 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished elder of Anash,
Rabbi A. S. Shlita,

Peace and blessing! I received with pleasure the supplement to your book, *Edus L'Asaf*, which contains *likutei amarim* to complete the section of *Remez* that was not included in your aforementioned book.

It is already well-known in the books of Kabbalah, and cited also in the teachings of Chassidus (see *Koheles Yaakov*, entry *Remez*; *Sichas Chof-Cheshvan* 5733, from my father-in-law, the Rebbe), that the four worlds of ABYA correspond to the four parts of Torah, *Pardes*. There are those who say that the section of *Remez* corresponds to the world of *Yetzirah*, while others say it corresponds to the world of *Beriah*. Each has its own advantage: the world of *Beriah* is the beginning of the created worlds, and therefore possesses an abundance of light; whereas the world of *Yetzirah* already possesses a form that the created being can grasp, which allows for a more complete unification with the concept and brings it closer to action, which is not the case in the world of *Beriah*.

This is alluded to (see *Likutei Torah*, *Shir HaShirim* 42d) in the verse, as transposed by the Men of the Great Assembly: "He who forms (*yotzer*) light and creates (*boreh*) darkness."

May it be the will of Hashem that you merit, together with all those who delve into *Remez*, that through their *remezim* they may be able to unite both advantages together, and—most importantly, regarding actual practice—to increase in "fear G-d and keep His commandments, for this is the whole of man."

As a token of appreciation, I have added in the margins some notes and references regarding the topics touched upon in your aforementioned booklet. May it be His will that for many more years you continue to increase soldiers for Torah and its mitzvos, and may this be with proper health and true expansion of the mind.

With respect and blessing for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good year.

**Notes**
**To section A.** Regarding the number 400 in "Esav," etc.: See *Torah Or*, *Vayishlach* (24c), and at length in *Or HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, *Parshas Chayei Sarah*, p. 230 and onwards.

**To section B.** Regarding the connection between Amalek and Mitzrayim (Pharaoh, whose name contains the letters of *oref*—the nape): *Torah Or*, end of *Parshas Tetzaveh*. It is worth noting *Bava Basra* (46b). Regarding "Amalek is a sign": The Yaavetz has already addressed this there.

**To section C.** It should be noted that the bird of the *metzora* (who caused separation between...) requires *shechitah* specifically.

**To section D.** See "HaChodesh HaZeh" in *Sefer HaMaamarim* 5726.

***

**650**
**Rabbi A. S.:** Nemtsov. Additional letters to him: see above, Vol. 14, letter 5115, and the references in the notes there.

## 6558

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Blessings and peace! In response to your letter of the 13th of Menachem Av, in which you write regarding the state of your health and the opinion of the doctors.

In such matters, one should follow the instructions of specialists in the field, at the very least by way of a consultation between two of them. As for what you write, that you will need to be in rest for several months afterward, this is very surprising, for generally, a **disproportionately** shorter time is sufficient. Perhaps you did not describe the ailment and the proposed treatment in your letter as clearly as you should have; please provide more details on this in your next opportunity.

Furthermore, if your description is accurate, even after the surgery and the aforementioned treatment, one continues to lead a normal married life. It would be worthwhile for you to consult with a Rav who is a *moreh hora'ah* regarding this.

The merit of your involvement, together with your husband—may he live and be well—in the education of the sons and daughters of Yisrael, who, as I hear, are being drawn by your influence to our Torah, the Torah of life, and its *mitzvos*, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them"—a life of fullness and a life of happiness—will surely stand for you, as well as for your husband and your children—may they live—in whatever they may need. And this is in accordance with the measure of the Ribono shel Olam, which is *middah k'neged middah* (measure for measure), only many times over. And from a state of tranquility of soul and expansion of mind, may you continue in the most exalted *avodah* of *chinuch* (education) in the spirit of the holy Torah, in a manner that is ever-increasing.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

M. Schneerson

## 6,559

**[24 Menachem Av, 5718]**

In response to your letter, in which you inform me that on the 15th of Menachem Av you reached the age of twelve, the time of your Bas Mitzvah.

May it be Hashem’s will that you accept upon yourself the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven and the yoke of the mitzvos with a whole heart. May Hashem, blessed be He, grant you success in your studies and your conduct, and may you grow to be worthy of the name "daughter of Chabad," in accordance with the will of our holy Nesi’im, of blessed memory.

May you also influence your friends in this regard, through your speech, and even more so by being a living example of a Bas Yisrael educated in the ways of Chassidus. This will bring you spiritual and material happiness...

Regarding your question about where to continue your studies and the manner in which to do so—

In my opinion, since the education of youth—and especially education during the years of your age—influences the entire course of one’s life, and upon it depends one’s independence and strength to withstand the trials that exist in the life of every individual,

And since we are in a period of many changes, where it is impossible to estimate now the character and conditions of life even a few years from now, and therefore it is also impossible to know the magnitude of the trials that will arise then, so as not to stumble in matters of justice and integrity, faith and religion,

—therefore, every young person must and is obligated to receive a religious education to the maximum degree, so that they will be able to withstand any danger that might arise, Heaven forbid.

And even if such an education involves some inconvenience or the like for a period of time—what does that count for compared to the fortification and added strength one receives, specifically through this education, for the entire duration of one’s life.

6460

B”H, 25 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and involved in communal needs,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter of the 21st of Menachem Av and the enclosure, may it be the will of Hashem that both you and your wife, may she live, will throw yourselves into avodas hakodesh with the ten powers of the nefesh habehamis, and certainly with the ten powers of the nefesh d’nefesh elokis. In such a state, it is obvious that the body will not only refrain from being a distraction, but will actually perform with perfection.

Then, the promise of our Sages will certainly be fulfilled: “You have labored” (which is both a requirement and a promise; the meaning of *yagatta* is literal—to toil, to work hard), “and you have found.” As explained in the farbrengen here, it does not say “you have understood” or “you have grasped,” for in that there is no novelty. Rather, the Torah promises that the success will be in a manner of “finding”—where, on the face of it, one does not understand how such a thing could be so far beyond one’s own level, and so on.

May Hashem grant you the merit to share good news, and in a manner that is ever-increasing. We are approaching the month of Elul, the month of mercy, when everyone recites “Hashem is my light and my salvation,” etc.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6561

B"H, 26 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

You write at the beginning of your letter regarding a trip here. Despite my desire—and the unpleasantness of the matter—I must inform you once again of my perspective on this: Each and every one of us is obligated to conduct himself according to the Shulchan Aruch, and specifically according to what is explained in Chassidus regarding this. It is explained therein that matters of *parnassah* are an obligation of a person toward his household and himself. It is also explained that *parnassah* in this world is bound up with action and exertion, as the verse states explicitly: "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do" (see *Kuntres U'Maayan*, *maamar* 23 and onwards, and in many other places). It is further explained there that the repayment of debt is an absolute necessity, also for its own sake...

Based on the above, it is absolutely clear that there is no room for expenses that can be avoided—and the aforementioned travel expenses are among them. Even if it were only for a few days or weeks, this is **contrary** to the *psak din* in *nigleh*, and in Chassidus in particular. If, in truth, he has the funds for the tickets, then first and foremost he should begin by settling the aforementioned debts. It is also possible that he will write to me that the trip is necessary for someone in the family and their affairs; to this I answer before he even asks: this is nothing more than an additional "excuse," and it is not at all necessary for the family either, etc.

The conclusion from what has been said is that regarding what you write to me—that seemingly this should be interpreted as wanting to know my opinion on the matter—it is **clear:** you should continue your holy work of *hafatzas hamaayanos* and its related matters, and the strengthening of the institutions of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, in... When the time comes that your work is organized and expanded, once you have broadened your situation by exiting from debt, etc., then you can look into traveling here. I hope that you will accept these words as they were said—that is, without any ulterior motives, etc., and only for the sake of what is truly good for you and your household, *shichye*. At the same time, this also touches upon general matters. May you bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned, and may it be soon.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6,462

6,462

B"H, 26 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

...Regarding the mikveh: You wrote that you constructed an additional *otzar* on the side to ensure *zeriah*. According to the method of the Rebbe (my father-in-law, of blessed memory)—which is a mikveh **on top of** the *otzar*, and he wanted the water from the lower one to rise above the floor of the upper one (as per Rabbi Y.L. Landau, shlita)—this is *zeriah* in the most effective manner, as it requires no *hashakah* at all according to all opinions, as is understood. Furthermore, even if they do not rise above the floor, it should be arranged so that the *sha'uvim* fall **directly** into the opening leading to the lower *otzar*, which constitutes *zeriah*. If so, what does the *otzar* on the side add? (Unless it is merely as a precaution, in case the lower *otzar* becomes compromised.)

#### ***6,462***

6506

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Eliezer Livneh,

Shalom u’vracha,

I received your article, "The Exile by Choice," which you were kind enough to send me. It was delayed in transit longer than usual, and due to many preoccupations, my response was delayed; please accept my apologies.

I read your article with interest, paying special attention to its central point: the substitutes that people seek to use as replacements for the true mission and inner core of Judaism and the Jewish people. It is easy for a person of understanding to grasp the serious and undesirable consequences that result from this.

Seeing that you do not hesitate to express views that are not in line with popular opinion, I hope that you will continue in this direction to reject any substitute whatsoever. After all, the very essence of a "substitute" emphasizes that it is not what it ought to be. From this, it is understood that the more perfect and attractive the imitation—the substitute—the greater the danger, even if, at first glance or from a superficial perspective, the difference is not so apparent and it may, for a short while, quench the soul’s thirst.

For someone like you, it is unnecessary to emphasize what is agreed upon and accepted—at least in theory, if not in practice—that although it is a necessity for every nation and people to have a foothold in material and worldly matters, since we are speaking of human beings and not herds of sheep and cattle, it is clear that their mission is not limited to matters of eating, drinking, fine housing, and the like. Rather, their mission is specifically in matters connected to the intellect and the spirit, which are the advantage of the "speaker" (human) over the animal. If this is true regarding other people and every nation and tongue, it is all the more so regarding the Jewish people. Despite the necessity of matters connected to fulfilling the needs of the body, these do not constitute their primary and inner mission; rather, that mission consists precisely of matters whose source is in the world of thought and spirit—that is, what is connected to the *neshamah*, while the body is merely a vessel for carrying them out. One must not exchange the means for fulfilling the mission with the mission itself, even if those means are necessary and vital for the survival of the *nefesh* within the body. In the language and style of our Sages, "saving a life (*pikuach nefesh*) overrides everything." The meaning of the word *nefesh* in that context is the survival of the soul within the body, but as stated, this is only a means—albeit a necessary one that overrides (almost) everything—but it is still only a means for fulfilling the mission. And just as this is true regarding the individual, so it is regarding the collective.

It is understood that if someone is mistaken and confuses a means with the mission, if the error concerns a means that is not essential and positive, one can hope that the person will recognize their mistake through some reflection, or at the very least, it is easy to set them straight. This is not the case if the means is vital and essential for fulfilling the mission; in that case, the error is more common and the substitution and replacement are more likely. Even when one comes to prove the truth to them with signs and wonders, it is much harder to set them straight so that they will acknowledge their error and abandon it. Therefore, as mentioned, the danger that they will neglect the mission is much greater.

Therefore, when it comes to the substitutes you write about in your article—through which many of our Jewish brethren wish to fulfill their obligations by donating a check, attending a meeting a few times, and the like, in order to exempt themselves from fulfilling their true mission—it is inevitable that they will eventually lead to the undesirable results you describe in your article: an emptying of all Jewish essence and content, etc. But despite all this, anyone who is not deterred from expressing a view that does not coincide with what is accepted by the majority of the public should sound the alarm regarding the danger that is looming, which is **many times greater.** The destructive results are already visible in their effects—primarily among the youth, the future of the nation—from more "subtle" substitutes, such as the substitute regarding the matter of politics, independent territory, and self-governance. Even if they achieve this fully and enjoy it fully, one must not forget that this, too, is only a means. We must demand that this be engraved in the heart and mind in a way that permeates every limb of the individual and every limb of the collective: that the mission is specifically a matter connected to the governance of the spirit and the intellect. In the language of Chassidus, this is "the dominance of the form over the matter." Another formulation, based on a story we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is that the Alter Rebbe, the founder of Chabad Chassidus, instructed the path in a person's *avodah* in this style: "One must discipline the horse, so that the horses become 'no longer horses'." And in another version, "so that the horses should know that they are horses"—meaning "horses" in the sense of the material.

With respect and blessing.

## 6,768

B"H, 1 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 25th of Menachem Av.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding what you need in accordance with the content of your letter. May it be His will that you bring good tidings in all the matters you write about.

Regarding what you wrote about forgetfulness, may Hashem spare us, the known *segulah* for this is to study *Mishnayos* by heart, and also to give a few *prutos* to *tzedakah* on weekdays before the morning *tefillah*. This is a *segulah* for many matters, and generally for a person’s requests of his Creator in his *tefillah*, as our Sages of blessed memory have informed us: "One should give a *prutah* to a pauper and then pray," and as it is written, "I, through *tzedakah*, will behold Your face," etc.

It is appropriate that you have your *tefillin* checked, as well as the *mezuzos* in your home, to ensure they are all *kosher* according to *halacha*. Also, maintain the practice of reciting the monthly *Tehillim* portion—as the *Tehillim* is divided for the days of the month—each day after the morning *tefillah*.

With blessings for good tidings and for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 6,459

B”H, 1 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval, your letter of 27 Menachem Av arrived with the good news that you are strengthening yourself to keep up with the *shiurim* of *Chitas*, as well as regarding the other matters you wrote about. Most importantly, regarding learning with *hasmadah* and *shekidah*—for regarding this it is said, "Great is study, for it leads to action"—through this comes a strengthening in all matters of *mitzvos*. 

Specifically regarding what you wrote concerning the matter of the beard: the instruction of the *Nasi*, the *Tzemach Tzedek*, based on the words of the holy *Zohar* (as explained by the *Tzemach Tzedek* in his commentary on *Tehillim* on the verse "And He is merciful"), is well known: that through the guarding of the hair of the beard, one draws down from the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim*, which is *rachamim rabim* (see there in the *miluim* to the *Yahel Ohr* commentary on *Tehillim*).

Regarding what you wrote about overcoming the well-known matter: the instruction in this is well known—that one must strive to think about it as little as possible, even not thinking about the *tikkun* for the matter. Rather, since a person’s thoughts are always occupied, one must immerse one’s thoughts in the matters one is learning or doing. Also, one should divide the *tzedakah* one gives into multiple occasions, and give it at *zmanim mesugalim* (among them, on weekdays before *davening* in the morning and before *Mincha*). In general, one should increase in the *osiyos* of *Torah* and *tefillah*, and engage in influence regarding *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*, according to the arrangement, provided that this does not interfere with the *sedarim* of the *yeshivah* or with one's health. 

May *Hashem Yisbarach* help you to report good news in all of the above, and soon.

With the blessing of *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah*.

## 6470

6470

B"H, 1 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the 25th of Menachem Av.

At an opportune time, I will mention you, as well as those you wrote about, at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever each one of you requires, in accordance with the content of your letter.

It would be appropriate for you to ask your Rosh Yeshiva and your mashpia to explain to you the concept of Hashgacha Pratis, as elucidated by the Baal Shem Tov and at length in the teachings of Chassidus Chabad—specifically, how it applies to every single Jewish man and woman, down to the smallest details of their lives. From this, it is understood that if a person only creates a vessel for this Hashgacha, then regardless of what has occurred in his past, it is within his power to rectify the situation from this point forward. In time, he can even fully rectify the past; this depends solely on his will. However, just as all human affairs proceed step by step, so too does this improvement come about step by step. If one only makes a true resolution in this regard, one can be certain that, in the end, everything will be rectified.

When you show this letter of mine to your mashpia, he will surely explain these matters as much as is necessary. May it be His will that you soon bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned.

With blessings for success in your Torah study with diligence and perseverance, with yiras shamayim, and for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6741

6741

B"H, Wednesday, the 4th of Elul, 5718

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter, which was delayed in transit longer than usual. In it, you write regarding your intention for the sake of Heaven and your prayer that no stumbling block should come about through your efforts. As you mention in your letter, "Whoever comes to purify himself is assisted," and one should add, as the Gemara adds there, that "they sanctify him greatly from Above."

May it be the will of Hashem that this be fulfilled in your case, and that you utilize your influence to its fullest to magnify the Torah of truth and the perfect Torah—both the revealed and the inner dimensions, which is called in the holy Zohar (Vol. III, 156a) "the soul of the Torah"—and to disseminate it among the children of Yisrael, especially the children, the youth, and the young, in a manner of "increasing and going further, increasing and lighting." Certainly, in this too, there will be *siyata d'shmaya*, as per the aforementioned statement of our Sages and many others like it.

Regarding what you write concerning the difficult financial situation of the kosher restaurant in Rabat, to the point that it is also burdened with debts, surely you are also aware of the difficult financial situation in which many Chabad institutions in various countries find themselves, and this is not the place to elaborate on that.

Nevertheless, due to the importance of the matter—and everything is by *hashgacha pratis*—and since you have written to me regarding the aforementioned, I am enclosing a check* herewith, at least as a one-time assistance. May it be the will of the Giver of the Torah, Who commands the mitzvos and is the Creator and Guide of the world, to expand the borders of all the children of Yisrael, and the institutions of pure holiness first and foremost, so that they may fully accomplish their mission to illuminate the darkness of the world with the "candle of a mitzvah" and "Torah is light" and the "light of the Torah." This is also the channel and vessel for blessing and success in material and physical matters as well.

With respect and blessing, as mentioned above, to utilize your ability to disseminate the Torah of truth that we received at the standing at Har Sinai, and as per the well-known statement of our Sages, that all souls, even those yet to be born, were present at the time of the Giving of the Torah. May it be in a manner where "study leads to action"—the fulfillment of the mitzvos of our Torah, the Torah of life, in practice—and especially the fundamental mitzvah of "And you shall teach them to your children," education of pure holiness.

And with the blessing of *Kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 6772

6772

B"H, 5 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Eliezer Steinman,

Greetings and blessings!

I recently received your book, *Alim Me'etz Hachaim*, and I thank you for it. Naturally, out of fondness for the subject, I went through its pages. It is specifically in matters that seemingly lack an internal connection and are not perfectly ordered that one can see the author in a clearer light than is reflected in polished books written for a singular purpose that unifies the book from beginning to end.

In keeping with the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, based on the saying of the Tzemach Tzedek interpreting the style of our Sages, "We are the workers of the day"—that our task is to increase light in the world, in this world of ours—and since this is an instruction for every single soul of the Jewish people while they are in bodies in this world, I will permit myself to awaken you. Based on what you write in your aforementioned book (p. 3): "We are here the vanguard of the Jewish people... the title of our people’s history, the essence of its suffering for its land and its G-d, that every tremor in our past... strikes at the apple of our eye," and in accordance with the influence you have in various circles, I find it puzzling why you do not take a firm stand against all those phenomena that affect the daily life in our Holy Land in the sphere of the internal life of the Jewish people—that is to say, the life of the soul, the *neshamah elokis*. Unfortunately, these phenomena are not decreasing; rather, the danger grows because these matters are categorized as a matter of "prestige," for which one must be prepared to die rather than transgress. Yet, in accordance with the lines mentioned regarding the G-d of Israel and the past of the Jewish people, surely many phenomena would not have come to pass were it not for the *yetzer* of competitiveness, which, like all *yetzarim*, causes a person to disregard even his own reason, let alone the will of his Creator. Surely this is not the time for anyone to seclude themselves within their own four cubits and say that whatever happens outside is not their concern because they are occupied with lofty matters "above ten handbreadths" of this world—especially when many listen to your voice, and [there is the obligation for] one who has the power to protest, etc.

It is possible that you have expressed your view on the aforementioned phenomena, but word of it has not reached here. Even if that is the case, it is proof that this response is insufficient, since the echo of other responses has reached and continues to reach here with trumpets and a loud blast. Therefore, it is clear that a response in defense of the pain of the *Shechinah* of the Jewish people, as you mention in your book there, certainly should have arrived, and in a more active manner.

And now that we have entered the month of Elul, when it is customary to recite *L’Dovid Hashem Ori V’Yishi* twice each day—and a verse does not depart from its literal meaning—*Ori V’Yishi* in this world, even though its deeds are difficult and evil and the wicked prevail in it (*Tanya*, end of Chapter 6), and *Ori V’Yishi* in a way that "I shall not fear." May it be the will [of Hashem] that the light pierce the darkness of the world and push it away, for even a little light pushes away much darkness, and from day to day it will increase until "the night shines like the day."

With respect and with the blessing of *Kesivah V’chasimah Tovah*.

In a separate package, I am sending you material published here by Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, and I hope you will find interest in it.

## 6743

B"H, 5 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you heard others say, that what I wrote concerning ships applies only to old ones and not to new ones:

It is understood that before I wrote regarding the aforementioned matter—and certainly before I gave permission to print my letters concerning ships, which was in the year **5718**—I contemplated the operation and management of ships at the time of the publication and printing of the letters; that is, during those years and up until the year 5718.

And I would add that, given the current pace of technological advancement, it is highly probable that in another several years, ships will be operated by machines called "automatic," but in such a way that **many** times throughout a twenty-four-hour period, they will require human intervention in a manner that constitutes *melachah* *d'oraisa*. Anyone who says otherwise either knows **nothing at all** regarding the actual, present-day operation of ships, or their desire and intent is to mislead the public, and with a most egregious error.

## 6474

6474

B”H, 9 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn

To the avreich Yaakov Dovid, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Sunday, Parshas Teitzei, regarding your question concerning the root of the souls of the pious among the nations of the world:

The words of the great Gaon, the great Chassid, and the great Tzaddik, etc., our teacher Rabbi Hillel of Paritch (in *Likutei Biurim* 47b) are as follows: "The souls of the idolaters, whose goodness and kindness are not for the sake of fulfilling the will of Hashem, nor for the sake of compassion for their fellow—for by nature they are cruel—but rather they act only for their own sake, to boast; for the root of their soul is from the three impure kelipos alone. This is unlike the pious among the nations of the world, who are taken from [kelipas] nogah, etc., as is known."

You are surely aware of the three daily portions—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, instituted for every person to study, which protect them. In any case, you should do so from now on, bli neder.

With blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 6745

B"H, 15 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

And finally, the main point, in response to the first matter in your letter: that when there is no sincere faith in the heart, etc., and because of this, one is in a state of depression, etc.

I heard a story from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that a Chassid once complained to the Tzemach Tzedek that he was experiencing doubts in his faith. The Tzemach Tzedek asked him, "What does it matter to you?" The Chassid replied with the greatest agitation, "How can you ask what it matters to me? After all, etc., etc." The Tzemach Tzedek then said to him, "That itself is the proof of your state—that you do believe, etc."

As with all stories of the Tzaddikim, there are several lessons to be learned from this one. Regarding your specific situation, the very concern over a lack of sincere faith is proof that it exists within the depths of the soul; it is simply that something is covering it, or, in the terminology of Chassidus, something is interposing between the inner essence and the external expression.

When one knows that this is the situation, this knowledge and recognition directs one’s avodah toward removing and nullifying that interposition. But it is obvious that the interposition and the barrier will not be removed—nor even diminished—by depression, which leads to a weakening of one's energy and activity; on the contrary.

May it be Hashem’s will that what I wrote in my previous letter be fulfilled in you: that you serve Hashem with joy and a glad heart. Especially since, even for someone in your position, this does not preclude contemplation of the negative aspects, as explained in Tanya; rather, it is a pity to waste time that could be utilized for matters of the "right side" by spending it dealing with the "left side," if that dealing is merely a state of slumber and produces no results.

With blessings for good tidings and for a *Kesivah V’chasimah Tovah*.

#### ***6745***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 17, p. 558.

## 6757

B"H, 17 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Yeruchem, may he live, and his wife, Mrs. Devorah, may she live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from 24 Menachem Av and 1 Elul.

It was a pleasure for me to read in your letter about the strengthening and development of the activities of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad and N'shei Chabad, and first and foremost, the strengthening of the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok institution. Surely you will not be satisfied with the above, but will continue to add to this, for we are commanded that "we increase in holiness," and the command of the Torah Hakdosha—Toras Chaim—is also a source of strength. May it be Hashem’s will that you influence the entire surrounding area in this regard, through speech, and even more so by being a living example of the matter.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Yisroel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings.

Regarding your question: a) The procedure for affixing a mezuzah abroad when living in a rented apartment.

I have not heard a specific instruction regarding this. My custom, and what I answer those who ask me about this, is: to affix the mezuzos immediately upon moving in. On the thirtieth day, take down one mezuzah in order to check it or replace it with a nicer one; in any case, this affixing on the thirtieth day is done with a *bracha*, and one should have in mind all the mezuzos.

c) The procedure for a birthday: Recently, the custom has been to give tzedakah before the morning and afternoon davening, to have a special shiur in Nigleh and Chassidus, and to complete the Chitas of the day specifically on this day (and *hisbodedus*, as explained in *Hayom Yom*).

***

**Procedure for a birthday:** See also above, Vol. 14, letter 4948, and in the references in the footnotes there.

**In Hayom Yom:** 11 Nissan.

## 6748

6748

By the Grace of G-d, 17 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you refer to my General Letter for Rosh Hashanah of the year 5718 and ask why many things that are part of the holy Torah were not mentioned in that General Letter as being important for Jews—citing many proofs from verses and statements of our Sages regarding many matters that are important for Jews, yet were not mentioned in the aforementioned General Letter—and, on the contrary, one could interpret the General Letter as implying that they are not important.

It surprises me that you wish to interpret my letter to mean that the things you write about are, Heaven forbid, not important. At the same time, it is **self-evident** that **all** 613 mitzvos, as well as the Rabbinic enactments and the minutiae of the Scribes, are important for all Jews and were given by the Holy One, Blessed be He, to Moses our Teacher at Sinai for all generations. Their importance is so great that, in the language of the Rambam (Hilchos Teshuvah, Chapter 3, Halacha 8), one who says that even a single verse or a single word of the Written Torah, or likewise of the Oral Torah, was said by Moses our Teacher of his own accord and not from the Holy One, Blessed be He, is called a denier of the Torah, and as he concludes there, he has no portion in the World to Come.

The aforementioned General Letter does not speak about importance **in general**; it only emphasized the matter without which, G-d forbid, there is no Judaism. What is more central than the matter of the sacrifices? The entire book of Vayikra, a large part of the order of Bamidbar, the order of Kodshim, and so on, deal exclusively with sacrifices. Yet, since the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash, we have (as the piyut in the Mussaf for Yom Kippur states) neither incense nor sacrifice, which no Jew in the entire world possesses. Furthermore, according to Torah law, one is currently forbidden to offer any sacrifice or incense, and yet, "You are standing today, all of you," refers also to "today" in the literal sense—**this very day.**

Regarding your question about the "war against compromises," at a time when—as you express it—the Written Torah and the Oral Torah are full of compromises, such as the *pruzbul*, the sale of *chametz*, etc.:

It is self-evident that "compromise" means, as in the English word "compromise," i.e., making a concession with the Torah. However, the *pruzbul* and similar things which are written **in** the Torah—the Written Torah and the Oral Torah—which, as stated above, were **all** given to Moses at Sinai, are **a part of the Torah** just as the Ten Commandments are, etc.

Judging by your quoting of verses and statements of our Sages, I hope that you have a fixed time for Torah study every day, according to the law and custom of Israel, morning and evening, and that from time to time you add to this, which is a sign of vitality—that it is growing and increasing. May the Holy One, Blessed be He, help you to increase in this many times over.

With blessings for good tidings and for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good year.
