## 680

680

B”H, 18 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings! After the longest of intervals, your letter of 8 Elul was received. It is written for you with good tidings, that your health and livelihood are in order. May it be the will [of Hashem] that from now on there will be even more increase in this, for we are commanded to "ascend in holiness," and the matters of a Yid are in his own hands to be made holy by living his life according to the instruction of our holy Torah, the Torah of life. Regarding your questions:

1) Regarding a partnership in your business.

Since Hashem has granted you success, why should you involve someone else in the matter? If the business requires expansion, you should endeavor to expand it through your own efforts. May it be the will that there be expansion in a good and successful hour, and that you use your profits for healthy and joyous matters, and for matters of Torah and mitzvos.

2) Regarding your question about the differences of opinion between you and your wife, tichyeh.

You should endeavor to have your friends explain to her that, on the contrary, since there is some matter that is not perfect in the conduct of your son, sheyichyeh, this is an additional reason to request from the Ribono shel Olam that He bless you with more children, and especially since we see tangibly that through an increase in sons and daughters, there is also an improvement in the previous children.

3) Regarding what you wrote about merchants who are competing with you, etc.

One of the pieces of advice for this is to divert your attention from them. According to the principle, "As water reflects a face to a face, so is the heart of man to man," ultimately, diverting your attention from him and his affairs will have an effect.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding your brother, sheyichyeh, in accordance with what was discussed—that you should endeavor to influence him in matters of Torah and mitzvos. There is nothing that can stand before the will, and it is a certainty that outreach does not return empty.

As we approach the new year, which is coming upon us and upon all Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessing.

The known advice for this is to study from the book and to daven from the Siddur. Even when you are studying by heart or contemplating a subject, the book should be open in front of you at the place where you are studying.

## 6,483

B"H, 19 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It is a great wonder that you do not mention anything regarding your activities in disseminating the wellsprings [of Chassidus] in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established. My hope is that for someone like you, there is no need for a lengthy explanation of what is written, "The steps of man are established by Hashem, and He delights in his way" (*Tehillim* 37:23). One of the interpretations of this is that the "way" refers to what is written, "To keep the way of Hashem, to do charity and justice" (*Bereishis* 18:19). And "He delights" refers specifically to *taanug*—the inner dimension of the will. From this, it is understood that the matter depends on the inner dimensions of things: the hidden aspects of the *neshamah* and the hidden aspects of the *Torah*.

This is especially true in these days, [as it is written], "One thing I have asked... 'Seek My face'; Your face, Hashem, I will seek" (*Tehillim* 27:4). May it be the will [of Hashem] that, at the very least, you now engage in this with the necessary vigor, and in a manner that fulfills what has not yet been done until now. After all, the *avira* of Eretz Yisrael and the *hisorerus* of these days are of great assistance.

With blessings for good tidings and to be inscribed and sealed for good.

P.S.
Perhaps, in order to bring the matter of dissemination into a more active mode, it would be worthwhile for you to connect with the *Tzeirei Agudas Chabad* and suggest to them that you are prepared to visit the appropriate locations, etc.

## 6,484

B”H, 19 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 11 Elul, the month of mercy, in which you write regarding the desire to transfer the casket of your father, of blessed memory, to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. The burial was performed with this condition, and he is even placed in a casket specifically designed for transport. However, there are several family members who claim that this is highly improper, as it will not be possible for the family to visit his grave on the yahrtzeit, and the like.

Generally, such questions belong to a Rav, a *moreh hora’ah*, in the place where he can hear the arguments from both sides, and therefore you should act accordingly. However, it is understood that you must emphasize that the condition was made at the time of the burial, as mentioned. Furthermore, what is even more significant is that he is placed in a casket specifically designed for transport—which constitutes a change in the burial—which, in all likelihood, delays the decomposition, etc. If you do not transfer him, the question arises regarding the delay of decomposition and the change in the burial, etc.

I must also say that the argument raised by the family members is applicable in the vast majority of cases when a niftar is transferred to Eretz Yisrael, as all the family members remain in their previous place of residence, and yet, they proceed as mentioned.

You conclude your letter by stating that you work in an accounting office, and regarding teaching, you have a desire to be a teacher for the children of Yisrael. It is understood that a desire in such matters is not sufficient at all, because this is a matter that involves another person. When the influence is lacking in the recipient, then certainly, for the recipient, it makes no difference what the intention of the *mashpia* was—and this is understood in the positive sense regarding influence. This is similar to the teaching of our Sages (Sifrei, Ki Teitzei 24:19): "He who lost a sela and a poor person found it—this is a matter of tzedakah" (even though in the vast majority of cases, the one who lost the sela is distressed by it), and the moral lesson is understood.

As for your point that you still lack much knowledge, etc.—every person lacks knowledge. Even one who has reached the ultimate level of knowledge, it is known from the statement of the philosophers (Ikkarim 2:30 and elsewhere): "The ultimate knowledge is that we do not know." We see tangibly that this is not only regarding the knowledge of the Creator and His matters, but even in secular sciences, and especially in our times, the area of the unknown is far greater than the additions in the area of the known.

In any case, even while you are in your current position, it is appropriate to organize a group with whom you will study holy subjects. Naturally, this should be done in a way that the study leads to action, as it is written: "Fear G-d and keep His mitzvos, for **this** is the whole man."

With blessings for good tidings and for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for you and for the entire family, may they live and be well.

## 6,485

B"H, 20 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn

To the administration of the institution for education in purity, "Oholei Torah," in Brooklyn, N.Y., and at their head, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Michael, may he live.

These days of the month of Elul, the month of mercy, are auspicious for all the aforementioned, especially the bright day of 18 Elul, which precedes and follows it—the birthday of the two luminaries, the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe, who sacrificed themselves for the education of the children of Bnei Yisrael, as is well known.

The magnitude of the reward for all who engage in this is understood from the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of the Baal Shem Tov: that the love of the Ribono shel Olam for each and every one of the children of Yisrael is even greater than the love of elderly parents for their only son born to them in their old age. Consequently, the *nachas ruach* caused to the Ribono shel Olam through their proper education, according to His will, is understood.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and I sign with a blessing for success and a *kesivah vachasimah tovah* for each and every one and their families, may they live, with revealed good.

M. Schneerson

Enclosed is my personal check, as my participation in the purchase of the building in a good and auspicious hour.

## 6,788

B"H, 20 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Avraham Moshe, may he live.

Peace and blessing! In response to your letter of 12 Elul.

It seems to me that you have already been answered previously regarding the question posed in this letter. It concerns the well-known dispute between the Rambam and the Ramban regarding the World to Come—in which there is no eating, etc.—specifically whether this refers to the soul alone, or whether the soul will then exist within a body. You conclude your letter by asking if it is possible to interpret the words of the Alter Rebbe on this subject in Likutei Torah as a parable.

It is understood that this cannot be interpreted in such a way, for it is explicitly written that there is a dispute on this matter between the Rambam and the Ramban, and the teachings of Chassidus concur with the opinion of the Ramban (see Likutei Torah, Tzav 15c; Derech Mitzvosecha, Mitzvas Tzitzis, and elsewhere).

As for your question regarding what the reality will be then, there are several points to consider. Among them is the fact that since the body participated in the performance of the mitzvos, it is simple to understand that the receiving of the reward pertains to it as well, and this is well-understood.

You are surely increasing your involvement in holy matters in general, in accordance with the directive to "ascend in holiness," and specifically through setting fixed times for the study of the teachings of Chassidus. May Hashem grant you success.

**R' Avraham Moshe:** Greenberg, Bnei Brak. Additional letters to him appear above in 6,168 and in the references noted there.

**You have already been answered:** See the letters above, 6,300 and 6,357.

## 6,489

B"H, 22 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of Yeshivas Akko,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Shalom u’vracha! Your letter, written on behalf of the students with the request to mention them for good and for blessing, was received in due time.

It is surely known to you and engraved in your memory the saying of our Sages, of blessed memory: "If you have labored and not found, do not believe." This means that the matter depends solely on your own will; if you truly desire it, you will succeed in achieving great things in the study of Torah—Torah that is life. The main thing is that the study should be in a manner appropriate to the instruction of the Torah, namely, study that leads to action: the fulfillment of mitzvos with hiddur, and with an increase in this from time to time, for we have also been commanded: "We ascend in matters of holiness."

It is my hope that you have begun the new term of study in this direction, and it will be a pleasure for me to hear good news regarding your success in your studies and in your conduct.

As we approach the new year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I send my blessing to each and every one of you: a blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

640

By the Grace of G-d
22 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in holy work, who is involved in the needs of the community, a man of energy and many accomplishments, R’ Alexander Zissel, may he live.

Peace and Blessing! I acknowledge receipt of your letter, and I ask your forgiveness for the delay in responding due to the many pressures.

I have expressed my clear opinion several times: if, in all times and eras, education in the purity of holiness is one of the vital matters for our people, the Children of Israel, then it is all the more so in our current era and in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established. From this, it is understood—and it is also simple—that fortunate is the lot of every man and woman who occupies themselves with this. Especially after several years, this is absolute proof that this is the mitzvah in which one must be most careful, as explained in several places in Chassidus, including the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Epistle 7, and in *Sefer HaSichos* Summer 5700, p. 22. This is especially true when one has seen good fruit from one’s labor, which is a foretaste of the highest reward: "You shall see your world in your lifetime."

As an immediate result of the above, it is understood that any thought casting doubt on the benefit of this work, or questioning whether it is desirable to continue in it, does not originate from the side of holiness, etc. See also *Hayom Yom*, 23 Sivan.

It is understood that in all the above, there is no intention whatsoever to conceal or minimize the negative matters about which you write. But it is clear that what our Torah, the Torah of life, has informed us—that this world and all it contains is called the world of *kelipos* and *sitra achra*, that its deeds are difficult and evil, and that the wicked prevail within it (Tanya, end of Chapter 6)—is not intended to cause despair or to weaken one’s energy. It is not even intended to justify a deficiency in one’s actions, in the event that one has not done as one ought to do. The negation of all this is explained in several places, including in Tanya, Chapter 30, in the *dih* "And behold, in truth, even one who, etc.," and see also there, Chapter 24.

Rather, one of the purposes of this information is that a person’s heart should not fail him when he encounters obstacles and concealments, and sometimes even a tremendous battle—and not only from those whose role it is to oppose, but also from those who, on the face of it, should have been the most helpful. For ultimately, the purpose of the creation of man is to serve his Creator, and he must do what is incumbent upon him, and Hashem will do what is good in His eyes. Furthermore, we have been promised that, in the end, we are victorious in this battle, for "none shall be cast away from Him," and "if you have labored and not found, do not believe."

Similarly, I do not mean by the above to say that the "good part" is what appears to the eyes—that one has not ended up in the framework one aspired to, as you explain in section 3 of your letter. But the full answer to this can be found in the wondrous story printed in the introduction of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, to the book *Pokeiach Ivrim*, regarding R’ Yosef the *mashpia*. In the words of the Mitteler Rebbe, copied there on page 34: "The father, for the sake of a private benefit, turned a *lamdan* into a wagon driver." Consider this: the subject there is a private benefit, and it concerns one of the Chassidim of the Alter Rebbe—one of the "men of stature" among them—who ended up at the other extreme, becoming a wagon driver in the literal sense. See the story there at length, which lasted for many years. This is not at all comparable to your situation, where you are educating the sons and daughters of Israel—of whom the Creator of the world says that "all before Him is considered as nothing," for each one is His only child, and they have been entrusted to be educated by you, with affection and with the prior granting of the ability and strength to attend to their education. Moreover, the subject here is youth, which means that every improvement in their condition grows many times over in the course of time, as is known from the example of the smallest improvement in a seed, which touches upon more and more, until it grows into a tree that bears fruit.

Regarding all those problems about which you write—how to rectify them—it is understood that one cannot set hard and fast rules. The absolute point in this is: in what manner will there be the maximum benefit? But in general, one sees tangibly in matters such as these that when one avoids a battle in an open manner, but infiltrates all the matters as if "by the way," etc., then ultimately the opposing side becomes weary and diverts its attention to other matters. It is understood that when one sees a need for an open battle, one should not be intimidated by that either, for one is walking on the mission of the Master of the World. But as mentioned, this is only after other methods have been exhausted.

According to the saying, "The trouble of many is half a consolation" (even though, woe and alas for such a consolation), I receive letters with similar content to yours from many activists, both in the field of education and in the field of public activism in general. Anyone who reads and studies *mussar* books from past generations, even from many generations ago, will find in most of them complaints about situations similar to those you describe in your letter. This is despite the known saying, "If the earlier ones were like angels, etc.," and the explicit verse in Scripture: "Do not say, 'How was it that the former days were better than these?' for it is not out of wisdom that you ask about this" (Koheles 7:10).

It is understood that with all the above, there are those who raise a question—and on the face of it, it is a tremendous question—as to why Hashem has done so, etc. But in general, what benefit is there in questions, at a time when the path of man is as it is said: "You shall be wholehearted with Hashem your G-d"? The aforementioned question was already addressed by the *Moreh Nevuchim*, the Rambam, in his introduction to the commentary on the Mishnah, in his explanation of the statement of our Sages, "The entire world was not created but to be subservient to this one," near the end.

The conclusion from the above is: you should increase your activities, similar to those you have done until now. Your heart should be confident that this is the mitzvah in which one must be "most careful" (*zehir*—from the word *leichten*, to illuminate). You should increase them in quantity and quality as much as possible, and even beyond that, for a person’s possibilities change in accordance with his will. As our Torah decrees: "A person who sanctifies himself a little below, they sanctify him much from above." Do this with joy and a good heart, and we have been promised that "joy breaks through barriers"—even the barriers and limitations of holiness, and all the more so the barriers and limitations of the "other side."

I await good news regarding all the above.

With the blessing of *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year in body and soul.

## 6. Vayeitzei

B"H, 22 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the beginning of the month of Elul—the month of mercy—in which you write the doctors' opinion regarding yourself and your wife, may she live and be well, stating that everything is in order, yet for the time being you have not been blessed with children, and therefore, as you write, the great Professor Zondek advised you to take [a certain medical course of action], etc.

Since we are currently in the days of abundant mercy—and as explained in Likutei Torah by our Alter Rebbe, that even in the month of Elul there is an illumination of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy, and the King, the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all—how much more so is this true in the month of Tishrei, which is called the "seventh month," saturated with all goodness. Therefore, you and your wife, may she live and be well, should strengthen your trust in Hashem and pray from the depths of your hearts throughout these days and weeks for the fulfillment of your heart's desires for the good. Only if, G-d forbid, these weeks pass [without result], then you may reconsider the aforementioned advice. However, our Rebbes have already said: "Think good and it will be good."

It is understood that any increase in matters of Torah and mitzvos brings an increase in the blessings of Hashem in what a person and his household require. No matter how good the situation may be in this regard, there is always room to add more. Specifically regarding your situation, you should establish a daily study session in the inner dimension of Torah, which is called the "Tree of Life," where there are no concealments or hiddenness, as explained in Iggeres HaKodesh by our Alter Rebbe, Epistle 26. Furthermore, every day before the morning davening and before the Mincha davening—on weekdays, of course—you should set aside some coins for tzedakah, and your wife, may she live and be well, should do the same until the end of the upcoming month of Tishrei (all of this, of course, must be done *bli neder*), which is the month saturated with all goodness.

May it be the will of Hashem that the "good inscription and sealing" for the coming year be first and foremost drawn down into reality with the fulfillment of your heart's desires for the good.

With blessings for good tidings and a good inscription and sealing.

P.S.
I will reiterate that the matter of setting aside tzedakah and establishing times for the study of Chassidus must be done *bli neder*.

## 692

692

B"H, 22 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the participants of the farbrengen on the auspicious day of 18 Elul, the birthday of the two luminaries, the Baal Shem Tov and our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, may their merits protect us, may they rest in peace, may their merit shield us.
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter and your report from the time of the farbrengen.

If a farbrengen of the type mentioned—at any time and in any season—has a great and immense effect, as is known from the saying of the Alter Rebbe, "What a Chassidishe farbrengen can accomplish, even the angel Michael cannot accomplish," then how much more so when the essence of the time itself contributes and adds to this.

And a person is obligated to speak in the language of his Rebbe: "18 Elul is the day that brought and brings life into Elul; 18 Elul gives vitality to the avodah of 'I am to my Beloved and my Beloved is to me.'"

For Elul encompasses all three lines and the concept of teshuvah that transcends them, as is explained in many places, including the introduction to the Kuntres Elul 5718. This is the point of vitality and the inwardness of all these avodos during the month of Elul.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that the effects of the aforementioned day be continued in all matters of thought, speech, and action—the garments of the neshamah—and with greater intensity and strength within the neshamah itself, and even reaching the inwardness of the neshamah.

For this is our inner request from the beginning of the month of Elul: "Seek My **face**; Your **face**, Hashem, I seek."

The magnitude of this matter is explained by the level one reaches through the aforementioned avodah, as is written in Likutei Torah at the end of the maamar beginning with the words "Shuvah Yisrael," that through it one reaches that level regarding which it is said, "And My face shall not be seen."

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for each and every one, together with their families, may they live and be well.

P.S.

The conclusion above is not a duplication of the blessing for the year in a specific sense, for each contains what the other does not. This is understood from Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah, beginning of Chapter 12, regarding the matter of that which transcends everything through the combination of many letters to form a word (for every single Jew has a letter in the Torah). And regarding the matters of the Aseres Yemei Teshuvah, there is a specific importance in the detailing and clarification of every single thing (see Shulchan Aruch of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Hilchos Rosh Hashanah, Siman 582, Paragraph 7).

6494

B"H, 23 Elul, 5718

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year to all who are involved in this and to their families, and to you and your family in particular, that you may succeed in communal and personal matters.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6,195

B"H, 25 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs,
R' Dovid, Shochet u'Bodek,

Shalom u'Bracha! After a very long interval, your letter of 23 Elul was received, along with its enclosure, in which you ask my opinion as to whether it is permissible to daven in a shul that uses a microphone on Shabbos and Yom Tov.

It is a great wonder that there is any doubt regarding such an appalling matter. The use of a microphone on Shabbos and Yom Tov is a desecration of the days of Shabbos and Yom Tov in public. Furthermore, it is a matter of "even forcing the queen while I am in the house" (Esther 7:8)—in a house of prayer to the Giver of the Torah and His mitzvos, where the mitzvah of Shabbos is equivalent to all the mitzvos, as our Sages say in Yerushalmi Nedarim (end of chapter 3).

Since the desecration of Shabbos is committed in the name of all the members of this shul—for the Gabbaim who decide these matters are their representatives—there is room for doubt regarding all matters of davening and Krias HaTorah that take place there, and not only regarding the parts transmitted via the microphone, but even those that precede and follow it.

Now, all of the above is according to the letter of the law of Hilchos Shabbos, even if there were no issue of Chillul Hashem involved. But when one also considers this point, the matter is many times more severe. In my opinion, it is absolutely simple that even on Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, one should daven in private, but G-d forbid in the aforementioned shul.

Approaching the new year, which is coming upon us and all of Yisroel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours, a blessing of *Kesivah v'Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessing.

## 6,298

6,298

B”H, 25 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter of 16 Elul, in which you raise the question of accepting restitution and compensation payments from Germany, which is currently under your consideration. You mention that you are inclined not to accept them, and you detail your reasons for this.

It is understood that the situation now is entirely different from when the discussion took place some time ago regarding whether or not to agree to accept these reparations. Since the matter has already been ongoing for several years and with the greatest publicity, it is clear that the actions of an individual regarding the aforementioned (I refer to whether or not one claims what is due to them) will not change the undesirable impression you write about (the raising of their status, the fostering of a positive attitude toward them, etc.).

Furthermore, regarding what you wrote—that when a thief returns stolen property, his punishment is mitigated, whereas if you do not accept it, this is not the case—it is well known in many places in our Torah that one must extract stolen property from the hand of a thief, even a non-Jew. Especially since if the stolen property remains in his possession, it strengthens his position and his affairs. In the case at hand, where the thief remains a thief even now, strengthening his power does not strengthen the side of good in the world.

It is also understood that this matter has nothing to do with the issue of accepting charity from non-Jews, for these reparations are paid equally to both the poor and the wealthy, and there is no element of charity involved.

In my opinion, you should do what is incumbent upon you and claim the largest amount due to you. However, following your letter, you should set aside a *chumash* (one-fifth) of this for *tzedakah*. It is understood and simple that this *tzedakah* confers no merit upon those who paid the reparations, for they have merely returned the stolen property to its rightful owners, and the owner does as they please with it.

You are surely aware of the good custom of the daughters of Israel to set aside money for *tzedakah* before lighting candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov, and in any case, you should conduct yourself in this manner from now on.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V’chasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 6,499

6,499

B”H, 25 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings! The month of Elul, and specifically the days of Selichos and the Aseres Yemei Teshuvah, is the time for making a *cheshbon tzedek*—not a superficial accounting—of the year that is passing, and from that, to draw the proper resolutions for how to conduct oneself, one’s home, and all its affairs in the coming year.

Together with this, these are *yemei segulah*, days that call out and demand, in accordance with the high point of the *mizmor* of Tehillim that we recite twice daily during this time:

**"Seek My face; Your face, Hashem, I will seek."**

Seek the content, the inner dimension, and the *pnimiyus* within yourself; seek the *pnimiyus* of your surroundings, the *pnimiyus* of the *neshamah* of the world; find and reveal the *Elokus* that enlivens and fills the world.

Both matters—the *cheshbon tzedek* and the *bakshu panai*—are interconnected and dependent upon one another.

When making an accounting of the *avar* (the past), one often—very often—makes a mistake by taking into account only the superficial, the external aspects that exist within oneself and that one sees in one’s surroundings.

The same is true when planning the *seder hachayim* for the coming year.

And this is the call and the demand of the day:

Do not underestimate your own *kochot* and capabilities.

No matter how much you may have "in cash"—open opportunities to conduct yourself in daily life according to the instructions of *Toraseinu Toras Chaim* (the Torah of life)—and no matter how great the measure and strength of character may be to not be *nispaleil* by an unfriendly environment and to walk in the path of *Torah u’mitzvos*, you have much more and much greater potential in "reserve"—capabilities that you can create through the appropriate effort, inner, very great *kochot* of independence and strength to implement in life that which is good and true.

But for this, it is required: **"Bakshu"**—seek and bring out your *kochot* and capabilities, and then it will be: **"U’metzaseta"**—"For you will find," if you seek Him—you will find, provided that you seek and demand.

***

The above applies especially, and to an even greater degree, to *mashpi'im*, spiritual leaders, *rabbanim*, and so on, down to the father and the one who sets the tone in the spiritual life of the home and family.

At every step, one sees that they stand in doubt and fear: perhaps the words are too strict, perhaps one is demanding too much, perhaps one will drive others away through this, and so on.

To them is the call of these days and the demand:

**"Bakshu panai"**—look closely, seek, and bring out the *pnimiyus* of those you influence. Value them according to their inner wealth, according to the capacity of their *neshamah*, which is a *chelek Eloka mima'al mamash*.

For through an appropriate approach and tireless work with them, one can bring out the hidden wealth and *kochot* in everyone, so that they begin to take effect even in daily life.

Have trust in Yidden, and give them that which they, Yidden, truly expect to receive: a *Torah temimah*, a complete Torah with all its *mitzvos*, and with the fundamental idea: **"HaTorah hi nitzchiyis"**—the Torah is eternal, for all times and for everywhere.

***

And precisely through this approach does one arrive at a *cheshbon tzedek*—in evaluating oneself and in evaluating those whom one wishes to lead on the proper path.

A *cheshbon tzedek* of the past and a *cheshbon tzedek* of how to arrange the *asid* (the future), so that it should be a "full" year—full of the proper content in everything that depends on the person.

And this also brings about that it should be a year-full, filled with the *Ribono shel Olam’s* blessings in everything, both in *gashmiyus* and in *ruchniyus*.

With blessings for *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year,

Menachem Schneerson

## 650

650

B"H, 26 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn.

Blessings and peace! In response to your letter of July 9, in which you write that you are frequently asked about matters of Yiddishkeit and the reasons why you wish to conduct yourself according to the instructions of the Torah and observe its mitzvos, and you ask how to respond to this and how to conduct yourself.

In general, it is not worthwhile to enter into such debates. When they ask you, it is best to reply that for such questions, they should turn to the Rav or the halachic authority in their area, or to the Rosh Yeshiva, for they are occupied with Torah daily, and therein are found the answers and explanations to all questions. You need only explain to them that it is a simple matter that every Jewish man and woman must observe the Torah and the mitzvos, which were given by the Creator of the world, whose leader is Hashem Yisbarach. And if this is connected with difficulties and requires effort, it is regarding this that it is said: "For Hashem your G-d is testing you to know whether you love Hashem." This is merely a temporary trial, and when one stands firm in the trial, one receives the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach. You must continue in your conduct as is fitting for a good daughter of Israel, for every one of them is called by the name of daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah. When you truly desire it, you will be able to conduct yourself in this way, and you will also succeed.

It would be appropriate for you to visit the Bais Rivkah office at the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch institutions in Casablanca, and see the teachers of Bais Rivkah there and speak with them; they will be able to explain the questions you write about, as well as any others that may arise in the future.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
In my secretariat, we do not write in French, which is why the response is in Lashon HaKodesh. However, you may continue to write in French in the future, as I am able to read that language.

## 6,501

B"H, 26 Elul, 5718
Brooklyn

To the Kfar Chabad Committee,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Shalom u’vracha! It is surprising that for a long time now there has been no news from you. May it be the will of Hashem that this is a good sign—and what better sign could there be—as there is a basis in Torah that "no news" implies that everything is in order and at peace.

The reason for my writing now is that the seventh year, the year of Shemittah, is approaching. Surely you have taken the appropriate measures regarding the livelihood of those who, until now, have been occupied with working the land—especially the Sephardim and the Moroccans, who are not yet established at all, and it is obvious that they do not have multiple sources of income.

This letter is being sent via express mail due to the urgency of the matter, and therefore, a detailed response to this letter would be appreciated.

With the blessing of *Kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

6112

B”H, Days of Selichos, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, the scholar, the man of action, etc.,
Rabbi Shlomo, may he live.

Peace and blessing! As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby extend my blessing to you and to all who are yours: a blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With respect and blessing.

I acknowledge receipt of your two seforim, *Nezer HaKodesh* (Vol. 1) and *Shaarei Taharah* on Maseches Mikvaos. I trust that you will also honor me with your other publications. Many thanks for the past and for what is yet to come.

Out of affection for the subject matter, I have gone through the pages of the sefer—albeit cursorily, despite the pressure of time—and I have transcribed here, in haste, some thoughts that occurred to me in certain places. As per the words of our Sages (Bava Metzia 84a), “One should raise difficulties... and thereby the study becomes clarified... do I not know...?” And the conclusion is the main thing.

**In the sefer *Nezer HaKodesh*, at the beginning:** Regarding Rambam, *Hilchos Pesulei HaMukdashin* 1:15, you explain that the Rambam holds that the *yotzei* (that which is taken out of the Temple courtyard) is tamei and imparts tumah, but that it does not impart tumah to hands.

With all due respect, it is difficult to attribute to the Rambam a novelty that is not absolutely necessary, especially since it is not hinted at in the Rambam’s own words (for if he had hinted at it, the hint would certainly not have escaped the *Kesef Mishneh*, *Lechem Mishneh*, *Mishneh LaMelech*, etc., here in *Hilchos Pesulei HaMukdashin*). Furthermore, the Rambam should have stated this **explicitly**. One cannot say that the reason for the omission is that it is not his custom to record anything but an explicit law, for according to your own explanation, the law is explicit in the Yerushalmi.

Moreover, according to your interpretation, a difficulty arises from *Hilchos Avos HaTumah* 8:3: “The *pigul*... is like a *rishon*... **therefore** they impart tumah to hands...” For the *yotzei* is also “like a *rishon*,” yet it is not subject to the tumah of hands.

It seems that you were compelled to interpret as you did for two reasons: 1) To resolve the difficulty of the *Mishneh LaMelech* in *Hilchos Avos HaTumah* (loc. cit.), as to why the Rambam specifically wrote there the law that the meat of the Pesach sacrifice that is *yotzei* is tahor. But the *Mishneh LaMelech* already resolved this by stating that the Rambam’s intention is to distinguish between a doubt and a certainty. Therefore, even for you, this intention is necessary in the Rambam, for otherwise, the length of his language there—“The *rishon*... is a doubt... therefore it does not impart tumah, for a doubt regarding the tumah of hands is tahor”—is entirely incomprehensible. 2) To resolve how it is possible that the Raavad here overlooked the fact that the Rambam ruled (in *Avos HaTumah*, loc. cit.) that the inquiry in *Keitzad Tzolin* is resolved leniently (and also why he did not challenge him there).

However, even according to your reasoning, it is not resolved, for the Raavad has no need to impose a novelty upon the Rambam and then challenge him. Remove the novelty and remove the difficulty; there is no necessity to say that the Rambam holds that due to the stringency of *kodshim*, all inquiries must be resolved stringently (and as for the fact that the Raavad did not challenge him in *Hilchos Avos HaTumah*, he also did not challenge him in *Hilchos Korban Pesach*).

Furthermore, it seems to me: First, consider the difficulty regarding the Raavad—why did he need to elaborate to prove that the halacha follows Ravina? The Rambam’s view is that anything prepared to be cut is considered as if it were already cut; thus, the *yotzei* imparts tumah even if he does not hold like Ravina (as you yourself noted regarding the *Lechem Mishneh*).

In my opinion, the Raavad, in his *Hasagos* on the Yad, is also expressing his own view on the law. If the Rambam follows his own system elsewhere in the rulings that the Raavad challenges, this does not change the Raavad’s ruling, obviously. On the contrary, his challenge in this place extends to and applies to this system of the Rambam in all its details. By accepting this principle regarding the Raavad’s intent, many difficulties raised against him and notes made in the *Kesef Mishneh* are nullified. This also applies to the notes of the *Lechem Mishneh* here, and to the second point mentioned above. Thus, it is understood why the Raavad elaborated to prove that the halacha follows Ravina—to clarify that the law is that it imparts tumah, even if one were to say that “anything prepared to be cut is not considered as if it were already cut.”

**In the aforementioned sefer, on the Rambam there, 1:23:** “Therefore, **in such a case**...” You conclude with a note of difficulty: What does “in such a case” accomplish here?

It seems to me, first, what is added and taught by the “Therefore...” phrase? He should have said: “And the carrying of the blood is not a valid carrying, and the sacrifice is disqualified.”

It can be explained that from the Rambam’s silence—that he does not say it is not a carrying and does not distinguish—it is implied that it applies in all cases, even when it is his custom to do so (i.e., when he slaughters at the side of the Altar, as written in *Lechem Mishneh* and *Mishneh LaMelech*). The Rambam adds that since it is his custom to do so because of the (proximity of) the place, this does not exempt him from carrying it on foot. Therefore (even when it is his custom to do so because of the person, i.e.,) in such a case where it is his custom to shorten his path while carrying the blood, and he receives the limbs and stands in his place and throws them, even then, if he received the blood and stood in his place and threw it, the sacrifice is disqualified.

- See *Yoma* 35b, “between the Hall and the Altar,” and the Gemara there. *Tamid*, Chapter 5, Mishna 3. Note that throwing from a distance depends on human strength (*Zevachim* 64a), and “such a one is greater than his brother in strength” (*Yoma* 18a).

In the *Mishneh LaMelech*, it is transcribed: “Therefore, a Kohen who received...” Apparently, it is imprecise.

**In the sefer *Shaarei Taharah*—*Tosefes Taharah*, at the beginning:** Regarding the commentary of the Rosh here on *mei gabaim* and his commentary on the *sugya* in *Pesachim*.

See the Rosh on *Taharos*, end of Chapter 8, where he explains that in *Pesachim* it refers to *sha’uvim* (drawn water)—the opposite of his commentary in *Hilchos Mikvaos*. This has already been noted in the sefer *Gulos Aliyos* (on Maseches Mikvaos), which left it as a difficulty. See there, where he elaborates on all the points you discussed.

**There, at the end:** “In the future, I will purify you with a permanent purification so that you will not become tamei, as it is written: ‘I will sprinkle upon you pure water and you shall be purified.’” In *Shaarei Taharah* there, it refers to the time when the spirit of tumah will pass from the earth.

However, “I will sprinkle upon you” is the purification of the person (the individual, the many, or even the entirety of the Jewish people), yet the existence of evil in the world remains (and also in practice, among the nations of the world, in animals, and even in the *Erev Rav*), and consequently, the possibility of evil acts remains (even among all the Jewish people).

This is unlike “I will remove the spirit of tumah from the earth,” which is the purification of the world. In the language of our Sages, this refers to the Holy One, Blessed be He, slaughtering the *yetzer hara* (*Sukkah* 52a).

There is nothing new under the sun, and there have already been instances of these two matters: “He has no *yetzer hara* because he killed it,” or more than that, “He made the *yetzer hara* good” (Yerushalmi, end of *Berachos*); and similar to this is one who has lived most of his years and has not sinned (*Yoma* 35b). This is unlike the surrender of the *yetzer hara* of idolatry to the Men of the Great Assembly (*Yoma* 69b; see there in *Chiddushei Aggados*).

This has a practical difference regarding reward and punishment, for they still exist in the manner and period of the first [category], even though the Holy One, Blessed be He, helps and purifies him, just as the Holy One, Blessed be He, always helps him—for without this, he could not overcome it.

This is unlike the manner and period of the second [category], which are years in which there is neither merit nor obligation (*Shabbos* 151b).

See also *Zohar* Vol. III, 125a (and this resolves the difficulty of the *Kesef Mishneh* and *Lechem Mishneh* in Rambam, *Hilchos Teshuvah* 8:3; the *Hasagos* of the Raavad and the commentary of the Radbaz on Rambam, *Hilchos Melachim* 12:1; *Avodas HaKodesh* by R. Meir ibn Gabbai, Part II, Ch. 38; *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, end of Epistle 26, etc.). I will not elaborate further.

***6112***

**Rabbi Shlomo:** Goren.

## 6,503

[Late Elul, 5718?]

It is surprising that for a very long time there has been no news from you, but my hope is strong that, in any case, you are continuing your study of our holy Torah within the walls of the yeshivah. The magnitude of this matter is, in and of itself, well-known and explained in many places in the words of our Sages, of blessed memory. Furthermore, these years are years of preparation for one’s entire life; the direction and completeness of one’s life depend upon the integrity, the foundation, and the strength of this preparation. Therefore, it is always worthwhile to add more and more to the intensity of this preparation, since the benefit is multiplied many times over throughout the decades of life that follow. This is especially true given your age, where this is not yet a matter of "adding" to the time required, but rather the time of preparation itself. From the above, it is understood that every week and month spent engaging in Torah with the necessary consistency and diligence—a matter which is only possible through attachment to peers within the walls of a yeshivah—is not only not a useless endeavor, Heaven forbid, but on the contrary, it is the maximum benefit one can derive from this period of time. As is also known by the parable regarding this: a small addition to a planted seed is multiplied many times over in the tree that grows afterward.

## 6,404

[Summer 5718?] 

Regarding the note concerning Sefiras HaOmer—that it should not become "like two Torahs," etc.—I did not merit to understand this. For the Torah stated **explicitly** that each person must count **for themselves** (similar to "and she shall count **for herself**," and not like the counting of the *Shmu'in*), and to establish Shavuos on the fiftieth day. This is the **only** way to establish Shavuos (the count of the **individual**). And if you raise the difficulty: "Is it not so that one person will celebrate Shavuos on the 49th day of his count (for he certainly will not be exempt from Sefiras HaOmer), another on the 51st day of his count, and a third on the 50th day of his count!"—and many other difficulties regarding the counting (lacking *temimus*, exceeding *temimus*, etc.).

The *Lechem Mishneh* (Hilchos Lulav, Chapter 7) which you cited —that is its own refutation. See there.

In my humble opinion, regarding what you call my conclusion a "great innovation"—the innovation is the simplicity of the matter, and "what is it coming to teach us?"

My letter of response regarding Tefillin —surely it was received in due time.

#### ***6,404***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 23, p. 327.

**The note regarding Sefiras HaOmer:** Regarding what was explained above in letters 6,390 and 6,415: that one who crosses the International Date Line in the middle of the days of the Sefirah must continue his own count, and likewise celebrate the festival of Shavuos according to his own count.
